Source: ADR-0017 (T16 retention sweep library + MemoryRetentionStore), 2026-05-23. Closes the F-51/F-52 surfaces with concrete library-level test obligations and adds five new surfaces specific to the sweep mechanism (lease, row-cap, schedule-hash, TestStore split, no-PII-in-errors).

**Scope split:** F-55..F-69 below are scored as a family. Library-scope assertions land in T16 (CI tests against `MemoryRetentionStore`). SQL-scope assertions land in T16.1 (pgTAP, `SupabaseRetentionStore`, pg_cron, Edge Function trigger). Each row tags `[T16]` or `[T16.1 deferred]` for the test-writer.

#### Trust boundaries this introduces

- **B6 — Retention service-role boundary (added here; activates at T16.1; library shape preserved in T16).** A non-login `retention_service_role` in T16.1 holds `GRANT EXECUTE` on the `SECURITY DEFINER` sweep functions and is the only role authorised to issue cross-table DELETEs aligned to the schedule. It has NO `GRANT` on base tables — the only attack surface is the function set, and the function bodies hard-code the schedule lookup. The library half (T16) mirrors this at the type level: `RetentionStore` forbids caller-supplied WHERE; the predicate is constructed from the schedule discriminator only. Treat B6 as "type-level in T16, role-level in T16.1." Reference: ADR-0017 §1, §4, §6; sibling task spec items #1, #3, #9.
- **Diagram note (consolidated diagram, §1 of this file).** B6 sits inside the Supabase-cloud box, adjacent to "Postgres + RLS-as-authz" and "Edge Functions". Edge: `pg_cron` (T16.1) -> SECURITY DEFINER functions (owner `migration_role`, GRANT EXECUTE to `retention_service_role`) -> per-event-type and per-table DELETEs bounded by `RETENTION_SCHEDULE` / `OPERATIONAL_TABLE_SCHEDULE`. The audit-log `retention.deleted` summary row is the LAST write in the transaction (F-24 variant; see F-58). When the diagram is next refreshed, add a B6 box labelled "Retention service-role (non-login, SECURITY DEFINER bounded by closed schedule)" with arrows: pg_cron -> sweep fn -> DELETEs (per-event-type, per-table) -> retention.deleted (LAST) -> `retention_sweep_runs` checkpoint.

#### Data flows (T16 library shape; T16.1 SQL shape mirrors)

```
[Retention sweep pass — per ADR-0017 §6 algorithm]
  Caller (CI test in T16; pg_cron / Edge Fn in T16.1)
    -> runRetentionPass({store, config})
       1. store.findOpenRun(lease_window_ms)            // lease acquire (B6 entry)
          if existing -> return {status: 'lease_held'}  // F-59
       2. store.recordSweepRun({run_id, started_at_ms, status: 'running'})
       3. for each RetentionEventType in alphabetised order:    // F-55 closed-allowlist
            cutoff = resolveCutoff(RETENTION_SCHEDULE[event_type], nowMs)
            if event_type is 'retention.deleted': skip (F-62 carve-out)
            if kind is 'match_underlying':
              ask store.isTargetGoneFor(target_id, source_table)  // F-61 ceiling
              gate on (linked_record_deleted_for >30d)
            store.deleteForEventType(event_type, cutoff, batch_size)  // F-64 no WHERE
            accumulate per_event_counts
            check per_pass_row_cap                       // F-60 row-cap
       4. for each table in OPERATIONAL_TABLE_SCHEDULE:
            store.deleteForTable(table_name, predicate, batch_size)  // F-56 totp 24h
            accumulate per_table_counts
       5. if total > alarm_threshold (default 20):       // F-57 over-delete alarm
            result.alarm_fired = true (T16.1 emits A-RETENTION-001)
       6. summary = buildRetentionDeletedSummary({       // F-58 audit-WITH-side-effect
            run_id, started_at_ms, ended_at_ms,
            schedule_hash,                                // F-63 binds to schedule version
            per_event_counts, per_table_counts,
            prev_pass_hash, status })
       7. store.emitRetentionDeleted(summary)           // LAST write in tx
          if throws: ENTIRE TRANSACTION ROLLS BACK
                     (no deletes, no summary; F-58 invariant)
       8. store.closeSweepRun(run_id, {status, ended_at_ms, ...})  // F-68 RA-2 anchor
  Errors throughout: {run_id, status, error_code} only  // F-66 no PII

[Dry-run mode (CI test default per F-57)]
  step 3/4 use countCandidates* instead of delete*;
  summary is built but NOT emitted; result returns would-delete counts.
```

Classification per surface: `retention_sweep_runs` carries NO PI (counts + run metadata only; confirmed per ADR-0017 §8 of T16.1 deliverables). `retention.deleted` audit rows carry NO `target_id` (ADR-0015 carve-out) and store actor as the synthetic `retention_service` HMAC pseudonym. The sweep itself reads `audit_log.retention_class` (C1) and writes `audit_log` (C1); it never reads or writes C3/C4 plaintext. Residency: ca-central-1 (no new processor, no new cross-border flow — confirmed in ADR-0017 §Compliance check). Retention of the surfaces themselves: `retention_sweep_runs` = 7y (mirrors `retention.deleted`); `audit_log_retention_schedule` = permanent_schema_table.

#### STRIDE scoring table — F-55 through F-69

| F-### | Lineage (architect ask)                | STRIDE                                                                                                                   | Asset / code path                                                                                                        | Mitigation (testable assertion)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Residual                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Test obligation                                                                                                                              | Scope                                                                                                                                      |
| ----- | -------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| F-55  | F-R1 / F-19                            | T (Tampering of code paths via mirror drift) + E (Elevation via missing schedule entry deleting more than intended)      | `RetentionEventType` union vs `RETENTION_SCHEDULE` const; ADR-0017 §2, §3                                                | _"Library CI parses `RETENTION_SCHEDULE` + asserts every value in the closed `RetentionEventType` union has exactly one entry; every `RETENTION_SCHEDULE` key is in the union. Drift fails CI. Removing any entry fails CI. Adding a key not in the union fails CI."_                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | **Low** (with CI test); without the test this would be Medium-High because a missing entry would silently skip an event type in the sweep.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | T16-DRIFT-1 (single test exercises three drift conditions).                                                                                  | T16 (library CI). Cross-mirror SQL drift deferred to T16.1 per ADR-0017 §H.                                                                |
| F-56  | F-R2 / G-T05-7                         | I (Information disclosure via stale TOTP-consumed rows) + T (Tampering — stale rows correlate with auth flow timing)     | `auth_totp_consumed_log` table sweep at 24h; ADR-0017 §6 step 4                                                          | _"Fixture seeds rows with `consumed_at` of -23h, -25h, -100h; library `runRetentionPass` deletes rows at -25h and -100h, preserves the -23h row. `OPERATIONAL_TABLE_SCHEDULE['auth_totp_consumed_log']` is `{kind: 'fixed_hours', hours: 24}`."_                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | **Low**                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | T16-SWEEP-OPS-1. #### F-57 math note (architect ask #1: drives F-51 Medium → Low?)

F-51's original residual was "Medium — high blast radius" because the sole control was "Crypto-shred for E2EE'd records; deletion logged; alert on volume" with no quantification of the volume threshold or default posture. F-57 generalises F-51 to ALL retention-eligible tables (not only `reprisal_log`) and stacks three controls:

1. **Dry-run as CI default.** Every CI run of the sweep is dry-run, so a regression that would mass-delete is caught BEFORE the live path executes. Likelihood of a bug reaching production with a delete-side-effect: high → low, because the implementer cannot land a green CI on a bug that would delete more than the fixture expects.
2. **Per-pass row-cap (default 20000).** Even a runaway sweep cannot delete more than `max_total_rows_per_pass` per execution. The blast radius is capped: at one pass per day (T16.1 pg_cron schedule), the maximum unrecoverable loss is bounded per 24h. Impact of a successful exploit / bug: high → medium, because hot recovery from a single pass is feasible from the backup (ADR-0012's pg_dump, 35-day retention) — the backup carries the rows the sweep deleted.
3. **Over-delete alarm at threshold 20 (configurable).** A pass whose deletes exceed 20 rows trips `alarm_fired = true`, emits the alarm via T16.1's A-RETENTION-001, and an operator reviews before the next pass at 03:30 ET. Operator latency: <24h in normal operation. Time-to-detect a runaway: ≤24h, often minutes once observability-setup wires the alert sink.

**Combined likelihood:** Low. A bug must (a) escape the drift test (F-55), (b) escape the dry-run CI test (F-57), (c) escape the alarm review window, AND (d) operate within the row-cap. The compound probability is at the "low" end across realistic deployment.

**Combined impact:** Medium. The row-cap bounds the per-pass blast radius to 20000 rows; the 35-day pg_dump window bounds recovery to the last 24h of writes-since-dump (acceptable per ADR-0015 §Risks "transient inconsistency is acceptable" posture). Not Low because a runaway hitting C4 audit metadata is still operationally painful; not High because the cap + backup combination is structural.

**Residual: Low.** F-57 drives F-51 down from Medium to Low when (1)+(2)+(3) all hold AND the T16.1 alarm wiring lands. Until T16.1 lands, residual is "Low (CI) / Medium (production-untested)" — the test obligation (T16-ALARM-1, T16-DRY-RUN-1) plus the architect-mandated production prerequisite (T16.1 A-RETENTION-001) carry the assertion.

#### F-58 invariant note (architect ask #2: F-24 inversion, not weakening)

F-24 in this file (export pipeline) reads "audit-BEFORE-side-effect": the export audit row commits before the Blob URL is created and the file leaves the worker's browser. The inversion intuition is "if the audit fails, the side-effect is harmless because nothing was disclosed." For retention sweep, F-24 takes a structurally equivalent form with the ordering INVERTED in time but the invariant PRESERVED:

- **The invariant (both F-24 and F-58):** _no side-effect commits without its audit row, and no audit row commits without its corresponding side-effect._
- **F-24 (export):** audit emitted first, side-effect (Blob URL) follows. Failure mode = audit emit fails → no Blob URL.
- **F-58 (retention sweep):** side-effects (deletes) accumulate within an open transaction, summary row written LAST inside the same transaction. Failure mode = summary emit fails → ENTIRE transaction rolls back → no deletes commit AND no summary row. Per ADR-0017 §Option D: "the summary row is the LAST row written in the transaction (after the deletes) so its `meta.deleted_per_table` / `meta.deleted_per_event_type` counts are authoritative for what landed."

The audit-WITH-side-effect form is **stronger** than audit-BEFORE-side-effect for this surface because the summary row's counts are authoritative — they cannot understate what landed (the deletes already executed within the same tx) and they cannot overstate (a failed summary emit takes the deletes down with it). For the export surface F-24's "audit-BEFORE" is the right pattern because the export side-effect (file leaves the browser) is irreversible once it occurs; for the sweep, the deletes are reversible only within the open transaction, so the summary-LAST pattern guarantees atomicity.

**Verdict:** F-58 is a coherent F-24 variant, not a weakening. Test obligations T16-ATOMIC-1 (force summary throw → assert rollback) and T16-ATOMIC-2 (force mid-batch delete throw after summary built → assert rollback) pin the invariant directly. Per-batch savepoints are explicitly rejected (ADR-0017 §Option D) because they admit a partial-state failure mode that would weaken the invariant.

#### F-59 / F-60 new-surface mitigations beyond library expressivity (architect ask #3)

The library (T16) cannot express all the controls these surfaces need; T16.1 must add:

**F-59 (lease / pg_cron race) — STRIDE: T (tampering of state via double-pass) + D (lock contention).**

- T16 library covers: checkpoint-row-based lease via `findOpenRun`. Sufficient for cooperative single-caller in-process tests. Test: T16-LEASE-1, T16-LEASE-2.
- T16.1 must add: `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('retention_sweep'))` inside the SECURITY DEFINER `runRetentionPass` wrapper function, BEFORE the checkpoint-row lookup. Two simultaneous pg_cron firings (e.g., a manual re-trigger overlapping the 03:30 ET scheduled run) serialise at the advisory lock. The library's `lease_held` return value continues to be the operator-visible signal. Test obligation T16.1-LEASE-LOCK-1: simulate concurrent invocations (two psql sessions, second invoked before first commits); assert second returns `lease_held` without attempting any DELETE.

**F-60 (per-pass row-cap / starvation) — STRIDE: D (denial of service) + T (incorrect partial recovery).**

- T16 library covers: `max_total_rows_per_pass` cap + `per_event_batch_size` and `per_table_batch_size` batching + `status='capped'` resume contract. Sufficient for deterministic batch boundaries in tests. Test: T16-CAP-1, T16-CAP-2.
- T16.1 must add: (a) `SET LOCAL statement_timeout = '60s'` and `SET LOCAL lock_timeout = '5s'` on every SECURITY DEFINER sweep function so the pass yields under contention rather than blocking auth-flow writers; (b) pg_cron schedule explicitly set to 03:30 ET (after the 03:00 ET pg_dump per ADR-0012) so the sweep does not contend with the backup; (c) the per-function comment must record both timeouts and the schedule rationale. Test obligations T16.1-TIMEOUT-1 (assert `current_setting('statement_timeout')` inside the function body is 60s; assert `lock_timeout` is 5s) and T16.1-PG-CRON-SCHEDULE-1 (`SELECT schedule FROM cron.job WHERE jobname = 'retention_sweep'` returns the daily 03:30 ET expression).

Both T16.1 additions are recorded in ADR-0017's sibling task spec items #5 and §Risks ("Lock-hold-time on `auth_sessions`"); this threat-model entry pins them as test obligations for the T16.1 pgTAP suite.

#### Residual assessment (aggregate)

All fifteen findings score Low at the library boundary (T16). Five carry a T16.1-deferred component that is required before the production wire-up clears: F-59 (advisory lock), F-60 (timeouts + cron stagger), F-64 (SQL function signature), F-66 (`xact_start()`), F-69 (pgTAP reconciliation). One — F-57 — is "Low (CI) / Medium (production-untested)" until A-RETENTION-001 is wired by observability-setup after T16.1. No finding is Critical or High at any horizon.

Aggregate posture: **Low residual** for the retention-sweep family with the T16.1 deferred items tracked as carry-forwards. F-51 (the pre-existing entry) is **closed by F-57** when T16.1 ships; until then, F-51's residual remains "Medium — high blast radius" _only as the production claim_, downgraded to Low at the library boundary.

#### Re-open triggers

This section re-opens if any of the following:

1. A new audit-log event type is added without all four mirrors (TS const, SQL function, SQL schedule table, RetentionEventType enum). The drift test (F-55) catches this in CI; if the test is disabled or the mirrors silently diverge, F-55 re-opens and the entire family is re-scored.
2. The `retention.deleted` carve-out (F-62) is altered (e.g., a `target_id` is added). The 7y independent retention assumes no target — adding one re-opens F-61 and F-62 jointly.
3. The hard-delete-uniformly semantics (ADR-0017 §Option A) is reversed to pseudonym-only redaction. F-58, F-61, F-62 re-score under a different invariant; the entire family requires re-pass.
4. Pre-deletion user notification is added (HG-10 fires retroactively per a regulator request). New surface for notification race and consent-revocation; new findings F-### in §3.9 family.
5. `retention_sweep_runs` is shortened below 7y or `audit_log_retention_schedule` is made non-permanent. F-68 / F-69 re-open (the reconciliation anchor and the export retention preservation depend on these).
6. A second sweep mechanism is added (e.g., a per-request "right of erasure" path under PIPEDA Principle 4.5 ad-hoc deletion). New finding for "ad-hoc DELETE outside the schedule" — currently structurally forbidden by the closed allowlist; relaxing it re-opens F-64.
7. `pg_advisory_xact_lock` is removed from T16.1 (e.g., for performance). F-59 re-scores to Medium; the architect must justify in an amendment.

#### Carry-forwards (test-writer / implementer must observe)

#### Architect ask #4 verdict — RA-1 control #5 and RA-2 trigger #3 NOT re-opened

**RA-1 compensating control #5 (post-export notification surface).** The sweep cannot shorten `export.generated` retention because (a) `RETENTION_SCHEDULE['export.generated']` is `{kind: 'fixed_years', years: 7}` in the frozen const (ADR-0017 §3, verbatim ADR-0015 mirror); (b) F-63's `schedule_hash` binds the audit row to the exact schedule version that produced it — any runtime tampering shifts the hash and the integrity check (F-50 + F-69) attributes the divergence; (c) F-68's test obligation pins the resolved cutoff to exactly 7y. The post-export notification surface (`ExportStore.sendPostExportNotification`) is NOT a retention target — it is logic, not stored data — and the audit row it depends on retains for 7y. **Verdict: NOT re-opened.** Confirmed; F-68 is the standing assertion.

**RA-2 trigger #3 (live-chain vs pg_dump divergence).** Pre-ADR-0017, an audit row absent from the live chain but present in pg_dump was treated as a tamper. Post-ADR-0017, the sweep is the legitimate DELETE path on `audit_log`; the structured `retention_sweep_runs.per_event_counts` jsonb anchors the attribution. RA-2 trigger #3 semantics are UNCHANGED — it still fires on **unattributed** divergence; attributed divergence (i.e., a row whose deletion timestamp and event type are accounted for in a sweep-pass row) is the new audited expected case. T18's integrity job inherits the join as G-T16-8. **Verdict: NOT re-opened.** Confirmed; F-69 is the standing assertion.

**Architect's claim validated.** No BLOCK from threat-modeler on either surface.

#### Architect ask #5 verdict — HG-10 NOT firing is defensible

PIPEDA Principle 4.5 (Limiting Retention) requires that PI be retained only as long as necessary to fulfil the identified purposes; it does **not** mandate pre-deletion notice to the individual. PIPEDA Principle 4.9 (Individual Access) requires that on request, an individual be given access to their PI — but it operates on the existing record, not on a future-deletion-pending record. ADR-0017's underlying-record-ceiling rule guarantees that audit rows expire AFTER the underlying record they reference, so a user querying their data while their membership is active sees the complete record; deletion at the floor is structural and follows the retention promise the user agreed to at consent time (the privacy policy / `.context/constraints.md` posture).

A pre-deletion notification surface would introduce: (a) a "deletion is pending; please confirm" interaction surface that ADR-0017 §Option F deliberately omits; (b) a new race between notification delivery, user response window, and the sweep's lease window; (c) a new attack surface for the employer adversary (A1) to subpoena a "pending deletion" snapshot. The threat-model concurs with ADR-0017 that v1 ships without pre-deletion notification and that HG-10 (if it existed for this purpose) does NOT fire.

If a regulator surfaces a pre-deletion-notice requirement post-launch, the carry-forward path is an ADR amendment re-firing HG-10 explicitly with new findings under §3.9. **Verdict: HG-10 NOT firing is defensible.** No BLOCK from threat-modeler.

#### Handoff to test-writer

Each F-### below maps to exactly one test in `apps/web/test/T16/` (library scope) or `supabase/tests/T16_1/` (SQL scope, deferred). The test-writer's deliverable for T16 is the library-scope set; the T16.1 set lands when that sibling ships.

| F-### | Test obligation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | File suggestion                                                                                           | Scope                                                                                                           |
| ----- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| F-55  | Drift between `RETENTION_SCHEDULE` and `RetentionEventType` enum fails CI. Three sub-assertions: every enum value has exactly one schedule entry; every schedule key is in enum; removing/adding an entry asymmetrically fails CI.                 | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-schedule-drift.test.ts`                                                      | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |
| F-56  | `auth_totp_consumed_log` sweep at 24h; fixture at -23h/-25h/-100h; -25h and -100h deleted, -23h preserved.                                                                                                                                         | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (totp section)                                                | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |
| F-57  | Dry-run is CI default; alarm fires at default threshold = 20; `meta.alarm_fired = true` on summary row when triggered; `meta.severity = 'warn'` when alarm fires.                                                                                  | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (alarm section)                                               | T16 (library); A-RETENTION-001 alert wiring DEFERRED to T16.1 + observability-setup.                            |
| F-58  | Force `emitRetentionDeleted` to throw → no deletes commit, no summary row. Force mid-batch delete to throw → same outcome. Clean pass → summary counts equal live deltas.                                                                          | `apps/web/test/T16/closed-allowlist-and-audit-before.test.ts` (atomicity section)                         | T16 (library); single-Postgres-tx assertion DEFERRED to T16.1 pgTAP.                                            |
| F-59  | Open run row within lease window → `runRetentionPass` returns `{status: 'lease_held'}` and performs no deletes. Open run row older than lease window → pass proceeds.                                                                              | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (lease section)                                               | T16 (library); `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` DEFERRED to T16.1.                                                   |
| F-60  | 25000 rows + cap 20000 → first pass deletes 20000 with `status='capped'`; second pass deletes 5000 with `status='completed'`.                                                                                                                      | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (cap section)                                                 | T16 (library); `statement_timeout`/`lock_timeout` DEFERRED to T16.1.                                            |

Same row at 29d → not swept.                                                                                                                                      | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (underlying-record-ceiling section)                           | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |

Underlying-record-ceiling does not apply.                                                                                                                             | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (carve-out section)                                           | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |
| F-63  | Monkey-patch one schedule entry between passes; `meta.schedule_hash` differs across summaries; hash is `SHA-256(canonical-JSON(...))`.                                                                                                             | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-schedule-drift.test.ts` (schedule_hash section)                              | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |
| F-64  | TypeScript-level: `RetentionStore` exposes only the three-arg `deleteForEventType`; ESLint rule `no-spread-into-retention-schedule` fires on `{...RETENTION_SCHEDULE}` outside `schedule.ts`.                                                      | `apps/web/test/T16/closed-allowlist-and-audit-before.test.ts` (type-level + ESLint section)               | T16 (library); SQL function signature DEFERRED to T16.1.                                                        |
| F-65  | Type-level: `RetentionStore` does NOT have `__debug*`; `TestRetentionStore extends RetentionStore` does. Cast attempt fails type-check.                                                                                                            | `apps/web/test/T16/closed-allowlist-and-audit-before.test.ts` (type-split section) or a `.test-d.ts` file | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |
| F-66  | `MemoryRetentionStore.nowMs()` strictly monotonic across 1000 consecutive calls.                                                                                                                                                                   | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (now-ms section)                                              | T16 (library); `xact_start()` DEFERRED to T16.1.                                                                |
| F-67  | Force every error path (seven sub-cases) in `runRetentionPass`; assert each carries only `{run_id, status, error_code}` and contains no UUID other than `run_id`, no email-shaped string, no pseudonym-shaped 32-hex string, no `*_ct` field name. | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (no-pii-errors section)                                       | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |
| F-68  | Snapshot resolved cutoff for `export.generated`; assert equals `nowMs() - 7y` exactly. Object.freeze prevents runtime shortening; drift test (F-55) catches a static shortening.                                                                   | `apps/web/test/T16/ra1-control-5-preserved.test.ts`                                                       | T16 (library)                                                                                                   |
| F-69  | Sweep deletes N rows; `retention_sweep_runs.per_event_counts` jsonb sums to N. Reconciliation join semantics defined as carry-forward G-T16-8.                                                                                                     | `apps/web/test/T16/retention-sweep.test.ts` (reconciliation section)                                      | T16 (library sum check); cross-table join DEFERRED to T16.1 pgTAP; T18 integrity job DEFERRED to T18 next pass. |

##### Four cross-cutting properties the suite MUST establish

(a) **No caller-supplied WHERE compiles.** Static (TypeScript) assertion lives in F-64; the test suite includes a `.test-d.ts` or expect-type assertion that `RetentionStore['deleteForEventType']` has arity 3 with parameter types `(event_type: RetentionEventType, cutoff_ms: number, max_rows: number)` and the return type does not allow any path through which a caller can inject a predicate. The ESLint rule `no-spread-into-retention-schedule` is exercised by a poisoned fixture file (in a CI-only directory) that is asserted to fail lint.

(b) **Drift between `RETENTION_SCHEDULE` and `RetentionEventType` fails CI.** F-55's three sub-assertions plus a "scrub-and-restore" fixture that temporarily removes one entry from `RETENTION_SCHEDULE` (via mutation of a deep-cloned copy fed through a test-only injection point) and asserts the drift test fails. Adding a non-existent event type to a deep-cloned copy and asserting the drift test fails.

(c) **`retention.deleted` is the LAST row in a sweep transaction.** F-58's two force-throw paths assert atomicity. Additionally: a transaction-order assertion using `MemoryRetentionStore.nowMs()` monotonic clock — the `retention.deleted` row's `meta.ended_at_ms` is strictly greater than every per-event-type and per-table delete's recorded `nowMs()` within the same pass. T16.1's pgTAP suite re-asserts the property at the SQL boundary using `xact_start()` ordering.

(d) **Over-delete alarm fires on threshold.** F-57's fixture sets 25 candidates with default threshold 20; assert `result.alarm_fired === true` and the emitted summary row has `meta.alarm_fired === true` AND `meta.severity === 'warn'`. Boundary: 20 candidates does NOT fire (`alarm_fired === false`); 21 candidates fires. T16.1's wire-up of A-RETENTION-001 is verified by observability-setup's next pass (deferred).

##### Handoff envelope

- **To test-writer:** ADR-0017 §10 originally listed F-R1..F-R15; this §3.9 assigns final numbers F-55..F-69. ADR-0017 §10 is updated below the table to point at the F-### range. All fifteen tests are mandatory for T16's four-way reviewer pass clearance; five carry `[T16.1 deferred]` tags whose tests land later but whose acceptance criteria are recorded now.
- **To security-reviewer:** at diff time on T16 PR, verify F-55 (drift CI), F-58 (atomicity), F-64 (no caller-supplied WHERE at type level + ESLint), F-65 (TestStore type split), F-67 (no PII in errors). At diff time on T16.1 PR (deferred), verify F-59 advisory lock, F-60 timeouts, F-64 SQL signature, F-66 `xact_start()`, F-68 RA-1 control #5, F-69 reconciliation jsonb shape.
- **To privacy-reviewer:** PI inventory for `retention_sweep_runs` (no PI; counts + run metadata only) and `audit_log_retention_schedule` (no PI; schema artifact) lands in T16.1 per G-T16-7. ADR-0017 §Compliance check confirms PIPEDA Principle 4.5 + 4.9 alignment; HG-10 NOT firing is defensible (architect ask #5 verdict above). Cross-border transfers: NONE introduced by this surface (architect ask: confirmed; ADR-0017 §Compliance check `[x] Data residency — no new processor; no new cross-border flow`).
- **To user (human-gate items):**
  - **HG-15 (re-fires at T16.1 PR submission)** for the two new physical tables `retention_sweep_runs` and `audit_log_retention_schedule`. Recorded in ADR-0017 §Compliance check.
  - **HG-10 explicitly NOT firing** in this pass (architect ask #5 verdict above; ADR-0017 §Option F).
  - **No new HG fires in T16 itself.**

---

### 3.10 Backup posture (T17 library + T17.1 SQL + Storage bucket — supersedes the §3.7 placeholder for the T17 surface)

Source: ADR-0018 (T17 backup object-lock library + MemoryBackupStore), 2026-05-23. Closes the F-48/F-49 placeholder surfaces with concrete library-level test obligations and stands up RA-2 compensating control #4 as a structurally testable join surface. The §3.7 entries F-48 and F-49 are NOT renumbered (history-preserving); F-70..F-85 below are the authoritative T17 surface and supersede the §3.7 narrative where they overlap (F-49 object-lock posture is now structurally enforced by F-71 + F-75 + F-84; F-48 key-handling posture is now structurally enforced by F-73 — `committee_data_key` wrap rather than bucket-adjacent dump-key — closing the F-48 narrative under ADR-0007 / ADR-0010 trust boundary).

**Scope split:** F-70..F-85 below are scored as a family. Library-scope assertions land in T17 (CI tests against `MemoryBackupStore`). Storage-bucket-scope and SQL-scope assertions land in T17.1 (pgTAP, `SupabaseBackupStore`, Supabase Storage bucket with object-lock policy, pg_cron wrapper, A-BACKUP-001/002/003 alert wiring, restore runbook). Each row tags `[T17]` or `[T17.1 deferred]` for the test-writer. **HG-10 explicitly does NOT fire** (zero user-facing copy; verdict and PIPEDA Principle 4.8 walk below). **HG-15 fires at T17.1 PR submission** (one new physical table `backup_manifests` + one new Supabase Storage bucket `backups-ca-central-1`; ADR-0018 §15 sibling task spec).

#### Trust boundaries this introduces

- **B6.1 — `backup_writer_role` boundary (added here; activates at T17.1; library shape preserved in T17).** A non-login `backup_writer_role` in T17.1 holds `GRANT EXECUTE` on the `SECURITY DEFINER` backup functions (`backup_extract_head_pointer`, `backup_dump_closed_allowlist(p_tables text[])`, `backup_write_manifest_pending`, `backup_transition_manifest_status`, `backup_list_manifests_older_than_ms`, `backup_emit_manifest_written`, `backup_has_open_run_within_window`, `deleteObjectIfUnlocked`). It is a SIBLING role to `retention_service_role` (B6, T16.1) and `audit_writer_role` — NOT an expansion of either. It has NO `GRANT` on base tables beyond explicit SELECT on the `BACKUP_TABLES` allowlist for the dump function, and no `BYPASSRLS`. The function bodies hard-code the table allowlist from the passed array; no caller-supplied predicate path. The library half (T17) mirrors this at the type level: `BackupStore` forbids caller-supplied `object_ref`, `table_list`, `lock_duration_ms`, or predicate; the only configurable surface is `dry_run` + `lease_window_ms`. Treat B6.1 as "type-level in T17, role-level in T17.1." Reference: ADR-0018 §4, §6, §11; sibling task spec items #1, #4, #11.
- **B7 — Object-lock storage boundary (added here; library-modelled in T17 as a store-side predicate; ratified by Supabase Storage in T17.1).** The `backups-ca-central-1` bucket holds the encrypted dump blobs under an S3-compatible object-lock policy (governance mode, 42-day retention). The invariant is: **within the lock window, no actor — including `backup_writer_role` itself — can overwrite or delete an object.** The library models this as `BackupStore.isObjectLocked(object_ref): Promise<boolean>` + `BackupStore.deleteObjectIfUnlocked(object_ref)` returning `{deleted: false, reason: 'still_locked'}` when the lock has not expired. The lock duration is library-controlled (`BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS = 42`) — never caller-supplied — so a cooperative caller cannot weaken the policy. T17.1 the bucket's policy answer is the production source of truth; T17 the library's `MemoryBackupStore` predicate is the test surface. Two-layer hard-delete at 42d (bucket lifecycle policy + library's explicit `runBackupRetentionPass`) is the constraints.md "Deletion is real deletion" honourer. Reference: ADR-0018 Decision §6, §9; sibling task spec item #3.
- **B8 — Restore-as-superuser boundary (added here; runbook-enforced in T17.1).** Implicit boundary surfaced by Hard Rule #2 cross-reference. A restore loads the encrypted blob, fetches the historical wrap from `committee_key_wraps_history` for the manifest's `committee_data_key_kid`, decrypts the DEK, decrypts the blob, and writes into a target Postgres. Default target is a staging project in `ca-central-1` (Hard Rule #4 invariant preserved); **restore-into-prod outside an approved incident is forbidden by the T17.1 restore runbook** because the restore writes operate above RLS (superuser path bypasses C3/C4 protection at the moment of write). The restore-as-superuser path is the only B8 crossing in normal operation; under incident response it is gated by the runbook checklist + the monthly drill cadence (ADR-0018 Option D). Reference: ADR-0018 Decision §6 (Option D), sibling task spec item #14.
- **Diagram note (consolidated diagram, §1 of this file).** B6.1 + B7 + B8 sit inside the Supabase-cloud box. B6.1 sits adjacent to B6 (`retention_service_role`) and the existing `audit_writer_role`. B7 wraps the new `backups-ca-central-1` bucket. B8 is a dotted-line egress from the bucket back into a separate `ca-central-1` staging Postgres (NOT into the live project's RLS-bound tables). Edge: pg_cron daily 03:00 ET → `backup_writer_role` SECURITY DEFINER `runBackupPass` wrapper → (1) head-pointer extract, (2) dump closed allowlist, (3) encrypt with current `committee_data_key.kid`, (4) write manifest pending row, (5) put-with-object-lock to B7 bucket, (6) transition manifest committed, (7) emit `backup.manifest_written` audit row (LAST). A separate daily 04:00 ET pg_cron drives `runBackupRetentionPass` → `deleteObjectIfUnlocked` for each manifest older than 42d → transition manifest `hard_deleted` → emit `backup.hard_deleted` audit row. When the diagram is next refreshed, add a B6.1 box adjacent to B6, a B7 box around `backups-ca-central-1`, and a dotted-line B8 egress to staging.

#### Data flows (T17 library shape; T17.1 SQL + Storage shape mirrors)

```
[Backup pass — per ADR-0018 §5 algorithm]
  Caller (CI test in T17; pg_cron daily 03:00 ET in T17.1)
    -> runBackupPass({store, config})
       1. store.hasOpenBackupRunWithinWindow(nowMs, lease_window_ms)
            if true -> return {status: 'skipped', reason: 'pass_already_in_window'}
            (F-59-pattern; SQL half lands in T17.1 as pg_try_advisory_xact_lock per G-T16-1)
       2. head = await store.extractHeadPointer()
            // head = {id, ts_ms, hash} of highest audit_log row at dump-start
            // F-76 RA-2 follow-up anchor; head BEFORE dump so chain state is captured
       3. kid = await store.currentCommitteeDataKeyKid()
            // ADR-0007 wrap reference; F-73 manifest carries this
       4. {blob, per_table_row_counts, per_event_row_counts,
           retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms}
              = await store.dumpClosedAllowlist(BACKUP_TABLES)
            // F-70 closed-allowlist; F-77 per-event preserved (NEVER aggregated)
            // F-84 BACKUP_TABLES hard-coded; no caller-supplied table_list
       5. sha256 = hexSha256(blob)
            // F-78 pinned-hex determinism (G-T11-23)
       6. build pending manifest:
            { run_id, status: 'pending', sha256, bytes, audit_log_head: head,
              per_table_row_counts, per_event_row_counts,
              retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms,
              committee_data_key_kid: kid, schedule_hash,
              node_runtime_pin: {node_version, openssl_version},
              retention_class: '42d',
              lock_until_ms: nowMs + BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS * MS_PER_DAY }
       7. store.writeManifestPending(manifest)
            // F-72 F-24 INVERSION: manifest WRITTEN before upload
            // If THIS write fails: return errored; NO upload attempted
       8. result = store.putWithObjectLock(object_ref, blob, lock_until_ms)
            // object_ref = backupObjectRefFor(manifest) — library-derived; F-84
            // On failure: transitionManifestStatus(run_id, 'aborted_' + reason, nowMs)
            //             return {status: 'errored', error_code: 'backup_upload_failed',
            //                     upload_reason: result.reason, run_id}
            // NEVER returns {status: 'completed'} on a non-ACK upload (F-82, G-T11-29)
            // Structured rejection vocabulary: 'object_lock_policy_rejected'
            //                                  'storage_quota_exceeded'
            //                                  'cross_region_destination_refused' (Hard Rule #4)
            //                                  'unknown_storage_error'
       9. store.transitionManifestStatus(run_id, 'committed', nowMs)
            // If throws AFTER successful upload: manifest stays 'pending';
            // next-pass reconciliation surfaces it. T17.1 wraps 7-9 in single tx.
      10. store.emitBackupManifestWritten(audit_row)
            // event_type: 'backup.manifest_written' (new enum; T17.1 dance)
            // actor_pseudonym at TOP LEVEL only (F-79; G-T16-PRIV-1)
            // meta carries the FULL manifest superset (F-80; structural only)
            // LAST step of the pass; emit failure does NOT roll back upload+manifest
            // (accepted tradeoff; manifest status='committed' is the persistent record)
  Errors throughout: {run_id, status, error_code, upload_reason?} only
                     (F-81; G-T16-PRIV-3 / G-T11-29 — no PII shapes, no row excerpts)

[Backup retention pass — per ADR-0018 §5 step 11 + Decision §9]
  Caller (CI test in T17; pg_cron daily 04:00 ET in T17.1)
    -> runBackupRetentionPass({store, config})
       1. cutoff_ms = nowMs - BACKUP_HARD_DELETE_DAYS * MS_PER_DAY
       2. manifests = store.listManifestsOlderThanMs(cutoff_ms)
            // committed-status only; pending/aborted/hard_deleted excluded
       3. for each manifest in manifests:
            result = store.deleteObjectIfUnlocked(manifest.object_ref)
            if result.deleted: store.transitionManifestStatus(run_id, 'hard_deleted', nowMs)
                               emit backup.hard_deleted audit row (enum dance, T17.1)
            if result.reason === 'still_locked' AND manifest age past 42d window:
              result.would_fire_alert = 'A-BACKUP-001' (sink lands in T17.1)
              // F-75 — refusal pre-window is structural; layer 1 defense-in-depth
              //        backstop is the bucket's lifecycle policy auto-release at 42d
  Errors: same vocabulary as pass; no PII (F-81)

[Restore pass — runbook-driven; T17.1 deferred; B8 crossing]
  Operator (runbook checklist) -> restore script
       1. Select target = staging (default); production is incident-only
       2. Fetch manifest from backup_manifests by run_id
       3. Lookup committee_key_wraps_history[manifest.committee_data_key_kid]
          if aged-out: undecryptable (crypto-shred is structural; ADR-0007 / ADR-0012)
       4. Unwrap DEK with historical wrap; decrypt blob
       5. Load into staging Postgres; never into live RLS-bound tables
       6. Emit restore.executed audit row (T17.1 enum dance; out of scope for T17 library)
```

Classification per surface: `backup_manifests` carries NO PI (structural metadata only — `run_id`, `sha256`, `bytes`, kid, counts, head-pointer tuple `(id, ts_ms, hash)`, snapshot timestamps, schedule_hash, node_runtime_pin; **NO pseudonyms** — F-80; **NO target_ids** — head-pointer's `id` is an audit_log row id, not a target_id of a PI record). The encrypted dump blob in B7 carries the union of all `BACKUP_TABLES` ciphertext (C1 audit-log rows + C3/C4 operational PI rows wrapped under `committee_data_key`-derived DEK + `committee_key_wraps_history` rows — the historical wraps are themselves at-rest encrypted via Supabase's transparent encryption inside `ca-central-1`). The `backup.manifest_written` audit row carries the synthetic `HMAC('system:backup-pass')` actor_pseudonym (mirrors `system:retention` from ADR-0017) and the manifest's structural fields in `meta` (G-T16-PRIV-7 — structural only). Residency: ca-central-1 (no new processor; library is region-agnostic but exposes `cross_region_destination_refused` structured rejection; T17.1 ratifies the bucket region pin). Retention: `backup_manifests` rows = 7y (mirrors `retention.deleted` and the `backup.manifest_written` audit row — manifest is the audit anchor surface; outlives the dump blob it points to); dump blobs in B7 = 42d hard-delete (ADR-0012 amendment HG-8; two-layer enforcement); `committee_key_wraps_history` rows = per ADR-0007 amendment (must cover 42d backup window for restorability; crypto-shred is structural beyond that).

| F-70  | F-19 / F-55 mirror                 | T (Tampering of code paths via mirror drift) + E (Elevation via missing/extra allowlist entry expanding dump scope or dropping a target table)                                                                      | `BackupTable` union vs `BACKUP_TABLES` frozen const; ADR-0018 §2, §3                                                                                                         | _"Library CI parses `BACKUP_TABLES` + asserts every value in the closed `BackupTable` union has exactly one allowlist entry; every `BACKUP_TABLES` entry is in the union; allowlist is `Object.isFrozen`. Removing any entry fails CI. Adding a key not in the union fails CI. Every `BACKUP_TABLES` entry has a §PI inventory row (T17 asserts against a pinned fixture list; T17.1 ratifies against the actual §PI inventory). ESLint rule `no-spread-into-backup-tables` forbids spread-into-`BACKUP_TABLES` outside `backup-tables.ts`."_                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | **Low** (with CI test); without the test this would be Medium-High because a missing entry would silently drop a target table from the dump (RA-2 trigger #3 would then fire on the next reconciliation because the head-pointer would not match the live chain).                                          | T17-DRIFT-1 (set-equality + freeze), T17-DRIFT-2 (§PI inventory fixture pinning), T17-DRIFT-3 (ESLint rule).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | T17 (library CI). Cross-mirror SQL drift (TS const vs SQL `backup_writer_role` GRANT footprint) deferred to T17.1 per ADR-0018 sibling task spec #6.                                                          |
| F-71  | NEW SURFACE — store-side invariant | T (Tampering of dump blobs via early delete) + E (Elevation via cooperative-caller weakening the lock duration) + R (Repudiation of "we object-locked this")                                                        | `MemoryBackupStore.deleteObjectIfUnlocked` refusal; cooperative-caller defense; ADR-0018 Decision §6 + §9; **B7 boundary**                                                   | _"`MemoryBackupStore.deleteObjectIfUnlocked(object_ref)` returns `{deleted: false, reason: 'still_locked'}` for any object whose `unlocked_at_ms > nowMs()`, regardless of caller 'intent.' Test: put an object with a 42d lock; immediately attempt delete; assert refusal. Test: put an object with a 42d lock; advance `__debugSetClock` to lock_until_ms - 1; assert refusal. Test: advance clock to lock_until_ms + 1; assert delete succeeds. Type-level: `BackupPassConfig` does NOT expose `lock_duration_ms` (covered jointly with F-84 type-test). The lock duration is derived from `BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS = 42` exclusively; there is no library path through which a caller can shorten it."_                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | **Low (library)** / **Medium until T17.1 bucket policy ratifies** governance-mode 42-day object-lock at the S3-compatible boundary. T17.1 mitigation beyond library expressivity: bucket policy answer is the production source of truth; the library predicate is the test surface.                       | T17-OBJECT-LOCK-1 (immediate refusal), T17-OBJECT-LOCK-2 (clock-advance boundary), T17-OBJECT-LOCK-3 (release after lock expiry). #### Architect ask #1 verdict — F-72 is a coherent F-24 variant, not a weakening

F-24 in this file (export pipeline) reads "audit-BEFORE-side-effect": the export audit row commits before the Blob URL is created and the file leaves the worker's browser. F-58 (retention sweep) generalises this to "audit-WITH-side-effect": the `retention.deleted` summary row is the LAST write inside a transaction whose deletes have already executed. F-72 (backup) is a THIRD shape — _manifest-WRITTEN-pending-before-upload, status-finalized-after, audit-emitted-after-finalize_ — and we need to verify it preserves the same invariant.

- **The shared invariant (F-24, F-58, F-72):** _no claim of a side-effect having occurred commits without its audit/manifest anchor, and the anchor's content cannot overstate what actually happened._
- **F-24 (export):** audit emitted first; if the audit fails, the side-effect (Blob URL creation) is never reached. The audit row is the claim; the side-effect follows the claim.
- **F-58 (retention sweep):** deletes accumulate inside a tx; summary row is written LAST inside the same tx; if the summary throws, the entire tx rolls back including the deletes. Single atomicity unit.
- **F-72 (backup):** the manifest row is written in `pending` status BEFORE the upload (the manifest is the audit anchor for the upload), then the upload happens, then the manifest transitions to `committed` (on success) or `aborted_<reason>` (on failure). The audit row (`backup.manifest_written`) is emitted AFTER the transition to committed. The state machine is `(no manifest) → pending → (committed | aborted_<reason>) → audit emitted`. Key claim: a manifest in `committed` status is a verifiable claim that the upload received a success ACK (G-T11-29 lesson); a manifest in `aborted_*` status is a verifiable claim that the upload failed with a specific structured reason; a manifest in `pending` status is a verifiable claim that the upload was attempted but the status finalisation crashed (this is the legitimate "stale pending" state that T18's reconciliation surfaces).

The invariant holds: the manifest's status field is the claim surface; the status transition is the moment-of-truth; the audit row is supplementary (its emit failure does NOT roll back the upload, because the manifest itself is the persistent record). Two cases need pinning:

1. **Manifest write fails before upload attempt** (step 7 fails): NO upload attempted; no `__debugListPutCalls` entry; return `{status: 'errored', error_code: 'manifest_write_failed'}`. **Invariant preserved**: no upload claim without manifest.
2. **Upload succeeds but `transitionManifestStatus(committed)` fails** (step 9 throws after step 8 ACKs): manifest stays in `pending`; T17.1's single-tx wrapper makes this case structurally impossible at the SQL boundary (the tx rolls back both the upload — via revoking the put — and the pending manifest); the library captures it via the next-pass reconciliation (a pending manifest older than the lease window is surfaced as a stale state). **Invariant preserved**: a pending manifest is a known recoverable state, not a false-committed claim.

**Verdict:** F-72 is a coherent F-24 variant (third shape; state-machine variant), not a weakening. Test obligations T17-INVERSION-1 (pending-before-upload order observable), T17-INVERSION-2 (each rejection-reason → aborted status), T17-INVERSION-3 (manifest-write failure → no upload) pin the invariant directly.

#### Architect ask #2 verdict — F-71 is a NEW SURFACE

Walked §3.1–§3.9 for an object-lock-as-store-side-invariant equivalent. None of T05 (auth+session), T07 (E2EE keys), T08 (concern intake), T10 (inspection sync), T11 (export), T12 (export retention), T13 (reprisal), T14 (work refusal), or T16 (retention sweep) ship a storage primitive whose write-once-then-immutable contract is enforced at the store boundary. The closest precedent is the F-58 single-transaction atomicity invariant, but that is a transaction-scoped guarantee (within one tx, ordering + rollback) — not a multi-pass immutability contract at the storage layer. F-71 is structurally different:

- **F-58:** "within one transaction, no write commits unless ALL writes succeed." Time-scope: single tx.
- **F-71:** "across the 42-day lock window, no actor — including the writing role itself — can overwrite or delete this object." Time-scope: 42 days, across many txs, across many processes, across many code-paths.

The cooperative-caller defense is also a new pattern: the library exposes `putWithObjectLock(object_ref, blob, lock_until_ms)` for testability (the test can vary `lock_until_ms` via `__debugForceUnlockedAtMs`) but the production caller (`runBackupPass`) computes `lock_until_ms` from `BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS` exclusively. The library NEVER exposes a `lock_duration_ms` config field. This is the same shape as F-84 (no caller-supplied predicate), but applied to a time-bounded immutability contract rather than a query predicate.

**Verdict:** F-71 is a NEW SURFACE. Test obligations T17-OBJECT-LOCK-1/2/3 establish the library-side invariant; T17.1-BUCKET-POLICY-1 ratifies at the S3-compatible boundary.

#### Architect ask #3 verdict — F-83 is LOAD-BEARING; scored accordingly

The three fields (`audit_log_head`, `per_event_row_counts`, `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms`) are not "nice-to-have manifest metadata" — they are the literal join surface T18's reconciliation uses to attribute a divergence. RA-2 trigger #3 reads: _"any divergence between the live chain and the most recent pg_dump backup for a row older than the dump fires on FIRST occurrence regardless of cause."_ The compensating control is "the pg_dump backup is the secondary witness" — but a witness with no testimony format is no witness at all. The three fields are the testimony format:

- `audit_log_head: {id, ts_ms, hash}` — defines "the most recent pg_dump backup" as a specific chain position. Without it, the divergence check has no stable anchor (which audit_log row do we compare against the live chain?).
- `per_event_row_counts` — defines what was IN the dump per event type. Without it, a row absent from the live chain cannot be attributed to (a) a legitimate sweep delete (which would show in the next pass's counts) vs (b) an unattributed tamper.
- `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms` — defines WHEN the dump observed the sweep checkpoint. Without it, sweep deletes that happened post-dump cannot be distinguished from tamper deletes; both look like "row gone from live chain, present in last dump."

If F-83 fails (any field missing, renamed, zeroed, or aggregated-to-sentinel on committed manifests), RA-2 trigger #3 fires on the next reconciliation pass because there is no stable comparison anchor. The score is **Low residual at the library boundary** (because the library structurally enforces it via the type system + the snapshot-pinned field names), but **the score is conditional on T17-RA2-ANCHOR-2** (the field-name snapshot pin) being a hard CI test — without it, a future innocuous rename ("let's call it `chain_head` for brevity") silently breaks the join. The test obligation is the structural seal.

**Verdict:** Scored Low residual; the load-bearing nature is reflected in the test obligation being a snapshot pin (rename-detection), not just an existence check.

#### Architect ask #4 verdict — RA-2 compensating control #4 is STRENGTHENED by T17

Pre-T17, RA-2 compensating control #4 was narrative: "the pg_dump backup is the secondary witness." The witness existed (ADR-0012 ratified the daily pg_dump) but the witness's testimony format was unstructured — a Postgres dump with no companion manifest carrying head-pointer, per-event counts, or sweep-snapshot timestamp. T18's reconciliation job would have to (a) load the entire dump into a staging Postgres, (b) compute its own head-pointer by scanning `audit_log` in the staging copy, (c) compute its own per-event histogram, (d) guess at the sweep state at dump-start, and (e) attempt to compare against the live chain — a fragile, expensive, error-prone path.

T17 strengthens the witness by giving it a structured manifest that exposes the join surface DIRECTLY:

- **Before T17:** witness = opaque pg_dump blob; reconciliation = full restore + scan.
- **After T17:** witness = pg_dump blob + structured manifest carrying `(audit_log_head, per_event_row_counts, retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms, sha256, kid, schedule_hash, node_runtime_pin)`; reconciliation = jsonb comparison against the manifest row + live `audit_log` SELECT at `audit_log_head.id`.

The strengthening claim is verified by walking the T18 reconciliation algorithm:

1. T18 reads the most recent `backup_manifests` row with `status='committed'` (manifest-side; no blob fetch needed for the diff check).
2. T18 reads the live `audit_log` row at `audit_log_head.id`; compares `audit_log.hash` against `manifest.audit_log_head.hash`.
3. If hash matches: no tamper at the head. If hash differs: RA-2 trigger #3 fires with the (live-hash, manifest-hash) pair as evidence.
4. T18 reads `retention_sweep_runs` at `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms`; for any row in `manifest.per_event_row_counts` whose live count is now lower, T18 attributes the delta to sweep passes recorded between `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms` and now; unattributed deltas fire trigger #3.

None of this requires loading the dump blob in the normal-case (no-tamper) path. The blob is the deep-evidence surface for the post-trigger investigation; the manifest is the routine-detection surface. This is a clean strengthening.

**Verdict:** RA-2 compensating control #4 is STRENGTHENED by T17. No BLOCK from threat-modeler.

#### Architect ask #5 verdict — RA-2 trigger #3 is NOT re-opened

Walking each of the four re-open triggers against T17's design:

1. **Platform-admin compromise.** T17 does not change the `audit_writer_role` reach; the new `backup_writer_role` is a sibling role with its own GRANTs (explicit SELECT on `BACKUP_TABLES` + EXECUTE on the SECURITY DEFINER backup functions; NO `GRANT` on `audit_log` writes beyond `backup_emit_manifest_written` which is itself bounded by the function body's hard-coded event_type). A platform-admin compromise has the same blast radius as before; T17 does not expand it. **Not fired.**
2. **Authenticity challenge.** T17 strengthens the authenticity story (the manifest carries `sha256` over the dump bytes, `kid` over the encryption envelope, `audit_log_head` over the chain state, `schedule_hash` over the retention schedule version, `node_runtime_pin` over the toolchain). An authenticity challenge has MORE evidence to point at, not less. **Not fired.**
3. **Current divergence.** T17 is the witness; T18 is the detector. T17's deployment does not by itself create a divergence — it creates the surface for detecting one. The first divergence detected post-T18 deployment would fire trigger #3, but that is the trigger doing its job, not the trigger being re-opened by architectural change. **Not fired by T17's deployment.**
4. **Expansion of `audit_writer_role` reach.** T17 does not expand `audit_writer_role`. The new `backup_writer_role` is a sibling, not a subset/superset. The new `backup.manifest_written` and `backup.hard_deleted` event types are emitted via the dedicated `backup_emit_manifest_written` SECURITY DEFINER function, NOT via the general `audit_log` insert path. **Not fired.**

**Verdict:** None of the four re-open triggers fires. RA-2 trigger #3 is NOT re-opened by T17. Architect's claim validated.

#### Architect ask #6 verdict — HG-10 NOT firing is defensible

T17 ships zero user-facing copy. The backup pass is a background system pass; the retention pass is a background system pass; the restore pass is operator-driven via a runbook (not user-facing). The `backup.manifest_written` and `backup.hard_deleted` audit rows are written under the synthetic `system:backup-pass` actor pseudonym — they are NOT surfaced to the user via any UI in T17 or T17.1.

PIPEDA Principle 4.8 (Openness) requires that an organisation make its policies and practices relating to the management of personal information readily available. The relevant policies for T17 are:

- **The privacy policy** (T17.1 ratifies — generic "we back up your data on a 42-day rolling window in ca-central-1 under encryption at rest" copy lives there; HG-10 covers privacy-policy changes if they happen).
- **The audit log** itself is the operational openness surface — `backup.manifest_written` rows are visible to a user requesting their data per PIPEDA Principle 4.9 (Individual Access), filtered to rows where the user's pseudonym is in `meta` (none, in this case — backup is a system actor; the user does not appear in the audit row). The user's RIGHT to know that backups happen is honoured at the policy layer; the SPECIFIC backup events are operational telemetry not legally required to be surfaced per-event.
- **No new user interaction surface** is introduced by T17 or T17.1 — no "your data was backed up" notification, no "your data will be hard-deleted in N days" notice, no "restore in progress" indicator. All of these would be new HG-10 surfaces if added; none of them are added.

HG-10 (user-facing pre-deletion copy / sensitive interaction surface) does not apply to a background system pass with no user touchpoint. The existing HG-10-covered surfaces (export consent dialog, recovery flow, panic wipe) are unchanged.

**Verdict:** HG-10 NOT firing is defensible. PIPEDA Principle 4.8 is preserved through the policy + audit-log paths. No BLOCK from threat-modeler.

#### Architect ask #7 verdict — Cross-border egress invariant preserved

The library's `BackupStore.putWithObjectLock` exposes `cross_region_destination_refused` as a structured rejection reason. The library NEVER specifies a region in its calls — the bucket region is a deployment-time concern T17.1 ratifies — but the structured rejection vocabulary explicitly includes this reason so a misconfigured production deploy (e.g., a bucket inadvertently created in `us-east-1`) surfaces the failure visibly rather than silently shipping data abroad.

Verification path:

- **Library side (T17):** `MemoryBackupStore.__debugForceCrossRegionDestinationRefused(true)` flips the next `putWithObjectLock` call to return `{committed: false, reason: 'cross_region_destination_refused'}`. The library's `runBackupPass` handles this as a normal upload failure (F-82 path) — the manifest transitions to `aborted_cross_region_destination_refused`, the pass returns `{status: 'errored', error_code: 'backup_upload_failed', upload_reason: 'cross_region_destination_refused'}`, the `A-BACKUP-001`-or-similar alert symbol is returned (operator notice). No data is uploaded; no silent egress.
- **Production side (T17.1):** `SupabaseBackupStore.putWithObjectLock` checks the bucket's region against an expected `'ca-central-1'` constant (sourced from `BACKUP_BUCKET_REGION = 'ca-central-1'` env-constant); if the bucket region differs, return `cross_region_destination_refused` WITHOUT attempting the put. The runbook (T17.1 deliverable) ratifies the bucket region pin; any departure is a flagged decision per Hard Rule #4 + a re-opening of ADR-0001.

This is a coherent library-side guard rail: the structured rejection is the operator-visible signal; the production check is the enforcement layer; the bucket region pin is the configuration ratification. ADR-0001 invariant preserved.

**Verdict:** Cross-border egress invariant preserved. No BLOCK.

#### Architect ask #8 verdict — No new subprocessor

ADR-0010 ratifies Sentry as the only non-Supabase subprocessor. Walking T17's dependencies:

- **Encryption key:** `committee_data_key` (ADR-0007). Held inside the Supabase Postgres trust boundary. No KMS. No external signer. Re-encrypt-on-rotation explicitly rejected (would defeat object-lock; defeats the at-rest immutability contract).
- **Storage:** Supabase Storage bucket `backups-ca-central-1` (T17.1). In-scope Supabase service; in-scope `ca-central-1` region.
- **Scheduler:** pg_cron (T17.1). Postgres extension; in-scope Supabase.
- **Hash function:** `crypto.createHash('sha256')` (Node native, via OpenSSL). In-scope toolchain; `node_runtime_pin` field traces the binding.
- **No third-party signer.** No DocuSign, no Cloudflare R2, no S3-compatible third party (Wasabi, Backblaze), no external KMS (AWS KMS, GCP KMS, Azure Key Vault, HashiCorp Vault). The S3-compatible object-lock policy is enforced by Supabase Storage's S3-compatible API surface — which is Supabase, not AWS.
- **No external alert sink at the library boundary.** A-BACKUP-001/002/003 alert wiring lands in T17.1 + observability-setup; the alert sinks (Sentry; ADR-0010 ratified) are in-scope.

ADR-0010 single-subprocessor posture preserved. No new dependency snuck in.

**Verdict:** No new subprocessor. No BLOCK.

#### Residual assessment (aggregate)

All sixteen findings score Low at the library boundary (T17). Five carry a T17.1-deferred component that is required before the production wire-up clears: F-71 (bucket-policy ratification), F-74 (lifecycle policy backstop), F-75 (A-BACKUP-001 alert sink), F-79 + F-80 (pgTAP column assertions on `backup_manifests`), F-83 (T18 integrity-job consumer). One — F-75 — is "Low (CI) / Medium (production-untested)" until A-BACKUP-001 is wired by observability-setup after T17.1. No finding is Critical or High at any horizon.

Aggregate posture: **Low residual** for the backup-posture family with the T17.1 deferred items tracked as carry-forwards. F-48 (the pre-existing §3.7 entry on dump-key adjacency) is **closed by F-73** when T17.1 ships — the kid-recording posture under ADR-0007 supersedes the "key in 1Password + paper" narrative because the encryption key is structurally inside the Supabase Postgres trust boundary, not adjacent to the bucket. F-49 (the pre-existing §3.7 entry on bucket-credential ransomware-delete) is **closed by F-71 + F-75** when T17.1 ships — object-lock at the store boundary structurally prevents the overwrite/delete-within-window attack the F-49 narrative warned about.

#### Re-open triggers

This section re-opens if any of the following:

1. A new audit-log event type bound to backup is added without all six mirrors (TS const, SQL function, SQL schedule table, RETENTION_SCHEDULE row, BackupTable closed allowlist if it's a new target table, scripts/check-audit-enum-coverage.sh). The drift test (F-70) catches the BackupTable half in CI; the audit-log enum dance (ADR-0003 Amendment A) catches the rest.
2. `BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS` or `BACKUP_HARD_DELETE_DAYS` is changed without an ADR-0012 amendment + this ADR-0018's mirror update + the SQL bucket-policy update (three mirrors; CI drift test in T17.1 catches the TS-vs-SQL drift; ADR-0012 catches the policy ratification).
3. The `committee_data_key` anchor is replaced by an external KMS or per-backup random key (Option B(ii) or B(iii) from ADR-0018). Re-opens ADR-0007 + ADR-0010 + this entry; F-73 re-scores under a different key hierarchy.
4. The single-tx wrapper in T17.1 (`writeManifestPending` + `putWithObjectLock` + `transitionManifestStatus` in one Postgres tx) is removed in favour of a multi-step posture without tx wrapping. F-72 + F-82 re-score because the rollback contract becomes best-effort instead of structural.
5. The two-layer hard-delete (lifecycle policy + explicit pass) is reduced to one layer. F-74 + F-75 re-score because the defense-in-depth backstop is removed.
6. A second backup destination is added (e.g., off-Supabase to an external Canadian bucket for "ransomware insurance"). Cross-border verification reactivates per Hard Rule #4; ADR-0010 single-subprocessor posture is re-opened; F-73 + F-84 re-score under a new trust boundary.
7. The closed `BACKUP_TABLES` allowlist is opened to caller-supplied table-list (e.g., a "partial-dump for testing" config field is added). F-70 + F-84 re-score; the partial-dump posture would also require a separate manifest schema variant to track which tables were in vs out.
8. Restore-as-superuser is changed to a non-superuser path (e.g., a "restore via Edge Function with RLS-aware logic" model). New surface for restore-side RLS enforcement; B8 boundary changes shape; new finding for "restore-as-non-superuser correctness."
9. T17.1 introduces a backup-completion dependency in the T16 sweep (forbidden by ADR-0018 Decision §13). The CI no-import test catches this; if disabled, ADR-0017 + ADR-0018 both re-open.
