Aborted manifests excluded from the assertion.                                                                                                                     | `apps/web/test/T17/ra2-anchor-preservation.test.ts`                                                       | T17 (library + snapshot); T17.1 pgTAP column existence; T18 join DEFERRED |
| F-84  | `tsc --noEmit` against `apps/web/test/T17/fixtures/poisoned-config.ts` attempting to construct `BackupPassConfig` with `lock_duration_ms`, `object_ref`, `table_list` — each fails compile. Runtime: `runBackupPass` computes `lock_until_ms` via `nowMs + BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS * MS_PER_DAY` exclusively (intercept via `__debugListPutCalls`).                                                       | `apps/web/test/T17/no-caller-supplied-config.test.ts` (+ `apps/web/test/T17/fixtures/poisoned-config.ts`) | T17 (library); SQL signature DEFERRED to T17.1                            |
| F-85  | `.test-d.ts` `keyof BackupStore` does NOT include any string starting with `__debug`. `TestBackupStore extends BackupStore` adds them. `apps/web/src/lib/backup/index.ts` re-exports do NOT include `MemoryBackupStore`, `TestBackupStore`, `__debug*`, `__assertBackupTableExhaustive`.                                                                                                                  | `apps/web/test/T17/test-store-split.test-d.ts` + `apps/web/test/T17/index-surface.test.ts`                | T17 (library)                                                             |

##### Five cross-cutting properties the suite MUST establish (load-bearing)

(a) **No caller-supplied `object_ref` / `table_list` / `lock_duration_ms` compiles.** Static (TypeScript) assertion lives in F-84; the test suite includes a `tsc --noEmit` invocation against `apps/web/test/T17/fixtures/poisoned-config.ts` that attempts to construct `BackupPassConfig` with each of the three forbidden fields and asserts the compile fails with an `excess property` error. The ESLint rule `no-spread-into-backup-tables` is exercised by a poisoned fixture file (CI-only directory) that is asserted to fail lint.

(b) **Closed-allowlist drift fails CI.** F-70's set-equality + frozen-ness + §PI inventory pinning assertions plus a "scrub-and-restore" fixture that temporarily removes one entry from `BACKUP_TABLES` (via mutation of a deep-cloned copy fed through a test-only injection point) and asserts the drift test fails. Adding a non-existent table name to a deep-cloned copy and asserting the drift test fails. ESLint rule `no-spread-into-backup-tables` fires on a poisoned fixture.

(c) **Manifest 'pending' precedes 'committed' precedes audit-row write order (F-72 variant).** The test asserts the order by reading `__debugListManifests()` and `__debugListAuditRows()` after a clean pass: the manifest's state-transition timestamps go `pending → committed`, and the `backup.manifest_written` audit row's `ts_ms` is strictly greater than the manifest's `committed_at_ms` (which is greater than `started_at_ms`). T17.1's pgTAP suite re-asserts the property at the SQL boundary by wrapping steps 7–9 in a single Postgres tx and asserting the tx commits atomically.

(d) **F-83 head-pointer field is present and structurally typed.** Every committed manifest in a fixture suite of 10 passes carries `audit_log_head: {id, ts_ms, hash}` (or null on empty chain), `per_event_row_counts: Record<string, number>` (or {}), `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms: number` (non-zero). The three field names are snapshot-pinned — a future rename ("let's call it `chain_head`") fails the snapshot test in CI before merge. T18's reconciliation join inherits this contract via G-T17-RA2-ANCHOR-CONSUMER.

(e) **Hard-delete refusal pre-window returns structured `still_locked` rejection.** F-75's harness-forced state (manifest at -45d but lock_until_ms in the future) → `deleteObjectIfUnlocked` returns `{deleted: false, reason: 'still_locked'}` AND `result.would_fire_alert === 'A-BACKUP-001'`. The library returns the alert symbol; the alert sink is wired in T17.1 + observability-setup. This is the structural defense against early-release lifecycle misconfiguration AND adversarial bucket-policy mutation; the test pins the refusal at the library boundary.

##### Handoff envelope

- **To test-writer:** ADR-0018 §12 originally listed F-70..F-85 as placeholders; this §3.10 ratifies the F-### range AS-IS (no renumbering needed — F-70..F-85 are sequential after §3.9's F-55..F-69 and have no collision in this file). ADR-0018's threat-model cross-reference section (Follow-ups bullet 4) is updated below the table to confirm F-70..F-85 are final. All sixteen tests are mandatory for T17's four-way reviewer pass clearance; eight carry `[T17.1 deferred]` tags whose tests land later but whose acceptance criteria are recorded now: F-70 (cross-mirror SQL drift), F-71 (bucket policy), F-72 (single-tx wrapper), F-74 (lifecycle policy backstop), F-75 (A-BACKUP-001 sink), F-76 (SQL `xact_start()` ordering), F-79 + F-80 (pgTAP column assertions), F-83 (T18 integrity-job consumer).
- **To security-reviewer:** at diff time on T17 PR, verify F-70 (drift CI + ESLint), F-71 (object-lock cooperative-caller defense), F-72 (F-24 inversion state machine), F-79 (pseudonym top-level only), F-80 (manifest no pseudonyms), F-81 (no PII in errors), F-82 (no false completion), F-83 (RA-2 anchor preservation — load-bearing — confirm the snapshot-pin test fires on rename), F-84 (no caller-supplied config — confirm `tsc --noEmit` fixture test), F-85 (TestStore type split). At diff time on T17.1 PR (deferred), verify G-T17-1 advisory lock, G-T17-3 SECURITY DEFINER signatures, G-T17-4 cross-mirror drift, G-T17-5 object-lock duration mirror, G-T17-6 enum extension dance, G-T17-BUCKET-POLICY-RATIFY.
- **To privacy-reviewer:** PI inventory for `backup_manifests` (no PI; structural metadata only — `run_id`, `sha256`, kid, counts, head-pointer tuple, snapshot timestamps, schedule_hash, node_runtime_pin; no pseudonyms, no target_ids of PI records) lands in T17.1 per G-T17-7. ADR-0018 §Compliance check confirms PIPEDA Principle 4.5 + 4.7 + 4.8 alignment; HG-10 NOT firing is defensible (architect ask #6 verdict above; PIPEDA Principle 4.8 preserved via privacy-policy + audit-log paths). Cross-border transfers: NONE introduced by this surface (architect ask #7 verdict; library exposes `cross_region_destination_refused` structured rejection; T17.1 ratifies the `ca-central-1` bucket region; ADR-0001 invariant preserved). Subprocessor posture: ADR-0010 preserved (architect ask #8 verdict; no KMS, no external signer, no third-party bucket).
- **To user (human-gate items):**
  - **HG-15 (re-fires at T17.1 PR submission)** for the new physical table `backup_manifests` AND the new Supabase Storage bucket `backups-ca-central-1` with object-lock policy. Recorded in ADR-0018 §Compliance check + sibling task spec #15.
  - **HG-10 explicitly NOT firing** in this pass (architect ask #6 verdict above; ADR-0018 §Compliance check; T17 ships zero user-facing copy).
  - **HG-9 (retention schedule) ratified 2026-05-22** for ADR-0012 amendment; NOT re-firing in this pass.
  - **No new HG fires in T17 itself.**

---

### 3.11 Audit-log integrity (T18 library + T18.1 SQL)

Source: ADR-0019 (T18 audit-log integrity library + MemoryIntegrityStore), 2026-05-23. Closes RA-2 compensating control #3 ("the T18 chain-integrity job runs at least daily and on every key rotation and every export") by making the witness's detection algorithm operationally testable: the two detection surfaces — chain-walk (in-place mutation) and backup-diff (pivot-rewrite) — are both pinned at the library boundary, and the reconciliation rule that distinguishes attributed sweep-driven divergence from unattributed tamper-driven divergence is the structural separator between an A-INTEGRITY-002 false-positive flood and a silently-swallowed tamper. This sub-section scores F-86..F-100 as the authoritative T18 surface. The §3.10 carry-forward `G-T17-RA2-ANCHOR-CONSUMER` is closed library-side here (T18 reads `manifest.audit_log_head`, `manifest.per_event_row_counts`, `manifest.retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms` per the snapshot-pinned contract).

**Scope split:** F-86..F-100 are scored as a family. Library-scope assertions land in T18 (CI tests against `MemoryIntegrityStore`). SQL-scope and infrastructure-scope assertions land in T18.1 (pgTAP, `SupabaseIntegrityStore`, `integrity_check_runs` table + migration, optional `audit_chain_anchors` table, pg_cron 04:30 ET daily + Mon 00:00 ET weekly, Edge Function `post_rotation` + `post_export` trigger surface, `pg_advisory_xact_lock` coordination with backup pass, A-AUDIT-001 / A-INTEGRITY-001 / A-INTEGRITY-002 alert wiring, off-app weekly anchor email delivery to worker co-chair). Each row tags `[T18]` or `[T18.1 deferred]` for the test-writer. **HG-10 explicitly does NOT fire** (zero user-facing copy — operator-facing alerts only; verdict below). **HG-15 fires at T18.1 PR submission** (new physical `integrity_check_runs` table + optional `audit_chain_anchors` table; ADR-0019 §Sibling task spec). **HG-9 does NOT re-fire** — the three new audit-log enum values ride the standard ADR-0003 Amendment A extension dance.

#### Trust boundaries this introduces

- **B6.2 — `integrity_check_role` boundary (added here; activates at T18.1; library shape preserved in T18).** A non-login `integrity_check_role` in T18.1 holds `GRANT EXECUTE` on the `SECURITY DEFINER` integrity-check functions (`integrity_check_walk_audit_chain_segment`, `integrity_check_read_latest_backup_manifest`, `integrity_check_list_sweep_runs_through`, `integrity_check_read_chain_rows_by_ids`, `integrity_check_emit_run_and_mismatches`, `integrity_check_emit_chain_anchor_weekly`, `integrity_check_has_open_run_within_window`, `integrity_check_record_run_started`, `integrity_check_extract_chain_head`). It is a SIBLING role to `retention_service_role` (B6, T16.1), `backup_writer_role` (B6.1, T17.1), and `audit_writer_role` — NOT an expansion of any. It has NO `BYPASSRLS`; SELECT-only on `audit_log` + `retention_sweep_runs` + `backup_manifests`; INSERT only via the dedicated `integrity_check_emit_*` SECURITY DEFINER functions whose bodies hard-code the closed event-type allowlist (`audit.integrity_check.ran`, `audit.integrity_check.mismatch`, `audit.chain_anchor.weekly`); no UPDATE; no DELETE (DELETE remains exclusively `retention_service_role` aged-row path). The function bodies hard-code the trigger discriminator (closed allowlist); no caller-supplied predicate / WHERE / pivot / row-range / runtime_pin path. The library half (T18) mirrors this at the type level: `IntegrityStore` forbids caller-supplied `predicate`, `where`, `pivot`, `row_range`, `start_id`, `end_id`, `table_name`, `backup_manifest_id`, `runtime_pin`; the only configurable surface is `dry_run` + `lease_window_ms`. Treat B6.2 as "type-level in T18, role-level in T18.1." Reference: ADR-0019 Decision §3 + §5 + §6 + §11; sibling task spec items #1, #2, #4, #12.
- **Diagram note (consolidated diagram, §1 of this file).** B6.2 sits inside the Supabase-cloud box adjacent to B6 (`retention_service_role`) and B6.1 (`backup_writer_role`) and the existing `audit_writer_role`. Edge flow: pg_cron daily 04:30 ET → `integrity_check_role` SECURITY DEFINER `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})` wrapper → (1) lease check, (2) record run row in `running` state, (3) read latest committed backup manifest, (4) runtime-pin coherence check, (5) chain walk in 1000-row batches up to 20000 row cap, (6) backup-diff for rows older than `manifest.committed_at_ms - 1h`, (7) reconciliation walker per Option G binding rule, (8) emit each mismatch audit row BEFORE alert fan-out (F-87), (9) emit `audit.integrity_check.ran` summary row LAST in tx (F-88), (10) state machine terminal transition. Separate pg_cron weekly Mon 00:00 ET drives `runWeeklyChainAnchor` → emit `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` row → T18.1 Edge Function reads and sends off-app email to worker co-chair (manual backstop, NOT a control). Edge Function `post_rotation` + `post_export` paths fire `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'post_rotation'|'post_export'})` within the 5-min upper bound per F-50. When the diagram is next refreshed, add a B6.2 box adjacent to B6 + B6.1; show pg_cron 04:30 ET + Mon 00:00 ET edges; show Edge Function trigger edges from rotation + export pipelines.

#### Data flows (T18 library shape; T18.1 SQL shape mirrors)

```
[Integrity check pass — per ADR-0019 §5 algorithm]
  Caller (CI test in T18; pg_cron 04:30 ET + Edge Functions post_rotation / post_export in T18.1)
    -> runIntegrityCheck({store, config: {trigger}})
       1. store.hasOpenIntegrityRunWithinWindow(nowMs, INTEGRITY_DEFAULT_LEASE_WINDOW_MS = 5min)
            if true -> return {status: 'skipped', reason: 'pass_already_in_window'}
            (F-59 lease pattern; T18.1 SQL half is pg_advisory_xact_lock SHARED with backup
             per Option F; key hashtext('audit_chain_global'); G-T16-1 mirror)
       2. run_id = generateRunId() with 'ic_' prefix (G-T16-PRIV-3 PII-shape rejection)
       3. store.recordIntegrityRunStarted({run_id, trigger, started_at_ms: nowMs})
            // F-72 state machine: status='running' BEFORE any chain walk
            // If throws -> return {status: 'errored', error_code: 'run_start_failed'}
       4. snapshotToken = store.snapshot()             // F-58 rollback hook
       5. manifest = await store.readLatestCommittedBackupManifest()
            // G-T17-RA2-ANCHOR-CONSUMER; snapshot-pinned three-field consumer:
            //   manifest.audit_log_head, manifest.per_event_row_counts,
            //   manifest.retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms
            // If null (Phase-0 / no committed manifest): backup-diff SKIPPED; chain-walk proceeds
       6. if manifest !== null:
            livePin = store.readNodeRuntimePin()        // G-T11-23 hash-determinism pin
            if livePin.node_version !== manifest.node_runtime_pin.node_version
               OR livePin.openssl_version !== manifest.node_runtime_pin.openssl_version:
              store.restore(snapshotToken)
              return {status: 'errored', error_code: 'runtime_pin_mismatch'}
              // OPERATIONAL error, NOT A-AUDIT-001 (false-positive prevention; F-93)
       7. // Chain walk (primary detection surface)
          for batch in walkAuditChainSegment({batch_size: 1000, start_after_id: cursor}):
            for row in batch:
              expected_hash = BLAKE2b-256(canonical_json(row + row.prev_hash))
              if expected_hash !== row.hash: push chain_walk mismatch (F-89)
              if row.prev_hash !== BLAKE2b-256(prev_row.hash): push chain_walk mismatch (F-89)
              if row.id !== prev_row.id + 1 AND gap NOT attributable to a sweep:
                push chain_walk gap mismatch (F-90)
              if rows_walked >= 20000: break with status='capped' + resume_after_id (F-99)
       8. // Backup-diff (RA-2 trigger #3 detection surface; only if manifest != null)
          if manifest !== null AND manifest.audit_log_head !== null:
            cutoff_ts_ms = manifest.committed_at_ms - INTEGRITY_BACKUP_DIFF_BUFFER_MS (1h)
            for dump_row in manifest.id_range where dump_row.ts < cutoff_ts_ms:
              live_row = await store.readChainRowsByIds([dump_row.id])
              if live_row present AND (live.hash !== dump.hash OR live.prev_hash !== dump.prev_hash):
                push backup_diff mismatch (F-91; pivot-rewrite detection)
              if live_row absent:
                apply reconciliation (step 9)
              // Rows newer than cutoff are NOT walked (no false-positive on post-dump inserts)
       9. // Reconciliation (Option G binding rule; F-92)
          for absent_row in absent_from_live_but_in_dump:
            sweeps = await store.listRetentionSweepRunsThrough(manifest.retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms)
            for sweep in sweeps where sweep.started_at_ms <= absent_row.ts <= sweep.completed_at_ms
                                  AND sweep.per_event_counts[absent_row.event_type] > 0:
              greedy-attribute; decrement sweep's per_event_counts budget
            if no eligible sweep:
              push UNATTRIBUTABLE mismatch (F-92; A-AUDIT-001 AND A-INTEGRITY-002 both fire)
            // per_event_counts[k] missing key treated as 0 (G-T17-9)
            // never reads per_event_counts['__ceiling__'] (G-T16-RECONCILE-CEILING)
      10. // State machine terminal + emission (F-87 + F-88 + F-72)
          await store.emitIntegrityCheckRunAndMismatches({
            run: {...started, terminal_status, completed_at_ms},
            mismatches: mismatch_rows,                  // F-87: each written BEFORE ran row
            ran_row: ran_row                            // F-88: LAST write in tx (omitted if errored)
          })
          // If emit throws -> store.restore(snapshotToken) -> errored / audit_emit_failed
          // (G-T11-29 lesson: no stub success; mismatches re-detected on next pass)
      11. // Build IntegrityRunResult (closed discriminated union)
          return one of:
            { status: 'completed', run_id, ..., would_fire_alert?: 'A-AUDIT-001' |
              readonly ('A-AUDIT-001' | 'A-INTEGRITY-002')[] }
            { status: 'capped', run_id, ..., truncated_to_row_cap: true, resume_after_id }
            { status: 'errored', run_id, error_code: 'run_start_failed' |
              'runtime_pin_mismatch' | 'chain_walk_failed' | 'backup_diff_failed' |
              'audit_emit_failed' }
            { status: 'skipped', reason: 'pass_already_in_window' }
  Errors throughout: {run_id, status, error_code} only (F-100; G-T11-29 / G-T16-PRIV-3 mirror)

[Weekly chain anchor pass — per ADR-0019 §7 algorithm]
  Caller (CI test in T18; pg_cron Mon 00:00 ET in T18.1)
    -> runWeeklyChainAnchor({store})
       1. head = highest-id row from walkAuditChainSegment({start_after_id: null, max_rows: Infinity})
            if empty chain -> return {status: 'skipped', reason: 'empty_chain'}
       2. await store.emitChainAnchorWeekly({event_type: 'audit.chain_anchor.weekly', ...,
            meta: {anchor_at_ms: nowMs, head: {id, ts_ms, hash}}})
       3. return {status: 'completed', anchor_at_ms, head}
  // Off-app email delivery is OUT OF LIBRARY SCOPE; T18.1's Edge Function reads the row
  // and sends to worker co-chair's email-of-record. Manual backstop per RA-2 §4298;
  // absence does NOT re-open RA-2.
```

Classification per surface: `integrity_check_runs` (T18.1) carries NO PI (structural counts + run metadata only — `run_id`, `trigger`, `started_at_ms`, `completed_at_ms`, `status`, `rows_walked`, `mismatches_count`, `attributable_count`, `unattributable_count`, `backup_diff_performed`, `backup_manifest_run_id`, `resume_after_id`, `node_runtime_pin`, `schedule_hash`; mirrors `retention_sweep_runs`). Optional `audit_chain_anchors` (T18.1, implementer choice) carries NO PI (head-pointer triple + delivery timestamp only). The three new audit-log event-type rows: `audit.integrity_check.ran` carries `{run_id, trigger, started_at_ms, completed_at_ms, status, rows_walked, mismatches_count, attributable_count, unattributable_count, backup_diff_performed, backup_manifest_run_id, resume_after_id, node_runtime_pin, schedule_hash}` in `meta` with synthetic `HMAC('system:integrity-check')` actor_pseudonym at top level (mirrors `system:retention` / `system:backup-pass`); `audit.integrity_check.mismatch` carries `{run_id, detected_via, row_id (the audit_log.id of the mismatching row — structurally bigint, non-PII), expected_hash, actual_hash, prev_hash_match, attribution_attempted, backup_manifest_run_id?}` — explicitly NO `actor_pseudonym` of the mismatching row's actor, NO `target_id` of the mismatching row, NO `meta` excerpt of the mismatching row's content (G-T17-PRIV-7); `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` carries `{anchor_at_ms, head: {id, ts_ms, hash}}` only. Residency: ca-central-1 (no new processor; T18.1 reads `audit_log` + `retention_sweep_runs` + `backup_manifests` all in `ca-central-1`). Retention: `integrity_check_runs` rows = 24 months (operational telemetry; mirrors `retention_sweep_runs` recommended class); `audit.integrity_check.ran` audit rows = 24 months; `audit.integrity_check.mismatch` audit rows = 7 years (load-bearing forensic); `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` audit rows = 7 years (load-bearing forensic; off-app email anchor target).

| F-86  | F-55 / F-70 mirror — closed-allowlist drift                                                 | T (Tampering of code paths via mirror drift) + E (Elevation via missing/extra allowlist entry expanding the integrity-check event-type surface or dropping a required event)                                                                                        | `IntegrityCheckEventType` union vs `INTEGRITY_CHECK_EVENT_TYPES` frozen const; ADR-0019 Decision §2                                                                          | _"Library CI parses `INTEGRITY_CHECK_EVENT_TYPES` + asserts every value in the closed `IntegrityCheckEventType` union has exactly one allowlist entry; every allowlist entry is in the union; allowlist is `Object.isFrozen`. Removing the literal `'audit.integrity_check.mismatch'` from the const fails CI. Adding a fourth string not in the union fails CI. Every entry has a recommended retention class (`{kind:'fixed_months',months:24}` for ran; `{kind:'fixed_years',years:7}` for mismatch and weekly). Cross-mirror SQL drift (TS const vs SQL `audit_log.event_type` CHECK constraint widening to include the three new strings) deferred to T18.1 per ADR-0019 sibling task spec #13.                                                                          |
| F-87  | F-24 lineage — audit-before-alert-fanout                                                    | R (Repudiation — A-AUDIT-001 fires but no audit-row evidence exists) + I (Information disclosure of an alert with no forensic anchor)                                                                                                                               | Mismatch row written BEFORE alert symbol surfaces; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 10 + Option E                                                                                   | _"Every `audit.integrity_check.mismatch` row appears in `__debugListEmittedAuditRows()` BEFORE the `IntegrityRunResult.would_fire_alert` symbol is observable on the returned object. Test: `__debugCorruptHashAtId(50)` on a 100-row fixture; run integrity check; capture the emitted-rows list AND the result; assert at least one mismatch row exists in the emitted-rows list AND `result.would_fire_alert === 'A-AUDIT-001'`. Test: the emission order within the store is `[mismatch_row_1, ..., mismatch_row_N, ran_row]` (asserted via the store's append-order debug view). Test: a forced emit failure ON the ran row (NOT on a mismatch row) results in NO would_fire_alert on the returned errored result — the alert symbol depends on the full emission succeeding (F-88 coherence)."_                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | **Low** — F-24 invariant preserved as "mismatch rows precede the alert-symbol return value, which is the library's stand-in for the T18.1 alert fan-out."                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | T18-AUDIT-BEFORE-ALERT-1 (mismatch row visible before alert symbol), T18-AUDIT-BEFORE-ALERT-2 (emission order pinning).                                                                                                                                                                    | T18 (library). T18.1 (SECURITY DEFINER wrapper around `runIntegrityCheck` invokes the A-AUDIT-001 sink AFTER the SQL tx commits — the in-tx mismatch rows are durable before the sink fires; pgTAP asserts).                                                                |
| F-88  | F-58 lineage — summary LAST in tx                                                           | T (Tampering — partial-detection state surfaces if the ran row commits without its mismatch rows) + R (Repudiation — "the integrity check completed" claim is verifiable only when the full atomicity unit lands)                                                   | `audit.integrity_check.ran` summary row written LAST in the same transaction as mismatches + run-row terminal transition; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 10 + Option E + Option H | _"In a clean pass with 3 forced mismatches (`__debugCorruptHashAtId` x3), the order of writes in `__debugListEmittedAuditRows()` is exactly `[mismatch_1, mismatch_2, mismatch_3, ran]`. The `ran` row is the LAST audit row written in the integrity-check transaction. Test: force the emit to throw ON the ran row (`__debugForceEmitException('ran')`); assert NO audit rows are visible afterward (full rollback — the 3 mismatch rows that were queued for emission also do not surface); the run row's terminal status is NOT 'completed' (state machine reverted via `store.restore(snapshotToken)`); the IntegrityRunResult is `{status: 'errored', error_code: 'audit_emit_failed'}`; NO `would_fire_alert` symbol on the errored result. Test: on errored runs, the `audit.integrity_check.ran` row is NEVER emitted (absence is the signal that a pass was attempted but did not complete; mirrors T16 retention.deleted absence semantic)."_                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | **Low** — F-58 invariant preserved exactly: no integrity-check verdict without its audit row, no audit row without its underlying check. | F-91  | RA-2 trigger #3 anchor — **LOAD-BEARING**                                                   | T (Tampering — A5 pivot-rewrite attack: re-hash chain forward from a pivot point so chain-walk passes but the dump has the old hashes) + R (Repudiation — "the chain has always been this way" claim defeats chain-walk-alone witnesses)                            | Backup-diff detection surface; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 8 + ADR-0018 manifest schema; RA-2 follow-up §4297                                                                  | _"**Pivot-rewrite walk-through:** chain-walk alone CANNOT detect a pivot-rewrite — a chain that has been re-hashed forward from row K to the head is internally consistent (every prev_hash matches every preceding hash; every hash matches the canonical-JSON recompute of its row). The chain-walk says 'pass.' Only the backup-diff detects this attack, because the dump captured at `latest_dump_ts` contains row K's PRE-rewrite hash, which differs from the live chain's POST-rewrite hash at the same id. Test: seed 50 rows + insert a backup manifest fixture (`__debugInsertBackupManifestFixture`) whose `audit_log_head.hash` matches the seeded row 50; advance clock 1 hour so all 50 rows are eligible (live rows older than `manifest.committed_at_ms - 1h`); `__debugCorruptHashAtId(10)` (a row older than the 1h dump-buffer cutoff); `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})`. | F-92  | G-T16-8 anchor — Option G binding rule                                                      | T (Tampering — chain row deletion masked as legitimate sweep) + R (Repudiation — "we cannot tell sweep from tamper" attribution dispute) + I (Information disclosure — false-positive A-INTEGRITY-002 floods operator into alert fatigue)                           | Reconciliation walker per ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 9 + Option G; G-T16-8 carry-forward closed library-side; G-T17-9 zero-event-count convention                             | _"**Both directions pinned (load-bearing).** Direction 1 — attributed (legitimate sweep): seed 50 rows + insert a backup manifest fixture whose `audit_log_head` includes id 30 (event_type `concern.created`). Direction 3 — zero-event-count convention: a sweep_run whose `per_event_counts` is missing the key entirely (NOT zero-valued; literally absent) is treated as count=0; the absent row is unattributable. Direction 4 — greedy attribution budget: a sweep with `per_event_counts: {'concern.created': 1}` can attribute exactly 1 row of that event_type; if 2 rows are absent of the same event_type, the second is unattributable. The reconciliation rule is the structural separator between the false-positive flood case (A-INTEGRITY-002 fires on every legitimate sweep) and the silent-tamper case (sweep deletes hide tampers). Both directions must be pinned; a one-direction-only test would allow the inverse failure mode through. Test: with exactly 20000 rows, `status:'completed'` (boundary inclusive on the floor side; cap is the max, not the threshold). Test: `INTEGRITY_MAX_ROWS_PER_PASS` is a library constant (20000) and NOT a `IntegrityCheckRunConfig` field (covered jointly with F-97 type-test — no `max_rows` field on config). Test: a capped pass that detects mismatches in the first 20000 rows still emits those mismatches and surfaces the would_fire_alert (capped does NOT swallow detected mismatches). Test: a subsequent run after a capped pass (production T18.1's next-scheduled or next-triggered pass) walks the remaining rows naturally — the library does not accept a `resume_after_id` parameter as input (the SupabaseIntegrityStore picks up from the highest-id row already walked via in-SQL cursor management; the library mirror is implementation-defined and the test asserts the production semantic against the in-memory mirror)."_                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | **Low** — defense for two scenarios (future scale + pathological row); both pinned.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | T18-ROW-CAP-1 (20001 → capped + resume_after_id), T18-ROW-CAP-2 (20000 boundary → completed), T18-ROW-CAP-3 (capped with mismatches still emits + alerts).                                                                                                                                 | T18 (library). T18.1 (`SupabaseIntegrityStore` cursor management; `statement_timeout 60s + lock_timeout 5s` operational-safety belt; pgTAP asserts).                                                                                                                        |
| F-100 | F-67 / F-81 mirror — closed-literal error_codes; no PII in errors                           | I (Information disclosure via error path leak of row content, row_id under a PII-bearing row's actor, event_type of a leaked row, or PI shape in the error message)                                                                                                 | Structured-error-not-PII per ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 11 + Decision drivers (G-T11-29 / G-T16-PRIV-3 / G-T17 F-81); closed literal `error_code` union                       | _"Force each of the four library error*codes: (a) `run_start_failed` via `__debugForceEmitException` on the started run row; (b) `runtime_pin_mismatch` via `__debugForceRuntimePinMismatch(true)`; (c) `chain_walk_failed` via `__debugForceChainWalkException(true)`; (d) `audit_emit_failed` via `__debugForceEmitException` on the terminal emit. For each, assert the returned result is exactly `{status:'errored', run_id, error_code: <closed literal>}` — no additional fields. Assert each error carries: NO `row_id` of a PI-bearing row (the only `row_id` that may appear is in the mismatch ROW's meta, NOT in the error result); NO `event_type` of any audit_log row; NO `actor_pseudonym` of any user (only the system pseudonym ever appears, and only on emitted rows, not on error results); NO hex longer than 64 chars; NO UUID other than `run_id` (which uses the `ic*`prefix to break 32-hex word boundary per G-T16-PRIV-3 rejection-sample); NO`_\_ct`field name; NO email shape; NO phone shape. The`error_code` is a closed literal union (`'run_start_failed'                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | 'runtime_pin_mismatch'                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | 'chain_walk_failed'                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | 'backup_diff_failed'                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | 'audit_emit_failed' | 'head_read_failed' | 'lease_check_failed'`; the trailing two added in the M8.B in-cycle Findings 1 + 5 fix, ratified by ADR-0019 Amendment A.2 — 2026-06-14) — a future addition requires a typed union extension + a test obligation update; runtime tests assert the result.error_code matches one of the seven exact literals. Same property for `runWeeklyChainAnchor`: forced errors carry `{status:'errored', error_code:'head_read_failed' | 'audit_emit_failed'}` only — no head triple, no row excerpt, no PI shapes."\* | **Low**     | T18-NO-PII-ERRORS-1 (four force-error paths in runIntegrityCheck), T18-NO-PII-ERRORS-2 (two force-error paths in runWeeklyChainAnchor), T18-NO-PII-ERRORS-3 (error_code closed-literal union enumeration). | T18 (library).                                                  |

#### Architect ask #1 verdict — F-91 is LOAD-BEARING for RA-2 trigger #3

The pivot-rewrite attack signature is the load-bearing reason for the backup-diff detection surface. A platform admin (A5) with `audit_writer_role` credentials can: (a) select a pivot id K in the live chain; (b) compute new BLAKE2b-256 hashes for every row from K through head, walking forward and re-linking each row's `hash` and the next row's `prev_hash`; (c) write the new hashes back. The resulting chain is INTERNALLY CONSISTENT — every prev_hash matches the preceding hash; every hash matches the canonical-JSON recompute of its row's content. **Chain-walk says "pass."** The only operational detection surface is the dump captured at `latest_dump_ts`, which contains the PRE-rewrite hashes for rows in `[K, head_at_dump_time]`. The backup-diff compares the live row's hash against the dump's hash at the same id — for any row in `[K, head_at_dump_time]`, the comparison fails, and A-AUDIT-001 fires with `meta.detected_via:'backup_diff'`.

This is why F-91 carries the "if it breaks, RA-2 re-opens by construction" tag. The chain-walk surface (F-89) catches naive in-place mutation (single-row hash corruption that breaks prev_hash linkage on the NEXT row); the backup-diff surface (F-91) catches the sophisticated pivot-rewrite that defeats chain-walk. RA-2 compensating control #3 requires BOTH surfaces operational because the threat model includes a sophisticated A5 adversary. Removing or degrading F-91 silently demotes the chain-integrity job from "two-surface witness" to "chain-walk only" — which means the pivot-rewrite class of attacks becomes invisible. The first such attack post-T18 deployment would, when eventually surfaced via some other means (off-app weekly anchor disagreement; restore drill divergence; external audit), trigger RA-2 trigger #3 with no operational pre-cursor — meaning the compensating control was on paper only.

**Verdict:** F-91 is LOAD-BEARING. The test obligation is the structural seal; the "if this test breaks, RA-2 re-opens" clause in the F-### row is not rhetorical — it is the literal failure mode. Score Low residual at the library boundary; the load-bearing nature is reflected in the test being non-negotiable for T18 ship.

#### Architect ask #2 verdict — F-92 attribution rule pinnable in BOTH directions

The reconciliation walker has TWO failure modes that are inverse of each other:

- **False-positive flood (over-attribution failure):** the walker mis-attributes a tamper-deletion to a legitimate sweep run (a sweep_run with the wrong event_type or wrong window is accepted as eligible). Result: a tamper goes undetected; A-AUDIT-001 does NOT fire when it should. Silent-tamper case.
- **False-positive flood (under-attribution failure):** the walker mis-rejects a legitimate sweep-deletion as unattributable (a sweep_run that DID account for the deletion is mis-classified as ineligible). Result: A-AUDIT-001 + A-INTEGRITY-002 fire on every legitimate retention sweep; the operator is buried in noise; real fires get missed in the alert-fatigue spiral.

The two failure modes have opposite test signatures, which is why the architect's rule says both directions MUST be pinned. F-92 directions 1 and 2 cover the two; directions 3, 4, 5 cover the structural sub-properties that the attribution rule's correctness depends on:

- Direction 3 (zero-event-count convention; G-T17-9): the library's read of `per_event_counts[event_type]` MUST treat missing keys as 0, not undefined. A typo-bug that returns `undefined` would silently fail the eligibility comparison (undefined > 0 evaluates to false in JS, so the attribution would be rejected — fine in this direction — but undefined === 0 evaluates to false too, so a future code change that compared `=== 0` instead of `> 0` would have inverse semantics). Pin the read semantic.
- Direction 4 (greedy attribution budget): the walker decrements the per_event_counts budget as it attributes rows. A non-decrementing implementation would let one sweep account for unbounded deletions of the same event_type; a tamper of N rows of the same event_type would all be absorbed by a sweep that only deleted 1. Pin the decrement.
- Direction 5 (`__ceiling__` rejection): the wire never carries the `__ceiling__` aggregate key (G-T16-RECONCILE-CEILING). A defensive library that read `per_event_counts['__ceiling__']` as a fallback would let an attacker inject a synthetic ceiling key to absorb all attribution. Pin the structural absence.

**Both directions pinnable; verdict: pinning the rule is the structural separator between the two failure modes.** A test suite that only pins direction 1 lets the under-attribution failure mode through (alert fatigue → real fires missed); a suite that only pins direction 2 lets the over-attribution failure mode through (silent tamper). The architect's rule "for each row in dump but absent from live, attribute IFF (event_type in some sweep_run.per_event_counts with count > 0 AND row.ts within that run's window). Unattributable → A-AUDIT-001 + A-INTEGRITY-002 fire DISTINCTLY (different causes)" is verified across all five directions.

#### Architect ask #3 verdict — F-88 is F-58 mirror; the invariant holds

F-58 (T16 retention sweep) reads: "the `retention.deleted` summary row is the LAST write inside a transaction whose deletes have already executed." F-88 (T18 integrity check) reads: "the `audit.integrity_check.ran` summary row is the LAST audit row written in the integrity-check transaction." Same shape: summary-LAST as the audit anchor for the side-effect (deletes / mismatch-detection); rollback contract on summary failure (the whole tx unwinds including the side-effect / detection state).

Walking the invariant against the integrity check:

- **Clean pass:** mismatches are accumulated in-memory during chain-walk + backup-diff + reconciliation; the run row is recorded in `running` state at step 3; the snapshot is taken at step 4; at step 10, the store atomically writes all mismatch audit rows BEFORE the ran row, transitions the run row to its terminal state, and writes the ran row LAST. The ran row's presence is the verifiable claim that the check completed; its content (`mismatches_count`, `attributable_count`, `unattributable_count`) is the verifiable summary.
- **Emit failure on the ran row (step 10 throws):** the store's tx rolls back (T18.1 single-tx wrapper makes this structural; T18 library's `MemoryIntegrityStore` models the rollback via `store.restore(snapshotToken)`). The mismatch rows that were queued for emission do NOT surface. The run row's terminal state does NOT transition (stays in `running`, which the next pass's lease check will surface as a stale state). The IntegrityRunResult is `{status:'errored', error_code:'audit_emit_failed'}`. **No partial detection state surfaces.** No `would_fire_alert` on the errored result (alert firing depends on full emission success).
- **Emit failure on a mismatch row (step 10 partial throw):** same rollback semantic. No mismatch rows surface; no ran row written; errored result; no alert. The mismatches will be re-detected on the next pass from the unchanged chain state (G-T11-29 lesson: stub side-effects do NOT silently succeed; the next pass is the recovery path, not the swallow path).

**Verdict:** F-88 preserves F-58 exactly. The invariant "no integrity-check verdict without its audit row, no audit row without its underlying check" holds. The test obligation T18-SUMMARY-LAST-2 (force-throw on ran-row emit → full rollback) is the structural seal.

#### Architect ask #4 verdict — F-87 vs F-88 are not contradictory

F-87 says the MISMATCH ROW is written BEFORE the alert fan-out (F-24 inversion: audit row precedes the alert claim). F-88 says the RAN-SUMMARY row is written LAST in the transaction (F-58 mirror: summary follows the side-effect). These are two DIFFERENT audit rows being written in two DIFFERENT positions of the transaction.

The transaction's write order is:

```
INSERT mismatch_row_1
INSERT mismatch_row_2
...
INSERT mismatch_row_N
UPDATE integrity_check_runs SET terminal_status=..., completed_at_ms=...
INSERT ran_row                                     <-- LAST
COMMIT
                                                   <-- after commit:
                                                       return IntegrityRunResult with would_fire_alert
                                                   <-- after return:
                                                       T18.1 sink fires A-AUDIT-001 / A-INTEGRITY-002
```

- **F-87 invariant:** the mismatch ROWS precede the alert symbol on the returned result (which is what fires the T18.1 sink). Within the tx, mismatch rows write FIRST among the audit rows for that pass; the ran row writes LAST. The alert symbol surfaces only after COMMIT.
- **F-88 invariant:** the ran SUMMARY row writes LAST in the tx — its presence is the "I completed and here's my verdict" claim. The summary's content references the mismatches the tx contains.
- **Coherence:** the mismatch rows are the per-detection forensic anchors; the ran row is the per-pass operational anchor. Both are written within the same atomicity unit (single Postgres tx in T18.1; single `emitIntegrityCheckRunAndMismatches` call in T18 library); either all of them land or none of them do. The order WITHIN the tx (mismatches first, ran last) is the F-87 + F-88 joint property.

**Verdict:** F-87 and F-88 are COHERENT, not contradictory. F-87 distinguishes the mismatch rows (which precede the alert symbol surfacing) from the ran row (which lands last). F-88 distinguishes the ran row as the LAST write in the tx atomicity unit. The two pin orthogonal properties of the same single-tx state machine.

#### Architect ask #5 verdict — F-93 runtime-pin coherence is OPERATIONAL, NOT A-AUDIT-001

A Node 21.5.0 → 21.6.0 patch upgrade, or a Node 21 → 22 major upgrade, can silently change the byte-output of `BLAKE2b-256(canonical_json(...))` if the underlying OpenSSL library changes its primitive output (rare in practice but possible across major version bumps; canonical-JSON serialization is also a potential variation point if the canonicalizer's number serialization changes). If the live runtime's `(node_version, openssl_version)` differs from the manifest's `node_runtime_pin`, the chain-walk recompute would produce different hashes than the stored ones — generating SPURIOUS A-AUDIT-001 fires across EVERY production pass post-upgrade. Alert fatigue → real fires missed.

The fix is the runtime-pin coherence check at step 6 of the algorithm (BEFORE the chain walk runs): read the live runtime pin; compare against the manifest's; if they differ, return `{status:'errored', error_code:'runtime_pin_mismatch'}` AND emit NO mismatch rows AND fire NO A-AUDIT-001. The error is the signal to the operator that a toolchain upgrade has landed and the integrity-check pass needs a coordinated re-baselining (a new manifest taken under the new runtime pin; the next pass under the new pin will pass cleanly because the recompute matches the stored hashes by construction within a single runtime).

T18.1's observability sink routes `runtime_pin_mismatch` to A-INTEGRITY-001-variant (operational error class) — distinct from A-AUDIT-001 (chain-tamper class). The operator's response is: (a) verify the toolchain upgrade is legitimate (deployment log); (b) take a new backup under the new runtime; (c) re-run the integrity check; (d) confirm clean pass. Adversarial upgrade (an attacker rolling the toolchain to mask a tamper) would surface as A-INTEGRITY-001-variant → operator deployment-log check → upgrade unaccounted for → escalate. The operational-vs-adversarial classification is the load-bearing distinction.

**Verdict:** F-93 routing `runtime_pin_mismatch` to OPERATIONAL (NOT A-AUDIT-001) is the correct call. The architect's rationale ("a node version bump that silently changes hash output would otherwise generate spurious alerts") is structurally correct. Confirmed.

#### Architect ask #6 verdict — F-95 A-AUDIT-001 vs A-INTEGRITY-002 distinct causes

The two alerts answer different operator questions:

- **A-AUDIT-001 — chain hash mismatch.** Fires on the FACT of a mismatch (chain_walk OR backup_diff). Operator question: "is the chain currently inconsistent with its prior state?" Forensic surface: the mismatch row's `(expected_hash, actual_hash, row_id, detected_via)`. Response: investigate the row at row_id; determine if the mismatch corresponds to a known operational event (toolchain upgrade w/o pin coherence — should have been caught by F-93; sweep w/o per_event_counts attribution — should have been caught by reconciliation; restore from backup — separate incident class) or an adversarial event.
- **A-INTEGRITY-002 — reconciliation walker found unattributable divergence.** Fires on the CAUSE classification failing — the dump has a row absent from the live chain, AND no sweep_run in the manifest's snapshot window accounts for that row's event_type within that row's ts. Operator question: "is the reconciliation cause-classifier itself functioning, or is there a sweep-bug?" Forensic surface: the mismatch row's `attribution_attempted: true` + `actual_hash: null` + the manifest's sweep snapshot. Response: investigate whether the sweep run's `per_event_counts` is correct (T16 retention surface) OR the divergence is adversarial (A5 deleted a row from the live chain without it appearing in any sweep_run).

The two alerts MAY fire together (unattributable backup-diff: A-AUDIT-001 fires on the fact of divergence; A-INTEGRITY-002 fires on the cause-classifier failing). The two alerts MAY fire independently (chain-walk-detected hash mismatch: A-AUDIT-001 alone — no reconciliation walker ran; or attributable backup-diff divergence: NEITHER fires — the cause classifier succeeded).

The architect's rule is structurally enforced by the library's `would_fire_alert` shape on the IntegrityRunResult: a single symbol for the chain-walk-only case (`'A-AUDIT-001'`), a readonly two-element array for the both-fire case (`readonly ['A-AUDIT-001', 'A-INTEGRITY-002']`), absent for the no-fire case. Conflating the two would either (a) over-route — both alerts fire on every chain-walk mismatch including operational events caught by reconciliation (alert fatigue); or (b) under-route — A-INTEGRITY-002 collapses into A-AUDIT-001 and the responder cannot distinguish sweep-bug from adversarial-tamper investigation paths.

**Verdict:** Distinct causes; distinct routing; confirmed. Score Low residual; the test obligation T18-ALERT-DISTINCT-1/2/3 (three scenarios pinned exactly) is the structural seal.

#### Architect ask #7 verdict — RA-2 compensating control #3 is STRENGTHENED by T18

Pre-T18, RA-2 compensating control #3 was narrative: "The T18 chain-integrity job runs at least daily and on every key rotation and every export (F-50)." The job's existence was committed (RA-2 §4296); the witness data was ratified by ADR-0017 (sweep runs) and ADR-0018 (backup manifests); the chain schema was ratified by observability/audit-log.md §2 (prev_hash-linear BLAKE2b-256). What was missing: the ALGORITHM that the chain-integrity job runs. Without it, "the job runs daily" is a deployment claim with no operational test of correctness; the job could be deployed but silently degrading (running the chain-walk but skipping the backup-diff; running the backup-diff but accepting any divergence as "attributed" without the reconciliation rule; emitting mismatch rows but never the alert symbol).

T18 strengthens the control by structurally pinning the algorithm:

- **Before T18:** chain-integrity-job = "code we'll write that does the right thing." Verification surface: deployment confirmation only.
- **After T18:** chain-integrity-job = a library with pinned test obligations covering chain-walk correctness (F-89), gap detection (F-90), backup-diff (F-91), reconciliation (F-92), runtime-pin coherence (F-93), alert distinct-cause routing (F-95), weekly anchor (F-96), and the cooperative-caller defenses (F-86, F-87, F-88, F-94, F-97, F-98, F-99, F-100). The library is the verifiable algorithm; the test obligations are the verifiable correctness; the T18.1 wire-up (pg_cron + Edge Functions) is the verifiable cadence.

The strengthening claim is verified by walking RA-2 compensating control #3 against the test obligations:

1. **"Runs daily":** F-99 (`status:'capped' → resume_after_id`) ensures a single pass terminates within the row-cap; T18.1's pg_cron at 04:30 ET schedules the daily run.
2. **"On every key rotation":** F-50 5-min upper bound is honoured by the library's `INTEGRITY_DEFAULT_LEASE_WINDOW_MS = 5min`; T18.1's Edge Function `post_rotation` fires within 5 min of `committee_data_key.rotation.completed`.
3. **"On every export":** F-50 5-min upper bound; T18.1's Edge Function `post_export` fires within 5 min of `export.generated`.
4. **"Chain-integrity":** F-89 + F-90 (chain-walk + gap detection); F-91 + F-92 (backup-diff + reconciliation); F-94 (no PII leak in the detection rows); F-93 (no false-positive on legitimate runtime upgrades); F-95 (distinct-cause alert routing).

**Verdict:** RA-2 compensating control #3 is STRENGTHENED by T18. No BLOCK from threat-modeler.

#### Architect ask #8 verdict — RA-2 trigger #3 NOT re-opened; no new RA-2 re-open triggers fire

Walking each of the four RA-2 re-open triggers against T18's design:

1. **Trigger #1 — Cryptographic algorithm withdrawal / external compulsion to sign.** T18 does NOT introduce an external signer (Ed25519 is bundled with v2 / RA-2 re-open trigger #1 default response per ADR-0019 Option A). The library stays on v1 prev_hash-linear BLAKE2b-256 chain shape. No new subprocessor; no KMS dependency. **Not fired.**
2. **Trigger #2 — A5 platform-admin chain modification surfaced without warning.** T18 is the operational TEST for this surface — F-91 (backup-diff) is the detection. T18's deployment STRENGTHENS the response (the detection floor is now operational); it does not CREATE the surface. The first such firing post-T18 would surface trigger #2 with full forensic context (the mismatch row carries `(expected_hash, actual_hash, detected_via:'backup_diff', backup_manifest_run_id)`). **Not fired by T18's deployment; trigger #2's response is now well-defined.**
3. **Trigger #3 — Any divergence between live chain and most recent pg_dump backup for a row older than the dump.** T18 ships the operational test of trigger #3 (F-91 + F-92). The first detected divergence post-T18 deployment fires trigger #3 with the reconciliation walker's output as evidence (attributed → no fire; unattributable → fire). T18's deployment does NOT create a divergence — it creates the detection surface. **Not fired by T18's deployment; trigger #3's detection is now operational.**
4. **Trigger #4 — Expansion of `audit_writer_role` reach.** T18 does NOT expand `audit_writer_role`. The new `integrity_check_role` is a sibling role; its INSERT path is bounded by the dedicated `integrity_check_emit_*` SECURITY DEFINER functions whose bodies hard-code the closed event-type allowlist. The three new audit-log event types extend the closed `AuditEventType` union via the ADR-0003 Amendment A extension dance (six-mirror coordination per G-T08-9 / G-T13-14 / G-T14-7 / ADR-0018 Option H). **Not fired.**

**Verdict:** None of the four re-open triggers fires. RA-2 trigger #3 is NOT re-opened by T18 — instead, the trigger is now structurally detectable, which is the strengthening claim of #7. Architect's claim validated.

#### Residual assessment (aggregate)

All fifteen findings score Low at the library boundary (T18). Seven carry a T18.1-deferred component that is required before the production wire-up clears: F-86 (cross-mirror SQL drift on `audit_log.event_type` CHECK constraint widening), F-87 (T18.1 SECURITY DEFINER wrapper invokes alert sinks after tx commit), F-88 (T18.1 single-tx wrapper across mismatches + run-row UPDATE + ran-row INSERT), F-94 (pgTAP JSONB structure assertions), F-95 (A-AUDIT-001 + A-INTEGRITY-001 + A-INTEGRITY-002 alert sinks; observability-setup next pass), F-96 (T18.1 Edge Function reads weekly anchor + sends operator email), F-99 (T18.1 `statement_timeout 60s + lock_timeout 5s` operational-safety belt). One — F-91 — is the LOAD-BEARING property for RA-2 trigger #3; its test obligation is non-negotiable. No finding is Critical or High at any horizon.

Aggregate posture: **Low residual** for the audit-log integrity family with the T18.1 deferred items tracked as carry-forwards. F-91 carries the additional "if it breaks, RA-2 re-opens by construction" tag (Architect ask #1 verdict). The RA-2 compensating control #3 transitions from "in plan" to "operational" upon T18 + T18.1 shipping (Architect ask #7 verdict).

#### Re-open triggers

This sub-section re-opens if any of the following:

1. The v1 prev_hash-linear chain shape is replaced with a Merkle anchor-per-batch posture (ADR-0019 Option A re-evaluation). Re-opens ADR-0018 (`audit_log_head` triple becomes a Merkle root quadruple) + this entry; F-89 + F-91 + F-96 re-score under the new chain shape; bundled with RA-2 re-open trigger #1 default response.
2. A new audit-log event type bound to integrity check is added without all six mirrors (TS const, SQL CHECK constraint widening, RETENTION_SCHEDULE row, audit_log_retention_schedule SQL row, audit-log.md §1 enum table, scripts/check-audit-enum-coverage.sh). The drift test (F-86) catches the TS half in CI; T18.1's cross-mirror SQL drift test catches the SQL half.
3. `INTEGRITY_BACKUP_DIFF_BUFFER_MS` (1h) is changed without coordinated update to RA-2 §4297 (or a new RA-2 amendment). Three-mirror coordination — fails CI on single-mirror update.
4. `INTEGRITY_DEFAULT_LEASE_WINDOW_MS` (5min) is changed without F-50 mirror update. Re-opens the triggered-detection-latency contract.
5. `INTEGRITY_MAX_ROWS_PER_PASS` (20000) is changed; F-99 re-score under the new cap.
6. The closed `IntegrityCheckTrigger` union is opened to caller-supplied predicates / pivots / row-ranges (e.g., "scope to id 100..200 for debug"). F-97 re-score; the cooperative-caller defense is removed; RA-2 trigger #3 reasoning re-evaluates.
7. The reconciliation rule (Option G) is changed (e.g., "any sweep with `per_event_counts > 0` is eligible regardless of window"). F-92 re-score; RA-2 trigger #3 attribution semantics change; bundled with re-opening of ADR-0017's per_event_counts contract.
8. The `pg_advisory_xact_lock` coordination in T18.1 is removed in favour of no-coordination posture. F-91 + F-92 re-score because the snapshot read may race the backup pass; the join surface becomes stale-tolerant in a way the test obligations did not pin.
9. T18.1 introduces a backup-completion dependency in the T16 sweep OR a sweep-completion dependency in the T17 backup OR a sweep-or-backup completion dependency in T18 itself (forbidden by ADR-0019 §Consequences). The CI no-import test catches; if disabled, ADR-0017 + ADR-0018 + ADR-0019 all re-open.
10. An external signer / KMS is introduced (Ed25519 + KMS bundled with the v2 chain). Re-opens ADR-0010 single-subprocessor posture + RA-2 re-open trigger #1.
11. The weekly off-app anchor email destination is changed from the worker co-chair's email-of-record to a platform-managed destination (e.g., a new "anchor-witness" subprocessor). Re-opens ADR-0010; F-96 re-score.

| G-T18-9                   | T18.1 A-AUDIT-001 (chain-walk + backup-diff mismatch) + A-INTEGRITY-001 (missed-cron) + A-INTEGRITY-002 (unattributable divergence) alert sinks; observability-setup next pass after T18.1.                                                                               | observability-setup                   | Alert sinks (Sentry)  |
| G-T18-10                  | T18.1 pg_cron 04:30 ET daily `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})` + pg_cron Mon 00:00 ET weekly `runWeeklyChainAnchor`.                                                                                                                                             | T18.1 implementer                     | SQL (pg_cron)         |
| G-T18-11                  | T18.1 Edge Function `post_rotation` (5-min upper bound from `committee_data_key.rotation.completed`) + `post_export` (5-min upper bound from `export.generated`); both call `runIntegrityCheck` via SECURITY DEFINER wrapper.                                             | T18.1 implementer                     | Edge Function         |

| G-T18-13                  | T18.1 ADR-0016 schedule rows for `integrity_check_runs` (24mo) and optional `audit_chain_anchors` (7y).                                                                                                                                                                   | T18.1 implementer                     | ADR-0016 + SQL        |

CI no-import test catches.                                                                           | T16 + T17 + T18 implementers          | TS import graph       |
| G-T18-RA2-PRE-SNAPSHOT    | T18 ships the LOAD-BEARING RA-2 trigger #3 pre-snapshot test: seed → backup-fixture → tamper row older than 1h → assert A-AUDIT-001 fires with `meta.detected_via:'backup_diff'`. Any future change to T18 that breaks this test re-opens RA-2 by construction.           | T18 test-writer + security-reviewer   | CI                    |

| F-96  | `runWeeklyChainAnchor({store})` with seeded 50 rows → one `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` row; `meta.head.{id,ts_ms,hash}` matches highest-id row. Empty chain → `{status:'skipped', reason:'empty_chain'}`; NO row emitted. `__debugForceChainWalkException(true)` → `{status:'errored', error_code:'head_read_failed'}`; NO row emitted. `meta.head` field-name snapshot-pinned (rename fails CI). `actor_pseudonym` HMAC of `'system:integrity-check'`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | `apps/web/test/T18/weekly-chain-anchor.test.ts`                                                                      | T18 (library; emission only); Edge Function email delivery DEFERRED to T18.1        |

Capped pass with mismatches in first 20000 still emits them + surfaces alert. `INTEGRITY_MAX_ROWS_PER_PASS` not exposed in `IntegrityCheckRunConfig` (covered jointly with F-97).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | `apps/web/test/T18/row-cap-resume.test.ts`                                                                           | T18 (library); production cursor management DEFERRED to T18.1                       |
| F-100 | Force each of four `runIntegrityCheck` error*codes (`run_start_failed`, `runtime_pin_mismatch`, `chain_walk_failed`, `audit_emit_failed`) AND two `runWeeklyChainAnchor` error_codes (`head_read_failed`, `audit_emit_failed`). Assert each error carries only `{status:'errored', run_id, error_code:<closed literal>}` — no row_id of PI-bearing row, no event_type, no actor_pseudonym, no hex >64 chars, no UUID other than `run_id` (with `ic*`prefix), no`\*\_ct`field name, no email/phone shape.`error_code` is a closed-literal union.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | `apps/web/test/T18/no-pii-in-errors.test.ts`                                                                         | T18 (library)                                                                       |

##### Five cross-cutting properties the suite MUST establish (load-bearing)

(a) **No caller-supplied predicate / pivot / WHERE compiles.** Static (TypeScript) assertion lives in F-97; the test suite includes a `tsc --noEmit` invocation against `apps/web/test/T18/fixtures/poisoned-config.ts` that attempts to construct `IntegrityCheckRunConfig` with each of the 11 forbidden fields and asserts the compile fails with an `excess property` error. The runtime defensive read (`config.<field>` is never accessed; only the typed fields) is pinned by a second assertion in the same test file: injecting `as any` extras has zero observable effect on `runIntegrityCheck` behaviour.

(b) **Closed-allowlist drift fails CI.** F-86's set-equality + frozen-ness + retention-class-coverage assertions plus a "scrub-and-restore" fixture that temporarily removes one entry from `INTEGRITY_CHECK_EVENT_TYPES` (via mutation of a deep-cloned copy fed through a test-only injection point) and asserts the drift test fails. Adding a non-existent event type to a deep-cloned copy and asserting the drift test fails. CI must reject any mirror update that lands a new event type without updating both the const AND the union AND the retention-class map AND the audit-emission builder.

(c) **Mismatch-row precedes alert-fanout (F-87).** The test asserts the order by reading `__debugListEmittedAuditRows()` and comparing against the `IntegrityRunResult.would_fire_alert` assertion: the mismatch row appears in the emitted-rows list BEFORE the test assertion on the alert symbol is made. The library's contract is that the emitted-rows list is visible synchronously after `runIntegrityCheck` returns; the alert symbol on the result is the library's stand-in for the T18.1 alert sink fan-out. T18.1's pgTAP suite re-asserts the property at the SQL boundary by wrapping mismatch INSERTs + alert sink invocation in a single SECURITY DEFINER tx, with the sink invocation outside the tx (the mismatch rows are durable before the sink fires).

(d) **Summary-LAST in tx (F-88).** The test asserts the order by reading `__debugListEmittedAuditRows()` after a clean pass with 3 forced mismatches: the order is exactly `[mismatch_1, mismatch_2, mismatch_3, ran]`. Force the emit to throw on the ran row; assert full rollback (NO audit rows visible afterward; the queued mismatch rows do not surface; the run row's terminal state did not transition). T18.1's pgTAP suite re-asserts at the SQL boundary by wrapping mismatch INSERTs + run-row UPDATE + ran-row INSERT in a single Postgres tx and asserting atomicity.

(e) **F-92 attribution rule pinnable in BOTH directions (load-bearing correctness property).** Direction 1 (attributed → no alert): assert NO `would_fire_alert` symbol AND mismatch row absent AND `attributable_count:1`. Direction 2 (unattributable → both alerts distinct): assert `would_fire_alert` contains BOTH `'A-AUDIT-001'` AND `'A-INTEGRITY-002'` AS DISTINCT SYMBOLS (set-equality on the readonly array) AND `unattributable_count:1` AND mismatch row `meta.attribution_attempted === true`. The two-direction pin is the structural separator between the false-positive flood (over-attribution) and the silent-tamper (under-attribution) failure modes; a one-direction test would let the inverse failure mode through.

##### Load-bearing RA-2 pre-snapshot test obligation

Per G-T18-RA2-PRE-SNAPSHOT carry-forward: the test fixture pre-snapshot of RA-2 trigger #3 firing is:

```
1. Seed audit_log fixture with 50 rows of varied event_types.
2. __debugInsertBackupManifestFixture({
     audit_log_head: { id: row_50.id, ts_ms: row_50.ts_ms, hash: row_50.hash },
     per_event_row_counts: <derived from seeded rows>,
     retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms: nowMs,
     committed_at_ms: nowMs,
     node_runtime_pin: <live pin>,
     ...
   })
3. __debugSetClock(nowMs + 1 * INTEGRITY_MS_PER_HOUR)  // advance past the 1h dump-buffer
4. __debugCorruptHashAtId(10)  // a row older than the buffer
5. result = runIntegrityCheck({trigger: 'scheduled'})
6. assert result.would_fire_alert === 'A-AUDIT-001'
7. mismatch = __debugListMismatches().find(m => m.meta.row_id === '10')
8. assert mismatch.meta.detected_via === 'backup_diff'
9. assert mismatch.meta.expected_hash === <row 10's dump hash>
10. assert mismatch.meta.actual_hash === <corrupted hash>
11. assert mismatch.meta.backup_manifest_run_id === <fixture.run_id>
```

This is the post-T18 operational test of RA-2 compensating control #3. **Any future change to T18 that breaks this test re-opens RA-2 by construction.** The test file: `apps/web/test/T18/backup-diff-mismatch.test.ts` (F-91 home).

##### Test-scope split (T18 library vs T18.1 SQL deferred)

**T18 library scope (mandatory for T18 ship; all 15 F-### tests):** F-86, F-87, F-88, F-89, F-90, F-91, F-92, F-93, F-94, F-95, F-96, F-97, F-98, F-99, F-100. All run against `MemoryIntegrityStore`; no Supabase local stack required; fast deterministic CI.

**T18.1 SQL scope (deferred; lands with sibling task):** G-T18-1 (advisory lock), G-T18-3 (SECURITY DEFINER signatures), G-T18-4 (cross-mirror SQL drift), G-T18-5 (single-tx wrapper), G-T18-6 (enum extension dance — six mirrors), G-T18-9 (A-AUDIT-001/A-INTEGRITY-001/A-INTEGRITY-002 alert sinks), G-T18-10 (pg_cron schedules), G-T18-11 (Edge Function trigger surface), G-T18-12 (off-app weekly anchor email Edge Function). pgTAP integration tests mirror F-86..F-100 + the audit-log.md §5 obligations.

##### Existing test scaffold rename (per ADR-0019 Decision §T18-12)

`apps/web/test/T18/audit-integrity.test.ts` exists as a pre-T18 scaffold that mixes T18 library scope and T18.1 SQL scope and contains an A-KEY-ROT-001 30s-window assertion that conflicts with F-50's 5-min upper bound. **Rename to** `apps/web/test/T18/audit-integrity.t18-1-deferred.test.ts` (consistent with T16/T17 lineage of `.t16-1-deferred.test.ts` / `.t17-1-deferred.test.ts`). The test-writer writes T18-scope tests against `MemoryIntegrityStore` per the F-86..F-100 obligations above; the deferred file is preserved for T18.1 pickup.

##### Handoff envelope

- **To test-writer:** ADR-0019 §Acceptance criteria originally listed F-86..F-100 as placeholders; this §3.11 ratifies the F-### range AS-IS (no renumbering needed — F-86..F-100 are sequential after §3.10's F-70..F-85 and have no collision in this file). ADR-0019's threat-model cross-reference section is updated below the table to confirm F-86..F-100 are final. All fifteen tests are mandatory for T18's four-way reviewer pass clearance; the LOAD-BEARING RA-2 pre-snapshot test (F-91) is non-negotiable for T18 ship. Seven carry `[T18.1 deferred]` tags whose tests land later but whose acceptance criteria are recorded now: F-86 (cross-mirror SQL drift), F-87 (SECURITY DEFINER sink wiring), F-88 (single-tx wrapper), F-94 (pgTAP JSONB structure), F-95 (A-AUDIT-001/A-INTEGRITY-002 sinks), F-96 (Edge Function email delivery), F-99 (statement_timeout / lock_timeout).
- **To security-reviewer:** at diff time on T18 PR, verify F-86 (drift CI), F-87 (audit-before-alert-fanout — mismatch row visible before alert symbol), F-88 (summary-LAST in tx — full rollback on emit failure), F-91 (LOAD-BEARING backup-diff with the pre-snapshot test; confirm "breaking this test re-opens RA-2" is structurally enforced), F-92 (reconciliation rule pinned in BOTH directions), F-93 (runtime-pin coherence → OPERATIONAL not A-AUDIT-001), F-95 (A-AUDIT-001 vs A-INTEGRITY-002 distinct), F-97 (no caller-supplied config — confirm `tsc --noEmit` fixture test), F-98 (TestStore type split + barrel re-export check), F-100 (no PII in errors — closed-literal error_codes). At diff time on T18.1 PR (deferred), verify G-T18-1 advisory lock, G-T18-3 SECURITY DEFINER signatures, G-T18-4 cross-mirror SQL drift, G-T18-5 single-tx wrapper, G-T18-6 enum extension dance.
- **To privacy-reviewer:** PI inventory for `integrity_check_runs` (no PI; counts + run metadata only — `run_id`, `trigger`, `started_at_ms`, `completed_at_ms`, `status`, `rows_walked`, `mismatches_count`, `attributable_count`, `unattributable_count`, `backup_diff_performed`, `backup_manifest_run_id`, `resume_after_id`, `node_runtime_pin`, `schedule_hash`; mirrors `retention_sweep_runs`) and optional `audit_chain_anchors` (no PI; head pointer triple + delivery timestamp only) lands in T18.1 per G-T18-7. ADR-0019 §Compliance check confirms PIPEDA Principle 4.5 + 4.7 alignment; HG-10 NOT firing is defensible (operator-facing alerts only; zero user copy). Cross-border transfers: NONE introduced by this surface (T18 reads `audit_log` + `retention_sweep_runs` + `backup_manifests` all in `ca-central-1`; the weekly off-app anchor email is operator-mediated to the worker co-chair's email-of-record; no platform subprocessor; ADR-0010 single-subprocessor posture preserved).
- **To user (human-gate items):**
  - **HG-15 (re-fires at T18.1 PR submission)** for the new physical table `integrity_check_runs` AND optionally `audit_chain_anchors`. Recorded in ADR-0019 §Compliance check + sibling task spec #14.
  - **HG-10 explicitly NOT firing** in this pass (operator-facing alerts only; zero user copy; ADR-0019 §Compliance check).
  - **HG-9 (retention schedule) ratified 2026-05-22** for ADR-0012 amendment + ADR-0015; NOT re-firing in this pass — the three new event types extend the closed `AuditEventType` union via the standard six-mirror ADR-0003 Amendment A extension dance, covered by ADR-0018 Option H / G-T08-9 / G-T13-14 / G-T14-7.
  - **No new HG fires in T18 itself.**
