  - _vitest (decrypt-fail is fail-closed):_ a corrupted `title_ct`/`body_ct`/`source_name_ct`/`wrapped_ciphertext` causes `openUtf8`/`crypto_box_seal_open` to return a typed failure (`decrypt_failed`), never a thrown raw exception leaking key/plaintext bytes (cross-ref F-148).

### Repudiation (R)

#### F-151 | R | Unwrap / concern-create / source-reveal audit rows forged or suppressed by the client; the unwrap audit could be bypassed

The audit rows `committee_data_key.unwrap` (Flow 1), `concern.created` (Flow 2), and `concern.source_revealed` (Flow 4) are the attribution witnesses. A malicious client could try to forge/suppress them, OR — the load-bearing new concern — obtain the wrap bytes WITHOUT the `committee_data_key.unwrap` row landing (audit bypass), which would let a member read committee material with no forensic trace.

- **Affected:** the new `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` audit-before-return invariant; the server-owned emission in `concern_submit` / `reveal_concern_source`.
- **Likelihood:** LOW. **Impact:** HIGH (untraced key-material access defeats the forensic posture). **Priority:** MEDIUM-HIGH — flagged.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) ALL three audit rows are emitted SERVER-SIDE inside SECURITY DEFINER SQL, atomically — the client cannot forge or suppress them; (2) **audit-before-return** on the unwrap RPC: the `committee_data_key.unwrap` row is emitted (folding `record_committee_data_key_unwrap`'s gate-check + `audit_emit`) INSIDE the same txn, BEFORE the `RETURN QUERY` of the ciphertext — exactly mirroring `reveal_concern_source` at `00000000000004_concerns.sql:317-330`. The audit row commits before the bytes leave the function; a dropped response still leaves the audit row. This collapses the prior two-call dance (read-wrap + `record_unwrap`) into one atomic audited read — there is NO ordering where bytes return without the audit row; (3) pseudonyms via the key-parity-gated `_hmac_pseudonym_key()` (F-124–F-126).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-10 / AC-3 / AC-11):**
  - _pgTAP (audit-before-return, the load-bearing assertion):_ inject a failure AFTER the `committee_data_key.unwrap` `audit_emit` but at/before the `RETURN QUERY` and assert the audit row is ALREADY committed (present) — i.e. the audit emit is ordered before the byte return in one txn, mirroring the `reveal_concern_source` pgTAP pattern (AC-10). Assert there is NO code path in `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` that returns `wrapped_ciphertext` without first emitting the audit row.
  - _vitest (client emits nothing):_ assert `unwrapCommitteeDataKeyViaProduction` and the three concern compositions call NO client-side audit-emit path — the only audit rows are server-emitted (no `recordKeyEvent`/client audit call in the production compositions).
  - _vitest (reveal audit-before-return end-to-end):_ on reveal, assert the `concern.source_revealed` audit-spy fires BEFORE the composition resolves the ciphertext (client must not `openUtf8(source_name_ct)` until the RPC returns) (AC-3).
  - _vitest (single unwrap per session, AC-11):_ two sequential seal/open ops in one session emit exactly ONE `committee_data_key.unwrap` row (holder reused); a sign-out wipe then a subsequent op emits a SECOND unwrap row. Confirms idempotent-read dwell does not duplicate audit, and that re-unwrap after wipe re-audits.

### Information disclosure (I)

#### F-142 | I/E | HIGH — the new committee-key-unwrap disclosure RPC: IDOR, scope, and server-compromise exposure

**`get_committee_key_wrap_for_self()` is the FIRST production RPC that returns committee key material across B2.** The disclosure risks: (1) **IDOR** — can a caller obtain ANOTHER member's wrap by supplying an id? (2) **disclosure scope** — what does a server/hosting compromise (A5) see? (3) over-return — does it leak more than the live key's own wrap? This surface is SHARED by Phase 2b/2c/2d, so the ruling is load-bearing beyond Phase 2a. **Security-reviewer co-sign required at PR 1.**

- **Affected:** `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` (migration `…38`); t07-op `get_key_wrap`; `SupabaseT07Client.getCommitteeKeyWrapForSelf`.
- **Likelihood:** LOW (mitigated by design — self-scoped + REVOKE + sealed). **Impact:** HIGH (key-material surface; blast radius = all Phase 2 E2EE features). **Priority:** HIGH — flagged for PR-1 co-sign.
- **Existing/required mitigation (all baked into the RPC contract):**
  1. **No IDOR — the actor is `auth.uid()`, NEVER a parameter.** The RPC takes no id argument; it reads `WHERE user_id = auth.uid() AND rotated_at IS NULL`. A client-supplied id is non-authoritative because there is no id input to supply. It can NEVER return another member's wrap.
  2. **Grants:** `REVOKE EXECUTE FROM PUBLIC, anon, service_role`; `GRANT EXECUTE TO authenticated, supabase_auth_admin`; `SECURITY DEFINER`, `SET search_path=public, extensions`; gated on `_t07_gate_active_member()` — exactly mirrors `committee_key_state_for_self` (migration 0037).
  3. **Disclosure scope under A5:** the RPC returns ONLY the SEALED wrap ciphertext — opaque without the device privkey (`crypto_box_seal_open` needs the actor's identity privkey, which never crosses B2, F-129). A server/hosting compromise or rogue admin (A5) sees only ciphertext it already holds at rest in `committee_key_wraps` — **the RPC adds NO new plaintext exposure at A5.** It returns the live key's wrap only (`rotated_at IS NULL`), not historical wraps.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-10 — HIGH; pgTAP + vitest):**
  - _pgTAP (no-IDOR / own-wrap-only):_ as member A, call `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self()` and assert the returned `key_id`/`wrapped_ciphertext` is A's OWN live-key wrap; seed member B's wrap and assert A's call NEVER returns B's row. Assert the function signature takes NO id parameter (own-wrap-only is structural, not a runtime check) (AC-10).
  - _pgTAP (grants):_ assert `EXECUTE` is REVOKED from PUBLIC/anon/service_role and GRANTED to authenticated + supabase_auth_admin; a non-member (active-member gate fails) call raises the gate exception (AC-10).
  - _pgTAP (live-key-only):_ with a rotated (`rotated_at` set) old wrap AND a live wrap for the actor, assert the RPC returns ONLY the live (`rotated_at IS NULL`) wrap, never the retired one.
  - _vitest (sealed-scope):_ assert the bytes returned by `getCommitteeKeyWrapForSelf` are the SEALED wrap (do not decrypt without the device privkey) — `crypto_box_seal_open` with a WRONG privkey fails; only the actor's privkey opens it (proves server-compromise sees only ciphertext).

#### F-144 | I | Unwrap on a no-wrap / no-device-privkey actor leaks provisioning state or mis-routes instead of failing clean

A caller with no committee-key wrap (not yet onboarded), or whose device lacks the identity privkey (new device / cleared IndexedDB), must NOT receive an error that leaks provisioning state nor be silently treated as "no access." It must route to the correct remediation (Phase 0a setup, or recovery-restore) — without ever hitting the disclosure RPC when no wrap exists (Decision 7 probe-first guard, the worker-without-key case).

- **Affected:** Decision 7 state-probe guard; `unwrapCommitteeDataKeyViaProduction` discriminated-union (`no_wrap` / `needs_recovery` / `ok` / `failed`).
- **Likelihood:** MEDIUM (a real onboarding state). **Impact:** LOW (no PI/key leak; UX/routing correctness). **Priority:** LOW-MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) **probe-first:** the page calls `getCommitteeKeyState` (metadata-only) FIRST; if `actor_has_wrap === false` it renders the Phase-0a-setup guard and **NEVER calls `getCommitteeKeyWrapForSelf`** — the disclosure RPC is not hit for a member with no wrap (Decision 7, the worker-without-key probe-first guard); (2) `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` returns NO rows (not an error) for a no-wrap actor → composition maps to `{ status: 'no_wrap' }` → routes to setup; (3) absent device privkey → `{ status: 'needs_recovery' }` → recovery-restore (cross-ref F-139 edge-B restore path), NEVER a second enroll.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-7):**
  - _vitest (probe-first, the worker-without-key guard):_ with `actor_has_wrap === false` from `getCommitteeKeyState`, assert the page renders the Phase-0a-setup guard and that `getCommitteeKeyWrapForSelf` is NEVER called (assert the disclosure RPC transport is not invoked) (AC-7).
  - _vitest (no-wrap branch):_ `unwrapCommitteeDataKeyViaProduction` against a no-wrap actor (RPC returns null) returns `{ status: 'no_wrap' }` and generates NO data key, opens NO holder.
  - _vitest (needs-recovery branch):_ with a server-side wrap present but `localIdentity.getIdentityPrivateKey(user_id)` empty, returns `{ status: 'needs_recovery' }` and routes to restore, NEVER to enroll (cross-ref F-139).

#### F-148 | I | Key material or concern plaintext leaks into logs, errors, audit-meta, storage, or URL

Phase 2a handles, transiently in the browser: the plaintext 32-byte committee data key (now session-resident, F-145), the identity privkey (B4, unchanged), and plaintext concern title/body/source (render scope). Any landing in `console.*`, a thrown error message, the structured-log path, an audit `meta`, sessionStorage/localStorage/IndexedDB, or a URL is a confidentiality break (A4/A5). The session-resident data key is a NEW surface the Phase 0a leak gate (F-132) did not cover.

- **Affected:** `unwrapCommitteeDataKeyViaProduction`, `CommitteeKeyHolder`, the three concern compositions, all error/toast/log surfaces touched by submit/list/reveal.
- **Likelihood:** LOW (mitigated by the leak-sweep gate). **Impact:** HIGH (a leak of the data key defeats the whole E2EE model; ADR-0003 Invariants 1/5). **Priority:** HIGH.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the data key exists in plaintext ONLY in the heap holder, NEVER serialized to storage/URL/log/audit (Decision 1); (2) identity privkey NEVER transmitted (F-129) and NEVER logged; (3) plaintext title/body/source exist ONLY in render scope, NEVER persisted or logged (Decision 3); (4) the SEALED ciphertext is what crosses the wire (Flows 2/3/4); (5) audit emission is server-owned — the client cannot put key material or plaintext into audit meta; (6) no-PI bodies on 429/403 (Decision 8 / F-152).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-9 — extends the §3.15 F-132 / Phase 0a leak-sweep CI gate):**
  - _vitest (full-workflow leak sweep):_ instrument `console.*`, captured thrown-error `.message`/`.stack`, the structured-log emit surface (`apps/web/src/lib/log/`), and any client-constructed audit `meta`; run submit + list + reveal (happy path + each error branch); assert NONE of {the 32 plaintext data-key bytes, the identity privkey bytes, any plaintext concern title/body/source string} appears in any captured surface (AC-9).
  - _vitest (no serialization):_ assert the data key is NOT readable from `sessionStorage`, `localStorage`, IndexedDB, any Svelte store that serializes, or any URL fragment at any point in the session (Decision 1 non-serialization invariant).
  - _CI grep (uniformity):_ extend the existing key-material-leak grep to flag any Phase 2a path passing the data-key buffer, the privkey, or a plaintext concern field into a log/toast/error/audit-meta constructor (AC-9 as a CI gate, P2a-10).

#### F-149 | I | List-view PI projection — confirm pseudonym, NOT raw actor_id, crosses the wire; no cross-surface correlation regression

Today `concerns_default_view` exposes raw `actor_id` (submitter uuid) to every active member — a re-identification vector (cross-reference with `committee_membership`) and an over-disclosure of who filed what. Decision 5 widens the view to `_committee_pseudonym(actor_id)` and DROPS raw `actor_id`. The threat is a regression: the migration must actually drop `actor_id` from the projection AND the pseudonym must match the audit pseudonym (so it introduces NO NEW cross-surface correlation vector beyond what the audit feed already has). **Privacy-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign at P2a-6.**

- **Affected:** `concerns_default_view` migration (P2a-6, `00000000000004_concerns.sql:270-279` redefinition); `_committee_pseudonym`; `ConcernListRow` client shape.
- **Likelihood:** n/a (this is a directional PI change, not an attack). **Impact:** POSITIVE (PI REDUCTION) if done right; MEDIUM-negative if the drop is botched (raw uuid keeps leaking). **Priority:** MEDIUM (PI-projection change — flagged).
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the view ADDs `_committee_pseudonym(c.actor_id) AS actor_pseudonym` (same key-parity-gated HMAC the audit feed uses at `:189`) and `(c.source_name_ct IS NULL) AS anonymous_default_kept`; (2) it DROPS the raw `actor_id` column from the projection — the raw uuid no longer crosses B2; (3) the pseudonym carries the SAME re-identifiability posture as the audit feed (no NEW vector — a member could already correlate audit pseudonyms; this just makes the list consistent with that posture and CLOSES the raw-uuid leak); (4) no new field COLLECTED (constraints.md hard rule 6 N/A).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-2):**
  - _pgTAP (raw actor_id absent):_ assert `concerns_default_view`'s column set does NOT include `actor_id` and DOES include `actor_pseudonym` + `anonymous_default_kept` + `has_named_source` — i.e. the raw uuid is structurally absent from the projection (AC-2).
  - _pgTAP (pseudonym matches audit):_ assert the view's `actor_pseudonym` for a given concern equals `_committee_pseudonym(actor_id)` computed the same way the `concern.created` audit row computes the submitter pseudonym (no cross-surface correlation regression — list pseudonym == audit pseudonym).
  - _vitest (no raw actor_id on the wire):_ `listConcernsViaProduction` rows carry `actor_pseudonym` and NEVER a raw `actor_id` field; assert no row object has an `actor_id` key (AC-2).
  - _vitest (no status; client-derived days):_ rows carry a client-derived `days_since_filed` (from `created_at`) and NO `status` field (Decision 6) (AC-2).

#### F-150 | I | Reveal-source: client decrypts source_name before the server audit row lands (audit-before-return broken end-to-end)

F-18 excludes `source_name_ct` from the default view; reveal is the only path to it, and `reveal_concern_source` emits `concern.source_revealed` BEFORE returning the ciphertext (`:317-330`). The end-to-end threat: the production composition must NOT `openUtf8(source_name_ct)` (nor display the source) until the RPC returns — if the client somehow obtained/cached the ct and decrypted it without the reveal round-trip, the audit-before-return invariant would be defeated and a source unmasked without a `concern.source_revealed` witness.

- **Affected:** `revealConcernSourceViaProduction`; `concern-op reveal_concern_source` (server, the SQL audit-before-return); `listConcernsViaProduction` (must NOT carry `source_name_ct`).
- **Likelihood:** LOW. **Impact:** HIGH (an unwitnessed source unmasking — the highest-sensitivity concern field). **Priority:** MEDIUM-HIGH — flagged.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) `source_name_ct` is EXCLUDED from `concerns_default_view` (F-18) — the list path never carries the source ciphertext, so the client cannot decrypt a source from the list; (2) the ONLY path to `source_name_ct` is `reveal_concern_source`, which emits `concern.source_revealed` audit-BEFORE-return inside one txn (`:317-330`) — the audit commits even if the response is dropped; (3) the composition opens the source ONLY after the RPC returns (it has no other source); (4) anonymous concerns (`source_name_ct IS NULL`) return `{ status: 'anonymous' }` with no decrypt.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-3 / AC-4 / F-18):**
  - _vitest (audit-before-decrypt end-to-end):_ on `revealConcernSourceViaProduction`, assert the `concern.source_revealed` audit-spy fires BEFORE the composition resolves the source plaintext; the client does NOT call `openUtf8(source_name_ct)` until the reveal RPC resolves (AC-3).
  - _vitest (list carries no source ct):_ assert `listConcernsViaProduction` rows carry NO `source_name_ct` field — only `has_named_source` (boolean) and `anonymous_default_kept` (F-18 carried forward); the source can ONLY be obtained via the reveal RPC.
  - _vitest (anonymous):_ a concern with `source_name_ct === null` returns `{ status: 'anonymous' }`, performs NO decrypt, and the list row shows `has_named_source === false` + `anonymous_default_kept === true` (AC-4).
  - _pgTAP (carry-forward):_ `reveal_concern_source` emits `concern.source_revealed` BEFORE returning ciphertext, in one txn (existing reveal contract test; cross-ref the F-142 audit-before-return pgTAP pattern).

### Denial of service (D)

#### F-152 | D | Submit-rate-limit 429 surfaced in a way that leaks which window tripped, or rate-limit not enforced

F-20's dual-window budget (20/hr + 200/24h, server-side) caps concern submission. The DoS/disclosure hazards: (1) a 429 response or client copy that reveals WHICH window tripped (hr vs 24h) leaks the limit structure to an abuser tuning a flood; (2) any client-side-only enforcement could be bypassed; (3) a 429 body carrying PI.

- **Affected:** `concern_submit` (F-20 budget, server-side); `submitConcernViaProduction` 429 handling.
- **Likelihood:** MEDIUM (rate-limit is reachable by any member). **Impact:** LOW (the budget holds; the leak is structural, not data). **Priority:** LOW-MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) F-20's budget is enforced SERVER-SIDE in `concern_submit` (client cannot bypass); (2) the 429 path surfaces a generic "you're submitting too fast" with NO PI in the body and WITHOUT disclosing which of the two windows tripped (Decision 4 step 5; Decision 8 no-PI bodies); (3) on 429 the holder is NOT wiped (rate-limit is not a session event, F-145) and NO ciphertext is persisted; (4) the dual-window structure itself is not echoed back.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-6):**
  - _vitest (429 no-leak, no-wipe):_ `submitConcernViaProduction` on HTTP 429 surfaces a rate-limited state with NO PI in the body and NO indication of which window tripped; no ciphertext is persisted; the `CommitteeKeyHolder` is NOT wiped (assert the buffer is still non-zero) and the JWT is NOT cleared (AC-6).
  - _pgTAP (carry-forward, server enforcement):_ the F-20 dual-window budget is enforced in `concern_submit` (existing F-20 test); the 21st submit in an hour / 201st in 24h is denied server-side.

#### F-153 | D | The new unwrap RPC as a DoS amplification vector

`get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` is a new authenticated endpoint. The DoS questions: does it amplify (cheap request → expensive server work)? Does the per-call audit emit (audit fires EACH call, idempotent read) create unbounded audit growth under a flood?

- **Affected:** `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self`; t07-op `get_key_wrap`; the `committee_data_key.unwrap` audit table.
- **Likelihood:** LOW (authenticated + active-member-gated; not anonymously reachable). **Impact:** LOW (a single indexed row read + one audit insert per call). **Priority:** LOW.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the RPC is gated on `_t07_gate_active_member()` + `session_is_live()` — only an authenticated active member reaches it (not anon, A4 external flood is blocked at B1); (2) it is a single indexed `WHERE user_id = auth.uid() AND rotated_at IS NULL` read — no fan-out, no amplification; (3) **audit-growth under flood:** the audit fires per call (idempotent read), which is acceptable BECAUSE Decision 1's session-scoped holder means the production client calls it ONCE per session (cached thereafter) — a member spamming the raw RPC to inflate audit is (a) authenticated/attributable, (b) self-limited (it is their own pseudonym on every row), and (c) bounded by the same session/auth controls; the forensically meaningful events (`concern.created`/`concern.source_revealed`) are per-op regardless. Per-call audit on this read is the intended, accepted design (Decision 1 audit-consequence note).
- **Testable mitigation:**
  - _vitest (holder caches — one unwrap per session):_ the production path calls `getCommitteeKeyWrapForSelf` exactly ONCE per session for N seal/open ops (holder reuse) — assert the transport is hit once, not per-op (AC-11; bounds the audit growth in normal use).
  - _pgTAP (single indexed read):_ assert the RPC body is a single self-scoped SELECT (no join fan-out, no loop) — structural, prevents an amplification regression.
  - _accepted residual:_ a member directly spamming the RPC inflates their OWN attributable audit rows; not a DoS on others, not anonymously reachable. No new control required.

### Elevation of privilege (E)

#### F-145 | E/I | HIGH — in-memory dwell of the plaintext committee data key: wipe-trigger exhaustiveness

Decision 1 makes the plaintext 32-byte committee data key dwell in browser RAM (the `CommitteeKeyHolder`) for the session — a dwell policy ADR-0003 Invariant 1 permits but the threat model had NO explicit policy for. The threat: a path where the plaintext key SURVIVES a session-end event (sign-out, revocation, panic-wipe, expiry) — leaving live key material in the heap of a device that should no longer hold it (A2 employer-owned device after the rep signs out; A3 coerced rep; A6 bfcache restore). The exhaustiveness of the SIX wipe triggers is the whole safety argument. **Security-reviewer co-sign required at PR 1 (P2a-4).**

- **Affected:** `CommitteeKeyHolder` (`committee-key-holder.ts`); the six wipe-trigger wirings (`clearJwt`/sign-out, `onSessionRevoked`/401, `BrowserWipeStore`/panic, session-expiry timer, `beforeunload`/`pagehide`, observed key rotation).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (requires a missed trigger + device access). **Impact:** HIGH (live committee key in the heap of a signed-out/wiped/revoked device — defeats the E2EE confinement for that device). **Priority:** HIGH — flagged for PR-1 co-sign.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** every trigger calls `holder.wipe()` which `.fill(0)`s the `data_key` buffer (libsodium `memzero` if exposed, else `.fill(0)`) then nulls the reference. The six triggers (ALL mandatory):
  1. **Sign-out / `clearJwt`** — the JWT-clear path also wipes the holder.
  2. **Session revocation / HTTP 401** — `onSessionRevoked` wipes the holder in the same handler that clears the JWT.
  3. **Panic-wipe (`BrowserWipeStore`)** — wipes the holder **BEFORE** clearing IndexedDB identity material (ordering is load-bearing: the most sensitive in-memory secret goes first, so a panic-wipe interrupted mid-way has already zeroized the live key).
  4. **Session expiry** — when the mint-session JWT expiry passes, the holder is wiped; next op re-unwraps (re-emits one `committee_data_key.unwrap`).
  5. **Tab/window close / page unload** — best-effort `beforeunload`/`pagehide` wipe (reduces dwell on bfcache restore; not a hard guarantee since the heap is torn down anyway).
  6. **Observed key rotation** — if an op/probe observes a `key_id`/epoch newer than the cached one, wipe + re-unwrap against the new key (prevents sealing under a stale key — the F-137 hazard).
  The single-buffer-by-reference handoff (F-147) guarantees there is exactly one buffer to wipe.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-8 / AC-11 — HIGH; vitest):**
  - _vitest (each of the 6 triggers zeroizes):_ for EACH trigger (sign-out/`clearJwt`, 401/`onSessionRevoked`, panic-wipe, session-expiry, `beforeunload`/`pagehide`, observed-rotation), populate the holder, fire the trigger, and assert the exact `data_key` `Uint8Array` is all-zero AND the holder reference is `null` afterward. Six assertions, one per trigger — no trigger may be skipped (AC-8 covers 401; the other five are explicit here).
  - _vitest (panic-wipe ordering — load-bearing):_ assert the holder is wiped BEFORE `BrowserWipeStore` clears IndexedDB — spy both and assert holder-wipe-happens-before-IndexedDB-clear ordering. If panic-wipe is interrupted after the holder wipe but before IndexedDB, the live key is already zero (AC-8 extension).
  - _vitest (401 distinct from 403):_ HTTP 401 wipes the holder + fires `onSessionRevoked` + clears JWT; HTTP 403 (`rls_denied`) does NOT wipe the holder and does NOT clear the JWT (AC-8).
  - _vitest (rotation re-unwrap):_ when a probe/op observes a newer `key_id`, assert the holder is wiped and re-unwrapped against the new key (no seal/open proceeds under the stale key).

#### F-146 | E/I | The committee data key serialized to persistent storage / Svelte store / URL / bfcache — surviving beyond the heap

A corollary of F-145: even with the six wipe triggers, if the key were ever written to IndexedDB, localStorage, sessionStorage, a serializing Svelte store, a URL, or the audit meta, it would survive the heap wipe and persist on a personal/employer-owned device (A2) past session end. Decision 1 forbids ALL of these — the holder is heap-only.

- **Affected:** `CommitteeKeyHolder` (must NOT be a `writable()` store that serializes; must NOT touch any storage API or URL).
- **Likelihood:** LOW. **Impact:** HIGH (a persisted key defeats every wipe trigger). **Priority:** HIGH (covered jointly with F-145/F-148).
- **Existing/required mitigation:** the holder is a module-scoped object holding `{ data_key, key_id, epoch } | null` in the JS heap ONLY — NEVER written to IndexedDB/localStorage/sessionStorage, a serializing Svelte store, a URL, or audit meta (Decision 1, explicit).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-9):**
  - _vitest (no-serialization, covered with F-148):_ after populating the holder, assert the 32 key bytes are NOT present in `sessionStorage`, `localStorage`, IndexedDB, any URL fragment, or any serialized store snapshot — at any point in the session lifecycle (extends the AC-9 leak sweep with a storage scan).
  - _static/CI guard:_ assert the `CommitteeKeyHolder` module imports NO storage API and is NOT registered as a persisted/serialized store (grep + review at P2a-4).

#### F-154 | E | Sealing/opening under a stale (rotated) key, or a low-priv path obtaining the live key it should not hold

If a member's holder caches a key that has since been rotated (a co-chair on another device rotated), continuing to seal under the stale key would create ciphertext no current member can read (the F-137 divergent-epoch hazard), or a member whose access was revoked could still hold a cached live key.

- **Affected:** `CommitteeKeyHolder` rotation-observed wipe (trigger 6); `unwrapCommitteeDataKeyViaProduction` epoch handling; the 401/revocation wipe (F-145 trigger 2).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (Phase 2a does not rotate; but a co-chair on another device might). **Impact:** MEDIUM (stale-key ciphertext is unreadable; a revoked member with a cached key is a confinement gap until the 401 lands). **Priority:** MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the observed-rotation wipe (F-145 trigger 6) wipes + re-unwraps against the new key when an op/probe sees a newer `key_id`/epoch — no seal under a stale key; (2) revocation drives an HTTP 401 (`session_is_live()` denies the revoked-but-unexpired JWT within ≤5s, F-116/F-121), which wipes the holder (F-145 trigger 2) — a revoked member's cached key is zeroized within ≤5s of the next privileged call; (3) the active-member gate on every concern RPC + the unwrap RPC means a revoked member cannot re-unwrap.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-11 / AC-8):**
  - _vitest (stale-key guard):_ given a cached key at epoch N and a probe/op observing epoch N+1, assert no `sealUtf8`/`openUtf8` runs under the epoch-N key — the holder wipes and re-unwraps against epoch N+1 first (AC-11 rotation case).
  - _vitest (revocation wipe within one cycle):_ a 401 (revoked session) wipes the cached key and the next op cannot proceed without a fresh (denied) unwrap (cross-ref F-145 trigger 2 / AC-8).

### §6 — Phase 2a compliance / breach-notification verification (PIPEDA s.10.1)

ADR-0027 introduces **no new PI field collected**, **no new subprocessor**, **no new region** (all rows land in the existing ca-central-1 project, ADR-0001), **no new audit enum value** (reuses `committee_data_key.unwrap` / `concern.created` / `concern.source_revealed`, all on the closed allowlist + ADR-0016 schedule), and **no new retention class**. Constraints.md hard rule 6 (documented-purpose-per-new-field) is **N/A** — no new field; the concern fields' purpose is the established OHSA s.8–9 worker-concern register (ADR-0003/0004). Hard rule 3 (subprocessor) and hard rule 4 (region) are **N/A** by construction.

**PIPEDA fair-information principle mapping (the Phase 2a deltas):**

- **P1 Accountability / P2 Identifying purposes / P3 Consent / P4 Limiting collection:** unchanged — no new collection; existing concern-register purpose + consent posture carry forward.
- **P5 Limiting use/disclosure/retention:** **IMPROVED.** Decision 5 REDUCES disclosure — raw `actor_id` no longer crosses B2 to every active member; only a pseudonym does. Retention unchanged (existing `concern.*` / `committee_data_key.*` enums + ADR-0016). This is a net-positive data-minimization move (constraints.md P4/P5).
- **P6 Accuracy / P8 Openness / P9 Individual access / P10 Challenging compliance:** unchanged — no new processing.
- **P7 Safeguards:** **STRENGTHENED in posture, with one new dwell surface.** The unwrap RPC is gated, self-scoped, audit-before-return, and returns only sealed ciphertext (F-142). The new safeguard concern is the in-memory dwell of the plaintext data key (F-145/F-146); the six-trigger wipe + non-serialization is the mitigating safeguard, and it is testable (AC-8). Net: safeguards are appropriate to the sensitivity and the new surface is mitigated.

**Breach-notification trigger assessment (the two surfaces, assessed separately as requested):**

1. **The unwrap RPC (F-142):** returns key material to the AUTHENTICATED OWNER ONLY (`auth.uid()`-scoped, no IDOR), audit-logged before return, returning only SEALED ciphertext that is opaque without the device privkey. A server/hosting compromise (A5) sees only ciphertext it already holds at rest — **no new plaintext exposure.** The plaintext key never crosses B2. **This introduces NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 "real risk of significant harm" surface.** (The in-memory dwell, F-145, is a device-local heap exposure mitigated by the six-trigger wipe; a missed-trigger residual is a single-device confidentiality concern, not a server-side mass-disclosure breach — and the wipe set is required + tested, so the residual is controlled. It does not, on its own, meet the s.10.1 mass-harm threshold; it remains HIGH-priority as a confinement invariant.)
2. **The view-projection change (F-149):** REDUCES PI exposure (raw `actor_id` → pseudonym). This is a privacy IMPROVEMENT — it CLOSES an existing over-disclosure (every active member could previously read the raw submitter uuid). It introduces no new exposure; the pseudonym carries the same re-identifiability posture as the audit feed (no new vector). **No new s.10.1 trigger; it narrows the prior surface.**

**Conclusion: Phase 2a introduces NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 breach-notification trigger.** The unwrap RPC adds no plaintext disclosure at A5; the view change reduces PI exposure. The 24-month breach-record-keeping obligation is unchanged. **No PHIPA trigger** (no health information — worker safety concerns under OHSA are not PHIPA "personal health information"; if a future concern field captured identifiable health info, PHIPA's 60-day notice + custodian + lockbox rules would fire — flagged as a re-pass trigger). **No PCI trigger** (no payment data). **No cross-border transfer** introduced — all data stays in ca-central-1.

### Top 5 prioritized risks (Phase 2a only; for the parent agent's summary)

1. **F-142 (HIGH) — the new committee-key-unwrap disclosure RPC (`get_committee_key_wrap_for_self`):** first production endpoint returning committee key material across B2; shared by Phase 2b/2c/2d. Mitigation: actor is `auth.uid()` (no id parameter → no IDOR); REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role + active-member gate; returns ONLY the live key's sealed wrap (opaque without the device privkey → A5 sees only ciphertext it already holds). **Security-reviewer co-sign at PR 1** (AC-10).
2. **F-145 (HIGH) — in-memory dwell of the plaintext committee data key (wipe-trigger exhaustiveness):** the plaintext key now dwells in browser RAM for the session. Mitigation: SIX mandatory `holder.wipe()` triggers (sign-out / 401 / panic-wipe / expiry / unload / rotation), each `.fill(0)`s the single buffer; panic-wipe zeroizes the key BEFORE clearing IndexedDB; one buffer by reference. **Security-reviewer co-sign at PR 1** (AC-8). Joint with F-146 (no serialization) + F-148 (no leak).
3. **F-148 (HIGH) — key-material / concern-plaintext leak:** the session-resident data key + plaintext title/body/source must never hit logs/errors/audit-meta/storage/URL. Mitigation: full-workflow leak-sweep CI gate across submit/list/reveal + no-serialization scan; extends the §3.15 F-132 gate (AC-9).
4. **F-151 (MED-HIGH) — audit-bypass on the unwrap RPC + reveal:** key material returned without a `committee_data_key.unwrap` row, or a source unmasked without `concern.source_revealed`. Mitigation: audit-BEFORE-return inside one txn on both RPCs (mirror `reveal_concern_source` :317-330); pgTAP asserts the audit row commits before the bytes return (AC-10/AC-3).
5. **F-149 (MED) — list-view PI-projection change:** must DROP raw `actor_id` and expose only the pseudonym, matching the audit pseudonym (no correlation regression). Mitigation: pgTAP asserts `actor_id` structurally absent from the view + `actor_pseudonym == _committee_pseudonym(actor_id)`; vitest asserts no raw `actor_id` on the wire. **Privacy-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign at P2a-6** (AC-2).

### Handoff packets

- **To test-writer (priority order; each test RED against `main` before its implementer PR opens):**
  1. **F-142 (HIGH, AC-10) — unwrap RPC disclosure surface (PR 1):** pgTAP — own-wrap-only / no-IDOR (no id parameter; never returns another member's wrap); grants REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role + active-member gate raises for non-member; live-key-only (rotated wrap never returned); audit-BEFORE-return (audit row committed before `RETURN QUERY`, inject-failure pattern mirroring `reveal_concern_source`). vitest — returned bytes are SEALED (wrong privkey fails `crypto_box_seal_open`, only the actor's privkey opens).
  2. **F-145 / F-146 (HIGH, AC-8/AC-11) — in-memory dwell (PR 1):** vitest — each of the SIX wipe triggers zeroizes the exact `data_key` buffer + nulls the reference (six assertions); panic-wipe wipes the holder BEFORE IndexedDB (ordering spy); 401 wipes + 403 does not; observed-rotation wipes + re-unwraps; no-serialization scan (key bytes absent from sessionStorage/localStorage/IndexedDB/URL/serialized store).
  3. **F-148 (HIGH, AC-9) — leak sweep (both PRs):** vitest — full submit/list/reveal sweep across `console.*`/thrown-error/structured-log/audit-meta asserts NONE of {32 data-key bytes, identity privkey, plaintext title/body/source} appears; extend the §3.15 F-132 / passwd-leak CI grep to the data-key + concern-plaintext surfaces (P2a-10).
  4. **F-151 (MED-HIGH, AC-10/AC-3/AC-11) — audit-before-return + no client audit:** pgTAP unwrap audit-before-return; vitest reveal audit-spy fires before the source resolves (client must not `openUtf8(source_name_ct)` until the RPC returns); compositions call NO client-side audit-emit; ONE `committee_data_key.unwrap` per session (holder reuse), a SECOND after sign-out + re-op.
  5. **F-149 (MED, AC-2) — PI-projection (PR 2 / P2a-6):** pgTAP — `actor_id` structurally absent from `concerns_default_view`; `actor_pseudonym == _committee_pseudonym(actor_id)`; `anonymous_default_kept` + `has_named_source` present. vitest — list rows carry `actor_pseudonym`, NO `actor_id` key, client-derived `days_since_filed`, NO `status`.
  6. **F-150 (MED-HIGH, AC-3/AC-4) — reveal audit-before-decrypt + source excluded from list:** vitest — reveal audit-spy fires before the source resolves; list rows carry NO `source_name_ct` (only `has_named_source`, F-18 carried forward); anonymous concern → `{ status: 'anonymous' }`, no decrypt.
  7. **F-152 (LOW-MED, AC-6) — 429 no-leak / no-wipe:** vitest — 429 surfaces a generic rate-limited state, NO PI body, NO disclosure of which window tripped, no ciphertext persisted, holder NOT wiped, JWT NOT cleared.
  8. **F-144 (LOW-MED, AC-7) — worker-without-key probe-first guard:** vitest — `actor_has_wrap === false` renders the Phase-0a-setup guard and the disclosure RPC is NEVER called; `no_wrap` / `needs_recovery` branches route correctly (recovery, not re-enroll).
  9. **F-143 (MED, AC-8/AC-10) — JWT/non-member:** pgTAP non-member gate on the unwrap RPC; vitest 401→sign-in-required+wipe, 403 distinct.
  10. **F-147 (MED, AC-9/AC-11) — single-buffer / no-alias + decrypt-fail-closed; F-153/F-154 (LOW/MED) — no DoS amplification (one unwrap per session) + stale-key/revocation wipe.**
  - Group as **"Phase 2a must-fail-first"**: **F-142, F-145/F-146, F-148, F-151** are the blocking four for PR 1 (the disclosure surface + dwell + leak + audit-bypass); **F-149, F-150** are the blocking two for PR 2 (PI projection + reveal). AC-10 (unwrap RPC) and AC-8 (dwell) are the architect's two flagged HIGH edges and must each be red first.
- **To security-reviewer (required at PR 1 per HG-CONCERNS-PHASE2A — the TWO HIGH surfaces co-sign):**
  1. **F-142 (PR 1, P2a-1):** verify `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` takes NO id parameter (own-wrap-only is structural, not a runtime check), reads `WHERE user_id = auth.uid() AND rotated_at IS NULL`, REVOKEs PUBLIC/anon/service_role + GRANTs authenticated/supabase_auth_admin, gates on `_t07_gate_active_member()`, and emits `committee_data_key.unwrap` audit-BEFORE-return in one txn (mirror `reveal_concern_source` :317-330). Confirm it returns ONLY the sealed wrap (opaque without the device privkey) and adds NO new ungated op (F-122 grep unaffected).
  2. **F-145/F-146 (PR 1, P2a-4):** verify ALL SIX wipe triggers call `holder.wipe()` (`.fill(0)` then null); verify panic-wipe wipes the holder BEFORE IndexedDB; verify the holder is heap-only (no storage API, not a serialized store, never to URL/audit-meta); verify the single-buffer-by-reference handoff (no second alias to the data key, F-147).
  3. **F-148 (both PRs, P2a-7/P2a-10):** verify the leak-sweep CI gate covers the data key + plaintext concern fields; verify the SEALED ciphertext is what crosses the wire on every flow.
  4. **F-151/F-150 (PR 2, P2a-7):** verify the reveal composition does not decrypt the source until the RPC returns (audit-before-return preserved end-to-end) and the compositions emit no client-side audit.
  5. **F-143/F-152/F-154:** verify the 401/403 split, the 429 no-leak/no-wipe posture, and the rotation/revocation wipe; confirm no new ungated op (F-122 grep unaffected).
- **To privacy-reviewer (required at P2a-6 — the PI-projection change):**
  1. **F-149:** confirm `concerns_default_view` DROPs raw `actor_id` from the projection and exposes `_committee_pseudonym(actor_id)` instead — ratify this as a PI REDUCTION (data minimization, PIPEDA P4/P5), and confirm the pseudonym carries the SAME re-identifiability posture as the audit feed (no new cross-surface correlation vector).
  2. **§6:** ratify that Phase 2a introduces NO new PI field, NO new subprocessor, NO new region, NO new retention class (hard rules 3/4/6 N/A by construction) and NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 breach trigger — the unwrap RPC adds no plaintext at A5; the view change narrows the prior surface.
  3. Confirm the plaintext concern title/body/source live ONLY in render scope (never persisted/logged) and the data key never serializes (F-146/F-148).
- **To the user (required human-gate decisions):**
  1. **HG-CONCERNS-PHASE2A (PR 1):** security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign of the TWO HIGH surfaces — the key-material-disclosure RPC (F-142, P2a-1) and the in-memory dwell policy (F-145, P2a-4). These are the first production key-material-read surface (inherited by Phase 2b/2c/2d) and the new heap-dwell of the plaintext data key.
  2. **HG-CONCERNS-PHASE2A (PR 2):** privacy-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign of the PI-projection change (F-149, P2a-6) and the end-to-end E2EE flow (P2a-7/P2a-9).
  3. **Production deploy of either PR** touches the E2EE/PI path → never auto-merge (constraints.md Human Gates: "Production deploys of changes touching … personal data"; hard rule 5: auth/authz/session are security-critical).
  - **No new cross-border transfer, no new subprocessor, no new credential surface, no new region** is introduced by Phase 2a — so NO HG-NEW-style transfer/credential gate fires. There is **nothing to approve under the cross-border human gate** for this feature (explicitly: all data remains in ca-central-1).

### Re-pass triggers (Phase 2a)

1. Any change that adds an id (or any client-supplied target) parameter to `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self`, or that returns a wrap for anything other than `auth.uid()`'s live key → re-open F-142 (IDOR) NO-GO.
2. Removal or weakening of any of the SIX `CommitteeKeyHolder` wipe triggers, any path that serializes the data key to storage/URL/store/audit-meta, or panic-wipe clearing IndexedDB BEFORE the holder → re-open F-145/F-146 NO-GO.
3. Any path that returns the wrap bytes WITHOUT first committing the `committee_data_key.unwrap` audit row (audit-before-return broken), or any reveal path that decrypts `source_name_ct` before the RPC returns → re-open F-151/F-150 NO-GO.
4. The view-widening migration NOT dropping raw `actor_id` from the projection, or a `actor_pseudonym` that diverges from the audit `_committee_pseudonym` → re-open F-149.
5. Any new log/toast/error/audit-meta path touching the plaintext data key or a plaintext concern field → re-open F-148.
6. A future concern field capturing identifiable health information → PHIPA fires (60-day notice, custodian, lockbox); escalate to privacy-reviewer + re-open §6.
7. A future paged/filtered `list_concerns_page` RPC, key rotation in scope, or any move of data off ca-central-1 / new subprocessor → re-open the relevant DFD + §6.

---

## §3.17 — Phase 2b live E2EE REPRISAL workflow + 4-eyes status-approval + forensic-reveal break-glass (ADR-0028)

Source: threat-modeler pass 2026-06-22, gating **HG-REPRISAL-PHASE2B**, driven by ADR-0028 (Phase 2b: the live, end-to-end, E2EE reprisal file/read/update/feed loop + the two governance surfaces). Branch: `claude/affectionate-carson-nqB03`. F-range continues from F-156 (no renumbering of prior findings); new findings **F-157…F-167**. The two HIGH-risk surfaces the architect flagged — (i) the **forensic-reveal break-glass** (de-pseudonymization of an audit-log actor in a retaliation context, the single highest-privilege operation in the app) and (ii) the **C4-body residual** (the probe-first stale-key window on `reprisal_read`, the architect's explicit (a)-vs-(b) escalation) — are pinned at **F-157** (forensic break-glass) and **F-162** (C4-body residual + the ruling) and **both require security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign** — F-157 especially at PR2 — per ADR-0028 Decision 9 / the HG-REPRISAL-PHASE2B gate. Verdict: **GO-WITH-CONDITIONS** — every testable mitigation below is implementation-blocking and maps to ADR-0028 AC-1…AC-18.

This pass re-verified the ground truth the architect handed me, file:line, before ruling. Confirmations: `reprisal_read` `RETURNS TABLE(title_ct, body_ct)` with NO `key_id` (`00000000000005_reprisal.sql:204`); audit-before-return on the read (`:222-226`); wrong-passphrase → `sensitive.access_attempt` warn THEN `RETURN` no rows (`:215-219`); not-found → `RETURN` no rows, NO audit (`:211`); the wire collapses both to `data:null` (EF `readReprisal` `r.data?.[0] ?? null`, `core.ts:105`; client `readReprisal` `if (!r.data) return { ok:true, data:null }`, `supabase-reprisal-client.ts:148-149`). Forensic: `reprisal_approve_forensic` self-approve `42501` (`:330`), expiry `P0001` (`:331`), role-pair `42501` (`:332`), reveal (`:334`), the **warn-severity `audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_completed` commits at `:336-341` BEFORE `RETURN v_revealed` at `:342`** — audit-before-reveal confirmed in-band. 4-eyes: `reprisal_approve_status` self-approve `42501` (`:287`), role-pair `42501` (`:288`), atomic flip + completed audit (`:290-297`). EF mapping: `mapRpcError` matches `KNOWN_REASONS.has(error.message)` FIRST so `self_approve_denied`/`role_pair_invalid` reach the client by message even though both carry SQLSTATE `42501`; `42501 → rls_denied` is only the fallback (`core.ts:65-75`). Feed: `reprisal_feed` omits `actor_pseudonym`, carries NO ciphertext, buckets `ts` DOWN to the hour (`:370`), gated `session_is_live() AND is_active_member()` (`:377`), REVOKE PUBLIC/anon (`:378`). The corresponding analysis ground-truth is ADR-0028 (decisions.md) Findings + Decisions 1–9.

### Scope reconciliation against existing entries

- **No new trust boundary.** Every Phase 2b surface rides boundaries already defined in §1. The reprisal ciphertext + the governance ops cross **B2 (E2EE boundary, browser ↔ Edge Functions)** — `reprisal-op` and `t07-op` are facets of B2, not new boundaries. The session-resident plaintext committee data key dwells in **B4 (browser session boundary)** — the EXACT dwell §3.16 F-145/F-146 already pinned for the `CommitteeKeyHolder`. No new region, table-class, subprocessor, audit enum, or retention class (ADR-0028 Compliance check; re-verified — the seven reprisal RPCs + the feed view reuse `reprisal.*` / `audit.forensic_reveal.*` / `sensitive.access_attempt` / `committee_data_key.unwrap`, all on the closed allowlist + ADR-0016 schedule).
- **§3.16 is the verbatim template; Phase 2b CONSUMES its infra, it does not re-introduce a disclosure surface.** F-142 (the `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` disclosure RPC) and F-145/F-146 (the six-trigger heap dwell + no-serialization) were ruled in §3.16 at PR1 and shipped (ADR-0027 PR1). Phase 2b reuses `ensureHolderPopulated` (probe-first, `production-flows.ts:129-182`), `classifyWireFailure` (`:201-219`), the `CommitteeKeyHolder`, and the audit-before-decrypt straight-await pattern (`:460-499`) verbatim. **F-163 below pins "reused, not re-implemented divergently"** — with one MANDATORY adaptation (the reason-first branch, F-160) that is NOT a divergence but a required extension.
- **F-148 (§3.16, the key-material/plaintext leak sweep)** is EXTENDED by AC-8 to the reprisal data key + reprisal plaintext (title/body) + `intake.passphrase` across submit/read/update/feed. **F-161 carries the extension.**
- **F-143 (§3.16, S — JWT/non-member on the unwrap + concern RPCs)** carries forward: both `reprisal-op` and `t07-op` run `assertKeyParity` + `assertSessionLive` + bearer check before dispatch; `_reprisal_gate()` (session_live + active_member) is enforced INSIDE every reprisal RPC (`:209`, `:266`, `:284`, `:310`, `:327`; the feed view body at `:377`). No new ungated op (F-122 grep unaffected — the seven reprisal RPCs all REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role at `:385-393`, and the new `reprisal_list_pending_ops`, F-159, inherits that posture). F-158 pins the gate on the governance RPCs.
- **§3.16 F-149 (the concerns view-widening PI-projection migration) has NO Phase 2b analog.** `reprisal_feed` shipped privacy-correct (no `actor_pseudonym`, no ciphertext, ts bucketed — `:366-379`, re-verified). There is **no F-149-style widening in Phase 2b.** The one new read surface, `reprisal_list_pending_ops` (F-159), is pseudonymized-by-design from inception — it is NOT a widening of an over-disclosing view, it is a new gated, pseudonymized inbox read.

### Data flow (per flow; B2 = browser ↔ Edge Functions, ciphertext + metadata only past the boundary; B4 = browser RAM dwell of the data key)

```
[Flow 0 — Probe-first guard (Decision 6; runs BEFORE any seal/open; mirrors §3.16 Flow 0)]
  Browser -> t07-op committee_key_state { actor_user_id }                  [B2; METADATA only]
  Server: committee_key_state_for_self() -> {key_id, epoch, wrap_count, actor_has_wrap}  (NO ciphertext)
  Browser: if !actor_has_wrap -> render Phase-0a-setup guard; STOP (never hit get_committee_key_wrap_for_self)
  CROSSES B2: metadata only. NEVER any wrap ciphertext. (Governance flows 5-8 do NOT run Flow 0 — no key needed.)

[Flow 1 — Committee-key unwrap (REUSED §3.16 F-142 surface; once per session via the holder)]
  (Identical to §3.16 Flow 1 — Phase 2b adds nothing here. The holder is populated by the SAME
   unwrapCommitteeDataKeyViaProduction; sealed wrap crosses B2, plaintext data_key dwells in B4.)

[Flow 2 — Submit a reprisal (seal client-side; Decision 3)]
  Browser: holder.data_key (cached)  -- ensure populated via Flow 0/1 if null
  Browser: title_ct = sealUtf8(intake.title, data_key)   [secretbox; SHARED concerns/seal.ts, Decision 2]
  Browser: body_ct  = sealUtf8(intake.body,  data_key)   (NO source-name seal — reprisal has no anon mode)
  Browser -> reprisal-op submit { title_ct, body_ct, passphrase: intake.passphrase }   [B2]
  Server: _reprisal_gate(); INSERT reprisal_log (ciphertext cols + per_record_passphrase_hash);
          emit reprisal.created (submitter pseudonym) [one txn]
  CROSSES B2: SEALED title_ct/body_ct + the per-record passphrase (friction gate, F-164). NEVER plaintext title/body.

[Flow 3 — Audited C4 read (audit-before-return SERVER-enforced; Decision 3; the load-bearing read)]
  Browser -> reprisal-op read { id, passphrase }                          [B2]
  Server: reprisal_read(): _reprisal_gate(); row-not-found -> RETURN no rows, NO audit (:211);
          wrong/absent passphrase on a protected row -> emit sensitive.access_attempt warn (:215-218)
                                                        THEN RETURN no rows (:219);
          correct passphrase -> emit reprisal.read (:222-225) BEFORE RETURN QUERY title_ct,body_ct (:226)
  Browser: data === null (covers BOTH wrong-passphrase AND not-found — the wire cannot distinguish, :105/:148)
             -> { status: 'unavailable' }; NEVER attempt decrypt on null (F-165)
           else openUtf8(title_ct)+openUtf8(body_ct) under holder.data_key in try/catch (render scope only)
  CROSSES B2: SEALED title_ct/body_ct (or null). Audit row commits even if the response is dropped.

[Flow 4 — Feed read (NO ciphertext, NO actor — C3 trivial; Decision 3)]
  Browser -> reprisal-op list_feed {}                                     [B2]
  Server: SELECT from reprisal_feed (:366-379): {id, event_type, ts_bucketed_to_hour, target_id,
          target_class, prev_hash, hash}  -- NO actor_pseudonym, NO ciphertext; ts bucketed to hour
  Browser: render rows directly. NO openUtf8, NO holder, NO unwrap (F-166).
  CROSSES B2: pseudonymized non-PI metadata only. NEVER an actor identity, NEVER ciphertext.

[Flow 5 — 4-eyes status PROPOSE (Decision 4)]
  Browser -> reprisal-op propose_status { reprisal_id, new_status }       [B2]
  Server: reprisal_propose_status(): _reprisal_gate(); validate status enum (:267);
          INSERT pending_four_eyes_ops(status_flip, proposer_id=auth.uid()) ; emit ...4eyes_pending (:271-274)
  CROSSES B2: status enum + reprisal_id + pending_id. NO key material, NO ciphertext.

[Flow 6 — 4-eyes status APPROVE (server-enforced 4-eyes; Decision 4)]
  Browser -> reprisal-op approve_status { pending_id }                    [B2]
  Server: reprisal_approve_status(): _reprisal_gate(); FOR UPDATE lock;
          proposer == approver -> RAISE self_approve_denied 42501 (:287)
          NOT _reprisal_valid_pair -> RAISE role_pair_invalid 42501 (:288)
          else flip status + emit ...4eyes_completed (proposer+approver pseudonyms) [one txn] (:290-297)
  CROSSES B2: pending_id. The two 403 reasons are discriminated by MESSAGE, not status (F-160).

[Flow 7 — Forensic-reveal PROPOSE (the break-glass request; Decision 4)]
  Browser -> reprisal-op propose_forensic { audit_log_id, reveal_reason }  [B2]
  Server: reprisal_propose_forensic(): _reprisal_gate();
          INSERT pending_four_eyes_ops(forensic_reveal, expires_at = now()+24h) (:311-313)
          emit audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_pending SEVERITY=warn (reveal_reason in meta) (:314-317)
  CROSSES B2: audit_log_id + reveal_reason (operational justification). NO identity revealed yet.

[Flow 8 — Forensic-reveal APPROVE (HIGHEST-privilege op; audit-before-reveal; Decision 4 / F-157)]
  Browser -> reprisal-op approve_forensic { pending_id }                   [B2]
  Server: reprisal_approve_forensic(): _reprisal_gate(); FOR UPDATE;
          self-approve -> RAISE self_approve_denied 42501 (:330)
          now() > expires_at -> RAISE expired P0001 (:331)         -- 24h live guard
          NOT _reprisal_valid_pair -> RAISE role_pair_invalid 42501 (:332)
          v_revealed := jhsc_forensic_reveal_actor_pseudonym(target_id) (:334)
          persist revealed_actor_pseudonym + emit audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_completed WARN (:336-341)
          RETURN v_revealed (:342)            <-- the warn-audit COMMITS BEFORE this RETURN
  Browser: AWAIT the response (load-bearing — the await guarantees the warn-audit landed before
           the pseudonym is surfaceable); render the de-pseudonymized actor ONLY in modal-local state,
           role=status, cleared on close/unmount; NEVER cached/logged/persisted/in-URL (F-157).
  CROSSES B2: the de-pseudonymized actor pseudonym (a string), authorized + audited + time-boxed.
              This is the ONE flow where an actor identity crosses B2 — by deliberate break-glass design.
```

**PI classification per store / transit path (Phase 2b deltas only; §3.16's committee-key + concern rows unchanged):**

| Surface | Classification | At rest where | Crosses B2 as | Residency | Retention |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| `reprisal_log.title_ct` / `body_ct` | PI / sensitive (OHSA s.50 reprisal allegation content — the HIGHEST-harm record in the system) — sealed | Postgres `reprisal_log` (C4) | SEALED secretbox ct (Flows 2/3) | ca-central-1 (ADR-0001) | existing `reprisal.*` enum + ADR-0016; **no new class** |
| Plaintext reprisal title/body | PI / sensitive | **Browser render scope only** (transient) — never persisted/logged | NEVER crosses B2 in plaintext | n/a | render-scoped (GC'd with view) |
| `reprisal_log.per_record_passphrase_hash` | Derived secret (crypt hash; the UX-friction gate, NOT the crypto gate) | Postgres `reprisal_log` (C4) | the passphrase crosses B2 at submit/read (F-164); the HASH never leaves | ca-central-1 | with the row; **no new class** |
| `reprisal_feed` projection | Pseudonymized non-PI metadata (event_type, ts bucketed to hour, target_id, hashes — NO actor) | derived in view (not stored) | pseudonymized metadata (Flow 4) | ca-central-1 | derived; no storage |
| `pending_four_eyes_ops.reveal_reason` | Operational justification (free text — NOT a PI field about a user; the requester's stated reason) | Postgres `pending_four_eyes_ops` | reveal_reason at propose (Flow 7) + in the warn audit meta | ca-central-1 | with the pending op + ADR-0016 audit schedule; **no new class** |
| `reprisal_list_pending_ops` projection (NEW, F-159) | Pseudonymized inbox metadata (pseudonymized proposer, kind, target, status/reason, created/expires — NO raw proposer_id, NO revealed pseudonym, NO ciphertext) | derived in fn (not stored) | pseudonymized metadata | ca-central-1 | derived; no storage |
| `revealed_actor_pseudonym` (the de-pseudonymized actor) | **The highest-sensitivity transient in the app** — an audit actor's identity de-pseudonymized in a retaliation context | `pending_four_eyes_ops.revealed_actor_pseudonym` for ≤24h (cleared by `expire_forensic_reveals()` `:347-358`) | the pseudonym crosses B2 on Flow 8 approve ONLY | ca-central-1 | **≤24h, server-enforced** — the expiry re-check (`:331`) + the sweep (`:347-358`); UI: modal-local, cleared on close (F-157) |
| Plaintext committee data key | Secret (32-byte symmetric key) | **Browser RAM only** (the SHIPPED `CommitteeKeyHolder`, §3.16 F-145) | NEVER crosses B2 | n/a (device-resident) | session-scoped; wiped on the 6 triggers (§3.16 F-145) — REUSED, not re-introduced |

**No name/email/phone is newly collected by Phase 2b.** No new PI field; `reveal_reason` is operational justification, not a new attribute about a user (constraints.md hard rule 6 N/A — confirmed). The reprisal-content purpose is the established **OHSA s.50 anti-reprisal register** (ADR-0003/0004 purpose, unchanged). The one genuinely new disclosure is the **forensic de-pseudonymization** — assessed at F-157 and §6 as a deliberate, authorized, audited, 4-eyes, ≤24h break-glass, NOT a new ambient collection and NOT a breach.

### Spoofing (S)

#### F-158 | S | Forged/replayed JWT or a non-member drives a reprisal C4 read, a status approve, or — gravest — a forensic reveal

Every Phase 2b RPC crosses B2 bearing the caller's mint-session JWT. A stolen/forged/replayed JWT (A4) or a non-member could attempt to read a C4 reprisal body, approve a status flip, or — the gravest — propose/approve a forensic de-pseudonymization under an attacker-asserted identity. The forensic reveal makes the spoofing impact materially higher than concerns: a spoofed approver in a valid role-pair could unmask a retaliation-context actor.

- **Affected:** all seven reprisal RPCs via `reprisal-op` (`reprisal_read` `:203`, `reprisal_approve_status` `:278`, `reprisal_approve_forensic` `:321`, etc.) + the new `reprisal_list_pending_ops` (F-159); `t07-op committee_key_state`/`get_key_wrap` (REUSED §3.16). All through `serveWithCors` + `assertKeyParity` + `assertSessionLive` + bearer check before dispatch.
- **Likelihood:** LOW (mitigated by the existing auth stack — §3.16 F-143 carry-forward). **Impact:** HIGH (C4 reprisal body + the forensic surface). **Priority:** MEDIUM (mitigated by inherited controls; pinned for the governance RPCs).
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) `serveWithCors` origin allowlist; (2) `assertKeyParity` 503s on parity mismatch (§3.14 F-124–F-126); (3) `assertSessionLive` / `session_is_live()` denies a revoked-but-unexpired JWT within ≤5s (§3.14 F-116/F-121); (4) F-117 — `auth.uid()` is server-resolved from the verified assertion, never from the request body, so the JWT cannot assert an arbitrary uid (this is WHY `reprisal_propose_status` sets `proposer_id = auth.uid()` `:269` and the approve compares `v_p.proposer_id = v_actor` `:287`/`:330` against the server-resolved actor — the 4-eyes self-approve check is un-spoofable from the body); (5) `_reprisal_gate()` (session_live + active_member) enforced INSIDE every reprisal RPC (`:209`/`:266`/`:284`/`:310`/`:327`) and the feed view body (`:377`); (6) all seven RPCs REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role (`:385-393`). No new uid-bearing input; no new ungated op (F-122 grep unaffected).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-6 / AC-11 / AC-12 / AC-16):**
  - _pgTAP (live-stack non-member gate):_ a NON-active-member call to each of `reprisal_read` / `reprisal_approve_status` / `reprisal_approve_forensic` / `reprisal_list_pending_ops` raises the `_reprisal_gate()` exception and performs NO side effect (no ciphertext, no flip, no reveal, no inbox rows) — assert the gate fires before any `RETURN`/`RAISE`-of-result.
  - _pgTAP (server-resolved actor — un-spoofable self-approve):_ assert `reprisal_approve_status`/`reprisal_approve_forensic` compare `v_p.proposer_id` against `auth.uid()` (`:287`/`:330`), NOT against any body field — a request cannot assert a different approver identity to bypass self-approve (cross-ref AC-11/AC-16).
  - _vitest (401 vs 403 split, REUSED §3.16):_ any reprisal-op call returning HTTP 401 surfaces session_expiry and fires `onSessionRevoked` (which wipes the holder, §3.16 F-145); HTTP 403 is handled WITHOUT wiping the holder or clearing the JWT (AC-6). (For 403 reason discrimination see F-160.)
  - _carry-forward (no new test owed):_ `assertSessionLive` + `assertKeyParity` on both EFs covered by §3.14 F-121/F-126 live-stack tests; Phase 2b inherits them.

### Tampering (T)

#### F-167 | T | Reprisal ciphertext modified in transit, or the shared `seal.ts` extraction silently changes the seal bytes

The seal/open compositions cross B2 with secretbox ciphertext. In-transit tampering (mitigated by TLS) surfaces as a decrypt failure (good, fail-closed). The Phase-2b-specific hazard is the **seal-extraction tidy** (Decision 2): `concerns/seal.ts` is moved/re-exported to a shared `crypto/committee-seal.ts` barrel and consumed by BOTH concerns and reprisal. If the move altered the byte format (`[nonce(24)][secretbox_easy ct]`) or the AEAD behaviour, it would (a) break concerns' already-shipped ciphertext compatibility and (b) introduce a divergent reprisal seal. The data-key-by-reference handoff hazard (§3.16 F-147) is inherited unchanged — the holder is the sole owner.

- **Affected:** the shared `sealUtf8`/`openUtf8` (post-extraction `crypto/committee-seal.ts`); the reprisal compositions in `reprisal/production-flows.ts`; the inherited single-buffer-by-reference holder handoff (§3.16 F-147).
- **Likelihood:** LOW. **Impact:** MEDIUM (a botched extraction breaks concerns interop or forks the reprisal seal; tampered ciphertext is fail-closed by AEAD). **Priority:** MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) secretbox is authenticated (AEAD) — tampered `title_ct`/`body_ct` fails open-verify, never silently mis-decrypts; (2) the extraction is a re-export / physical-move-plus-re-export with ZERO behaviour change — the seal bytes are unchanged, so the pinned-hex KAT (patterns.md) and the existing concern-core seal tests stay green (Decision 2); (3) the data key is handed to the holder by reference; the seal fns read it but do not store a second alias (§3.16 F-147, inherited).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-1 / AC-8):**
  - _vitest (extraction is byte-identical — the KAT gate):_ the pinned-hex KAT over `sealUtf8`/`openUtf8` and the existing `concern-core` seal tests pass UNCHANGED after the move/re-export — assert the seal output for a fixed (plaintext, key, nonce) is byte-for-byte the pre-extraction value (no seal-format drift across the two consumers).
  - _vitest (reprisal round-trip under the shared seal):_ `submitReprisalViaProduction` seals title/body via the shared seal; opening the persisted ciphertext with the same committee key yields the original plaintext (AC-1) — proves reprisal uses the IDENTICAL scheme, not a fork.
  - _vitest (decrypt-fail is fail-closed):_ a corrupted `reprisal_log.title_ct`/`body_ct` causes `openUtf8` to surface a typed `decrypt_failed`, never a thrown raw exception leaking key/plaintext bytes (cross-ref F-161, the F-148 carry-forward).

### Repudiation (R)

#### F-158-R [tracked under F-157/F-158] — see the forensic audit-before-reveal (F-157) and the 4-eyes completed-audit (F-160)

The Phase 2b repudiation surface is fully covered by the audit-before-side-effect findings: the forensic reveal's warn-audit-before-return (F-157), the 4-eyes `...4eyes_completed` server-emitted attribution (F-160), and the C4 read's `reprisal.read`-before-ciphertext (F-165). All audit rows are emitted SERVER-SIDE inside SECURITY DEFINER SQL, atomically — the client cannot forge or suppress them, and the compositions emit NO client-side audit (the §3.16 F-151 "client emits nothing" invariant carries forward). No standalone R finding is owed; the load-bearing repudiation assertions live in F-157/F-160/F-165 to keep them adjacent to the operations they witness.

### Information disclosure (I)

#### F-157 | I/E | HIGH — the FORENSIC-REVEAL break-glass: de-pseudonymization of a retaliation-context actor (the highest-privilege operation in the app)

**`reprisal_approve_forensic` de-pseudonymizes an `audit_log` actor — the retaliation-context identity — and returns it across B2 for ≤24h.** This is the single highest-harm operation in the system: a leaked, cached, or prematurely-surfaced reveal exposes WHO took an action in a reprisal investigation, exactly the identity OHSA s.50 protects. The disclosure risks: (1) the client surfaces the pseudonym BEFORE the warn-audit of the de-pseudonymization commits (audit-before-reveal broken end-to-end); (2) the revealed pseudonym is CACHED past the modal (Svelte store, localStorage, URL, list-row cache, log) and survives the intended ≤24h modal-local lifetime; (3) the 24h expiry is honored server-side but the UI lets a stale reveal be re-surfaced; (4) a client bypass of role-pair / self-approve. **Security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign required at PR2** (the architect's PR2-weighting rationale, ADR-0028 Decision 7).

- **Affected:** `reprisal_approve_forensic` (`:321-343`); `approveForensicViaProduction` (the load-bearing await, Decision 4); the forensic-reveal break-glass UI (Decision 5: modal-local state, `role=status`, clear-on-close); `SupabaseReprisalClient.approveForensicReveal` (`:234-241`, returns `{ revealed_actor_pseudonym: string | null }`).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (every gate is server-enforced; the UI no-cache is required + tested). **Impact:** HIGH (an unmasked retaliation-context actor — the worst confidentiality outcome in the threat model; blast radius = a named individual exposed to potential s.50 reprisal). **Priority:** HIGH — flagged for PR2 co-sign.
- **Existing/required mitigation (server gates re-verified this pass; client invariants required):**
  1. **Server-enforced 4-eyes — the client CANNOT bypass.** `reprisal_approve_forensic` enforces, in order, inside one SECURITY DEFINER txn under a `FOR UPDATE` lock: self-approve `RAISE self_approve_denied USING ERRCODE='42501'` (`:330`); 24h expiry re-check `IF now() > v_p.expires_at THEN RAISE expired USING ERRCODE='P0001'` (`:331`); role-pair `IF NOT _reprisal_valid_pair(...) THEN RAISE role_pair_invalid USING ERRCODE='42501'` (`:332`, = co-chair+co-chair OR co-chair+certified). The composition is a thin typed wrapper — there is NO client path to the reveal that skips these (the de-pseudonymization `jhsc_forensic_reveal_actor_pseudonym` `:334` runs only AFTER all three pass).
  2. **Audit-BEFORE-reveal, in-band + enforced by the composition's await.** The warn-severity `audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_completed` commits at `:336-341` BEFORE `RETURN v_revealed` at `:342` — the warn-audit of a de-pseudonymization lands before the identity leaves the function (the same invariant as `reprisal_read` `:222-226`, mirroring `reveal_concern_source` §3.16 F-150). The composition uses straight `async/await` (NO eager `.then()`-then-paint) so the client cannot surface the pseudonym before the awaited response resolves — i.e. before the audit committed.
  3. **The revealed pseudonym is modal-local and NEVER cached.** The composition returns the pseudonym BY VALUE and holds NO module-level reference (Decision 4). The UI renders it ONLY in the modal's local component state, in a `role=status` region, and CLEARS it on modal close / route-leave / unmount (mirror the concerns reveal-clear, `routes/concerns/+page.svelte:196-206`). It is NEVER written to a Svelte store outliving the modal, to `localStorage`/`sessionStorage`/URL, to a list-row cache, or to any log line.
  4. **24h expiry honored on display.** The server re-checks expiry on approve (`:331` → `expired`); the UI ALSO greys/disables the Approve affordance once `now() > expires_at` (from the pending op's `expires_at`) and surfaces the typed `expired` as "this reveal request expired (24h limit) — file a new request." The sweep `expire_forensic_reveals()` (`:347-358`) clears `revealed_actor_pseudonym` past the window.
  5. **`null` revealed pseudonym** (target audit row already retention-wiped) renders "the referenced audit record is no longer available" — no decrypt, no error leaking state.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-14 / AC-15 / AC-16 / AC-17 — HIGH; vitest + pgTAP):**
  - _vitest (audit-before-reveal — the load-bearing assertion, AC-15):_ on `approveForensicViaProduction`, assert the `audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_completed` (severity=warn) audit-spy fires BEFORE the composition resolves the pseudonym — the client does NOT surface `revealed_actor_pseudonym` until the awaited RPC resolves (straight await; no eager paint). Mirror the AC-2 reprisal-read audit-before-return assertion.
  - _vitest (revealed pseudonym NOT cached past the modal, AC-17 — a leak-sweep over post-close state):_ after a successful forensic approve, assert the revealed pseudonym exists ONLY in the modal's local state; after modal close / route-leave / unmount, assert it is absent from the DOM, from any reachable JS state, from any Svelte store outliving the modal, from `localStorage`/`sessionStorage`/URL, from any list-row cache, and from every captured log line. (Extends the F-161 leak sweep with a post-close scan.)
  - _vitest (24h expiry honored on display, AC-14):_ `approveForensicViaProduction` on a pending op past `expires_at` returns `{ status: 'expired' }` (server `:331`, HTTP 409); the UI disabled the Approve affordance once `now() > expires_at` (assert the affordance is greyed/disabled before the call when expired).
  - _vitest (self-approve / role-pair distinct, AC-16):_ self-approve → `{ status: 'self_approve_denied' }` (server `:330`); a member outside the co-chair/certified pairing → `{ status: 'role_pair_invalid' }` (server `:332`); both HTTP 403, discriminated by reason (cross-ref F-160).
  - _vitest (null reveal):_ a `revealed_actor_pseudonym === null` renders "the referenced audit record is no longer available" and performs no decrypt / no error.
  - _pgTAP (server gates structural):_ assert `reprisal_approve_forensic` RAISEs self_approve_denied/expired/role_pair_invalid in that order before `jhsc_forensic_reveal_actor_pseudonym` is called, and that the warn `...4eyes_completed` `audit_emit` is ordered BEFORE `RETURN v_revealed` (inject-failure pattern mirroring the §3.16 F-151 / `reveal_concern_source` audit-before-return pgTAP).

#### F-159 | I | The new `reprisal_list_pending_ops` inbox read — must be pseudonymized, gated, and leak no raw proposer / no revealed pseudonym

The approvals inbox (Decision 5) needs a source of pending ops, but there is NO `pending_four_eyes_ops` read RPC today (the table REVOKEs SELECT from authenticated; only the propose/approve SECURITY DEFINER fns touch it — confirmed `00000000000005_reprisal.sql:78`). PR2 adds a minimal `reprisal_list_pending_ops()` SECURITY DEFINER read. The threat: this NEW read surface must project ONLY pseudonymized, non-sensitive inbox metadata — leaking the raw `proposer_id` (re-identifiable vs `committee_membership`) or, far worse, the `revealed_actor_pseudonym` (the de-pseudonymized forensic identity) through the inbox would defeat F-157. This is the only new migration Phase 2b proposes (PR2 only). **threat-modeler co-sign at P2b-5** (LOW-risk relative to F-157 — no key material, no C4 body, no raw actor — but a NEW read surface).

- **Affected:** the new `reprisal_list_pending_ops()` migration (P2b-5); the approvals-inbox UI (Decision 5); the inbox client read.
- **Likelihood:** n/a (this is a new projection contract, not an attack); MEDIUM-negative if the projection is botched. **Impact:** MEDIUM (a botched projection leaks the raw proposer uuid; a catastrophic one leaks the revealed pseudonym → folds into F-157 HIGH). **Priority:** MEDIUM (new read surface — flagged).
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the read is gated `_reprisal_gate()` (session_live + active_member) — same gate as every reprisal RPC; (2) it projects `{ id, kind, target_id, new_status, reveal_reason, proposer_actor_pseudonym, created_at, expires_at }` — **pseudonymized proposer (`_committee_pseudonym(proposer_id)`), NO raw `proposer_id`, NO `revealed_actor_pseudonym`, NO ciphertext** (mirrors the `reprisal_feed` privacy posture, §3.17 ground truth); (3) REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role + GRANT authenticated/supabase_auth_admin (same as the seven existing RPCs `:385-393`).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-18 — pgTAP):**
  - _pgTAP (pseudonymized projection):_ assert `reprisal_list_pending_ops` returns `proposer_actor_pseudonym` = `_committee_pseudonym(proposer_id)` and the result column set does NOT include raw `proposer_id`, does NOT include `revealed_actor_pseudonym`, and includes NO ciphertext column (structural absence, mirroring the §3.16 F-149 raw-actor-absent assertion).
  - _pgTAP (grants + gate):_ assert EXECUTE is REVOKED from PUBLIC/anon/service_role and GRANTED to authenticated + supabase_auth_admin; a non-member (gate fails) call raises the `_reprisal_gate()` exception and returns no rows.
  - _pgTAP (no forensic identity ever in the inbox):_ seed a COMPLETED forensic op (with a `revealed_actor_pseudonym` set) and assert `reprisal_list_pending_ops` NEVER returns that revealed pseudonym in any column — the inbox read cannot become a second path to the de-pseudonymized identity (folds into F-157).

#### F-160 | I | The two 403 governance reasons (`self_approve_denied` vs `role_pair_invalid`) must be discriminated WITHOUT leaking other members' identities — and a verbatim copy of the concerns `classifyWireFailure` would erase them

`self_approve_denied` and `role_pair_invalid` are BOTH HTTP 403 but carry distinct RAISE messages (both SQLSTATE `42501`); the EF `mapRpcError` matches `KNOWN_REASONS.has(error.message)` FIRST, so both reasons reach the client (`core.ts:65-75`, re-verified — `42501 → rls_denied` is only the fallback for an unknown message). The threat is twofold: (1) the concerns `classifyWireFailure` collapses `status === 403` to a generic `rls_denied` (`production-flows.ts:212-213`) — copying it VERBATIM into the reprisal compositions would ERASE the governance-meaningful distinction the UI must show, surfacing both as generic-forbidden (this is the architect's Decision 4 "reason-first" mandate, and a real divergence-risk if missed); (2) the distinct copy must NOT leak WHO the other approver/proposer is (e.g. "you can't approve — member X already proposed") — the discrimination is about the CALLER's relationship to the op, not a disclosure of other members' identities.

- **Affected:** the reprisal `classifyWireFailure` (must branch on `reason` BEFORE status, NOT a verbatim concerns copy); `approveStatusViaProduction` / `approveForensicViaProduction` typed unions; the governance UI copy.
- **Likelihood:** MEDIUM (a verbatim copy of the concerns helper is the natural, wrong, default). **Impact:** LOW-MEDIUM (erased distinction degrades the governance UX + could mask a role-misconfiguration; no PI leak if the copy is reason-only). **Priority:** MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the reprisal `classifyWireFailure` branches on `reason` FIRST — `self_approve_denied` / `role_pair_invalid` / `expired` are surfaced as DISTINCT typed values BEFORE any generic `status === 403 → rls_denied` fallback (Decision 4); (2) the server already discriminates by message (`core.ts:67`), so the distinction is available — the composition must not throw it away; (3) the UI copy is relationship-scoped, NOT identity-disclosing: `self_approve_denied` → "you can't approve your own proposal"; `role_pair_invalid` → "your role can't approve this — a co-chair pairing is required" — NEITHER names the other party; (4) the inbox suppresses the Approve affordance on a self-proposed op (F-157 mitigation 1 / affordance-suppression — a UI mirror of the server gate, not the only defense).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-11 / AC-12 / AC-16):**
  - _vitest (reason-first discrimination, AC-12):_ `approveStatusViaProduction` by a member outside the pairing returns the DISTINCT typed `{ status: 'role_pair_invalid' }`, NOT a generic `rls_denied` — assert the discrimination is on `reason` (both being HTTP 403). The same for `approveForensicViaProduction` (AC-16).
  - _vitest (self-approve distinct, AC-11):_ `approveStatusViaProduction` where the approver IS the proposer returns `{ status: 'self_approve_denied' }` (server `:287`), distinct from `role_pair_invalid`.
  - _vitest (copy is identity-safe):_ assert the surfaced copy for both reasons contains NO other member's id/pseudonym/name — only the caller-relationship message (a string-content assertion over the two error copies).
  - _vitest (affordance-suppression, AC-11):_ the inbox NEVER renders an Approve button on an op the current `user_id` proposed (UI mirror of the server gate).

#### F-161 | I | Reprisal data key, reprisal plaintext, or the per-record passphrase leaks into logs, errors, audit-meta, storage, or URL

Phase 2b handles, transiently in the browser: the plaintext 32-byte committee data key (session-resident, §3.16 F-145 — REUSED), plaintext reprisal title/body (render scope), and the per-record passphrase (forwarded at submit/read). Any landing in `console.*`, a thrown error message/stack, the structured-log path, an audit `meta`, sessionStorage/localStorage/IndexedDB, or a URL is a confidentiality break (A4/A5). The reprisal title/body is the HIGHEST-harm plaintext in the system; the passphrase is a credential-class value. This EXTENDS the §3.16 F-148 / §3.15 F-132 leak-sweep gate to the reprisal surfaces.

- **Affected:** `submitReprisalViaProduction` / `readReprisalViaProduction` / `updateReprisalViaProduction` / `listReprisalFeedViaProduction`; the shared seal; the inherited `CommitteeKeyHolder`; all error/toast/log surfaces touched by the reprisal flows; the EF reason-only logging (`functions/reprisal-op/index.ts:142-146`, closed-literal reasons — re-confirm no PI).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (mitigated by the leak-sweep gate). **Impact:** HIGH (a leak of the data key defeats the E2EE model; a leak of reprisal plaintext/passphrase exposes the highest-harm content; ADR-0003 Invariants 1/5). **Priority:** HIGH.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the data key exists in plaintext ONLY in the heap holder, NEVER serialized (§3.16 F-145/F-146, REUSED); (2) plaintext reprisal title/body exist ONLY in render scope, NEVER persisted/logged (Decision 3); (3) `intake.passphrase` is forwarded verbatim to the transport (the F-34 friction gate) and NEVER logged — it is a credential-class value (constraints.md Secrets handling / logging hygiene); (4) every decrypt is in try/catch surfacing a typed `decrypt_failed`, NEVER the raw libsodium error (the F-148 no-buffer-bytes property — C3/F-148 carry-forward); (5) the SEALED ciphertext is what crosses the wire (Flows 2/3); (6) audit emission is server-owned — the client cannot put key material/plaintext/passphrase into audit meta; (7) the EF logs closed-literal reasons only (`index.ts:142-146`).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-8 — extends the §3.16 F-148 / §3.15 F-132 leak-sweep CI gate):**
  - _vitest (full-workflow leak sweep):_ instrument `console.*`, captured thrown-error `.message`/`.stack`, the structured-log emit surface (`apps/web/src/lib/log/`), and any client-constructed audit `meta`; run submit + read + update + feed (happy path + each error branch); assert NONE of {the 32 plaintext data-key bytes, the identity privkey bytes, any plaintext reprisal title/body string, the `intake.passphrase` string} appears in any captured surface (AC-8).
  - _vitest (no serialization, REUSED §3.16):_ assert the data key is NOT readable from `sessionStorage`/`localStorage`/IndexedDB/URL/any serialized store at any point (§3.16 F-146 invariant, re-asserted for the reprisal path).
  - _vitest (decrypt-fail surfaces typed, no bytes):_ a corrupted `title_ct`/`body_ct` yields a typed `decrypt_failed`, with NO libsodium error bytes / NO key / NO plaintext in the thrown message (cross-ref F-167).
  - _CI grep (uniformity):_ extend the existing key-material-leak grep to flag any reprisal path passing the data-key buffer, the privkey, a plaintext reprisal field, or `intake.passphrase` into a log/toast/error/audit-meta constructor (AC-8 as a CI gate, P2b-4).

#### F-165 | I | Audited C4 read — client decrypts before the `reprisal.read` audit lands, or decrypts on the null (wrong-passphrase / not-found) the wire cannot substantiate
