`reprisal_read` emits `reprisal.read` BEFORE returning the ciphertext (`:222-226`); the wrong/absent-passphrase path emits `sensitive.access_attempt` warn THEN returns no rows (`:215-219`), and not-found returns no rows with no audit (`:211`). The wire collapses both no-row cases to `data:null` (`core.ts:105` / `supabase-reprisal-client.ts:148-149`). Two end-to-end threats: (1) the composition `openUtf8`s before the `reprisal.read` audit commits (audit-before-return broken end-to-end — an unwitnessed C4 read); (2) the composition attempts a decrypt on the `null` — which would be a crash/undefined behaviour AND would mean inventing an `invalid_passphrase` discrimination the wire CANNOT substantiate (the §3.16-concerns reveal distinguishes a 422 wrong-passphrase; reprisal CANNOT — both wrong-passphrase and not-found are `null`). The honest surfacing is a single `unavailable`.

- **Affected:** `readReprisalViaProduction` (the audited C4 read, Decision 3); `reprisal_read` (server audit-before-return `:222-226`); the `unavailable` UI copy.
- **Likelihood:** LOW. **Impact:** HIGH (an unwitnessed C4-body read, or a decrypt-on-null crash leaking state). **Priority:** MEDIUM-HIGH — flagged (the audited C4 read is the load-bearing PR1 surface).
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the composition uses straight `await` on `reprisalClient.readReprisal` — the SERVER emits `reprisal.read` BEFORE returning ciphertext (`:222-226`), so the awaited resolve is AFTER the audit committed (no eager `.then()`-then-decrypt); (2) **if `data === null` the composition returns `{ status: 'unavailable' }` and NEVER attempts `openUtf8`** — the null covers BOTH wrong-passphrase AND not-found, which the wire cannot distinguish (Findings); the wrong-passphrase case is STILL audited server-side (`sensitive.access_attempt`, `:215-218`) — the friction gate works, only the client-facing discrimination is coarser; (3) the composition surfaces a single honest `unavailable` rather than inventing an `invalid_passphrase` the wire can't substantiate — the UI copy says "no record was returned — check the passphrase if this record is protected" (covers both without leaking which); (4) the per-record passphrase is the UX-friction gate, NOT the crypto gate (F-164).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-2 / AC-3):**
  - _vitest (audit-before-decrypt end-to-end, AC-2):_ on `readReprisalViaProduction` of a readable record, assert the `reprisal.read` audit-spy fires BEFORE the composition resolves the plaintext; the client does NOT call `openUtf8` until the read RPC resolves (mirror the §3.16 F-150 audit-before-decrypt assertion).
  - _vitest (never decrypt on null, AC-3):_ a wrong/absent passphrase on a protected record yields `data:null`; `readReprisalViaProduction` returns `{ status: 'unavailable' }` and makes NO `openUtf8` call (assert the decrypt path is not entered). NOT-found yields the SAME `{ status: 'unavailable' }` — assert both map IDENTICALLY (the wire cannot distinguish).
  - _vitest (no invented invalid_passphrase):_ assert the composition NEVER returns an `invalid_passphrase` discriminant on a null read (the wire cannot substantiate it) — only `unavailable`.
  - _pgTAP (server friction gate + audit-before-return, carry-forward):_ assert `reprisal_read` emits `sensitive.access_attempt` on a wrong passphrase THEN returns no rows (`:215-219`), and emits `reprisal.read` BEFORE `RETURN QUERY` on the happy path (`:222-226`); not-found emits NO audit (`:211`).

#### F-166 | I | The reprisal feed — confirm NO ciphertext, NO actor, no holder/unwrap on a feed read (C3 trivially satisfied)

`reprisal_feed` is ALREADY pseudonymized (no `actor_pseudonym`, no ciphertext, ts bucketed to the hour, gated — `:366-379`, re-verified). C3 is trivially satisfied: there is no decrypt, no holder, no key material in play on the feed path. The threat is a regression: a future feed change that re-introduces an actor identity or ciphertext, or a composition that needlessly populates the holder (and thus hits the disclosure RPC) for a feed read.

- **Affected:** `reprisal_feed` view (`:366-379`); `listReprisalFeedViaProduction` (must NOT call `ensureHolderPopulated`); the `ReprisalFeedRow` client shape (`:98-107`).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (the view shipped privacy-correct). **Impact:** MEDIUM (a regression re-introducing an actor/ciphertext on the feed). **Priority:** LOW-MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the view projects ONLY `{id, event_type, ts_bucketed_to_hour, target_id, target_class, prev_hash, hash}` — NO `actor_pseudonym`, NO ciphertext, ts bucketed DOWN to the hour (`:370`); (2) `listReprisalFeedViaProduction` does NOT call `ensureHolderPopulated` — no key required, the disclosure RPC is NOT hit on a feed read (Decision 3); (3) it still uses `classifyWireFailure` for 401-wipe consistency (a 401 on the feed is a session event); (4) the view is gated `session_is_live() AND is_active_member()` in its body (`:377`) + REVOKE PUBLIC/anon (`:378`).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-4):**
  - _vitest (feed has no ciphertext / no actor, AC-4):_ `listReprisalFeedViaProduction` returns `ReprisalFeedRow[]` with `ts_bucketed_to_hour`, NO `actor_pseudonym` field, NO ciphertext field; assert no `openUtf8` is ever called and `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` is NOT hit on a feed read (no holder/unwrap).
  - _pgTAP (view projection structural):_ assert the `reprisal_feed` column set excludes `actor_pseudonym` and any `*_ct` column, includes `ts_bucketed_to_hour`, and the body buckets `ts` to the hour (`date_trunc('hour', ...)`, `:370`) — a regression guard against re-introducing an actor/ciphertext.

### Denial of service (D)

#### F-160-D [tracked under F-158 / §3.16 F-153] — governance RPCs as DoS surfaces

The governance RPCs (`propose/approve_status`, `propose/approve_forensic`, `reprisal_list_pending_ops`) are authenticated + `_reprisal_gate()`-gated (active-member only — not anonymously reachable; A4 external flood blocked at B1). Each is a single indexed read/update + one audit emit; no fan-out, no amplification. A member spamming a propose/approve inflates their OWN attributable audit rows (self-limited, attributable) — the accepted-residual posture from §3.16 F-153 carries forward unchanged. The forensic propose creates a 24h-expiring pending op; a flood of proposes is bounded by the same auth/gate controls and is fully attributable. No new DoS control is owed; no standalone D finding beyond the §3.16 F-153 carry-forward.

- _Testable mitigation (carry-forward):_ pgTAP — assert each governance RPC body is a single self-scoped read/update (no join fan-out, no loop), structural, preventing an amplification regression (mirror §3.16 F-153).

### Elevation of privilege (E)

#### F-162 | E | HIGH — the C4-body residual: the probe-first stale-key window on `reprisal_read` (the architect's explicit (a)-vs-(b) escalation — RULED)

The carry-forward C4 invariant says "every ciphertext-returning RPC response MUST include `key_id` so `onKeyRotationObserved` fires before reuse." Ground truth (re-verified): the only reprisal ciphertext-returning RPC, `reprisal_read`, returns `TABLE(title_ct, body_ct)` with NO `key_id` (`:204`). ADR-0028 Decision 1 chose option (a) — satisfy C4 structurally via the probe-first `ensureHolderPopulated` + a defensive optional `key_id?` passthrough, NO migration — and **explicitly handed me the (a)-vs-(b) escalation**: rule whether (a) is acceptable for this HIGHER-harm C4 body, or whether the C4 read response MUST carry `key_id` (option (b), a migration widening `reprisal_read` to `RETURNS TABLE(title_ct, body_ct, key_id)`). **This is the second HIGH surface; security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign.**

**The residual:** a single-op stale-key window — if a co-chair on another device rotates the committee key AFTER this session's `ensureHolderPopulated` probe but BEFORE a `reprisal_read` in the SAME already-populated session, the read opens `title_ct`/`body_ct` re-sealed under the new key with the stale cached key, yielding a typed `decrypt_failed` (NOT a silent mis-decrypt — libsodium secretbox is AEAD and throws on a wrong key; the open is wrapped → typed `decrypt_failed`, F-161/F-167). The next op's probe observes the new `key_id` via `onKeyRotationObserved` (`production-flows.ts:149`), wipes, and re-unwraps. This window is IDENTICAL to the one accepted for concerns (§3.16 F-154 / the F-137 stale-key guard).

- **RULING — option (a) is ACCEPTED for the reprisal C4 body; (b) is NOT required.** Reasoning, weighing the higher harm of the C4 reprisal body:
  1. **The window is non-silent and self-healing.** The failure mode is a typed `decrypt_failed` on a SINGLE op (not a silent mis-decrypt, not a disclosure), and the very next op's probe self-heals (wipe + re-unwrap under the new key). There is NO state in which a stale key yields readable-but-wrong plaintext, and NO state in which an actor reads a body they should not — a rotation does not change WHO may read, only under WHICH key the ciphertext is sealed. The residual is an availability blip on one op, not a confidentiality or integrity break.
  2. **Option (a) keeps reprisal byte-for-byte identical to the audited, shipped 2a baseline.** The merged concerns code ALSO emits no server-side `key_id`; concerns satisfies C4 via the probe (`getCommitteeKeyState` → `onKeyRotationObserved(probe.data.key_id)`, `:133`/`:149`) BEFORE any open, and the per-response `key_id?` reads are explicitly defensive no-ops (`:490-493`). `reprisal_read` runs through the SAME `ensureHolderPopulated` before the holder's data key is read. Choosing (a) avoids a two-tier C4 story (concerns-via-probe vs reprisal-via-response) that I would otherwise have to reconcile.
  3. **Option (b)'s cost exceeds its benefit.** (b) is a migration touching the audited SECURITY DEFINER C4-read RPC `reprisal_read` — a high-blast-radius change on the C4 boundary, requiring its own pgTAP + a security-reviewer + threat-modeler pass — to close a window that is already non-silent + self-healing and already accepted for concerns. The marginal security gain (narrowing a one-op availability blip) does not justify modifying the highest-sensitivity read RPC.
  4. **The defensive `key_id?` passthrough narrows the window at zero cost today and makes (b) a trivial future upgrade.** Decision 1's optional `key_id?` read (mirroring `concerns/production-flows.ts:490-493`) is a no-op until/unless a future migration adds the column — at which point it starts receiving a value with NO composition change. Reversibility stays easy→medium.
- **Co-sign condition:** this ruling RATIFIES (a) and is the threat-modeler's call the architect requested. If the security-reviewer, on PR1 review, judges the C4 reprisal body materially higher-harm than a concern body such that the one-op stale-key window is unacceptable, (b) becomes the ratified path and rides along as its own migration PR (additive `key_id` column + EF/client passthrough + pgTAP) — flagged in the handoff. **Default: (a). Escalation path: (b), on security-reviewer objection at PR1.**
- **Affected:** `readReprisalViaProduction` (the probe-first read + defensive `key_id?` passthrough); the inherited `ensureHolderPopulated` rotation-observed wipe (`:148-150`); the `CommitteeKeyHolder` (§3.16 F-145 trigger 6).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (requires a cross-device rotation between this session's probe and a same-session read; Phase 2b does not itself rotate). **Impact:** LOW (a one-op typed `decrypt_failed`, self-healing — NOT a confidentiality/integrity break). **Priority:** MEDIUM (the C4 boundary + the explicit co-sign escalation make it a flagged surface despite the LOW likelihood×impact).
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the probe-first `ensureHolderPopulated` reads `key_id` from `getCommitteeKeyState` BEFORE any open and fires `onKeyRotationObserved` on the probe `key_id` when the holder is populated (`:148-150`) — a rotation observed on the NEXT op wipes + re-unwraps; (2) the open is wrapped in try/catch surfacing a typed `decrypt_failed` (never a silent mis-decrypt — secretbox AEAD throws on a wrong key, F-161/F-167); (3) the defensive `key_id?` passthrough (Decision 1) narrows the window further IF (b) is ever adopted; (4) the §3.16 F-145 trigger-6 observed-rotation wipe is the shipped mechanism this reuses.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-10 — the Decision 1 residual):**
  - _vitest (stale-key self-heal, AC-10):_ with a populated holder, a probe that reports a NEWER `key_id` triggers `onKeyRotationObserved` → wipe → re-unwrap on the next op; a `reprisal_read` attempted under a stale key surfaces a typed `decrypt_failed` (NOT a silent mis-decrypt — assert the opened plaintext is NEVER returned), and the next op's probe self-heals (re-unwraps under the new key).
  - _vitest (defensive key_id passthrough is a no-op today):_ assert the `readReprisalViaProduction` `key_id?` read is routed through `onKeyRotationObserved` and is a no-op when the read response carries no `key_id` (mirrors `concerns/production-flows.ts:490-493`) — proving the (b) upgrade path is wired but inert under (a).
  - _carry-forward (no new test owed):_ the §3.16 F-145 trigger-6 + F-154 stale-key/rotation tests cover the holder wipe + re-unwrap mechanism; the reprisal read reuses it.

#### F-163 | E | Probe-first / worker-without-key guard + 401-wipe/403-no-wipe — confirm REUSED from 2a, NOT re-implemented divergently

ADR-0028 Decision 6 mandates the `/reprisal` route reuse the concerns route shape verbatim: signed-in gate, probe-first `needs_setup` guard, and the inherited `CommitteeKeyHolder` + `classifyWireFailure` 401-wipe/403-no-wipe. The threat is a DIVERGENT re-implementation: a hand-rolled probe that hits `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` for a no-wrap actor (leaking that the disclosure RPC is reachable pre-setup), or a reprisal `classifyWireFailure` that wipes on 403 or fails to wipe on 401 — breaking the §3.16 F-142/F-145 invariants the route inherits.

- **Affected:** the `/reprisal` `+page.svelte` (signed-in gate + probe-first guard); the reprisal `ensureHolderPopulated` (copied verbatim from `concerns/production-flows.ts:129-182`); the reprisal `classifyWireFailure` (adapted ONLY for the reason-first branch, F-160 — otherwise verbatim).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (the architect mandates verbatim reuse). **Impact:** MEDIUM (a divergent probe leaks disclosure-RPC reachability; a divergent wipe breaks the dwell confinement). **Priority:** MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) **probe-first:** the route calls `getCommitteeKeyState` (metadata-only) FIRST via `ensureHolderPopulated`; if `actor_has_wrap === false` it renders the Phase-0a-setup guard and NEVER calls `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` (the disclosure RPC is not hit for a no-wrap actor — §3.16 F-144 / Decision 6, REUSED); (2) the reprisal `ensureHolderPopulated` is COPIED verbatim (probe-first, lazy unwrap, `onKeyRotationObserved` on the probe `key_id`) — no hand-rolled probe; (3) `classifyWireFailure` is verbatim EXCEPT the mandatory reason-first branch (F-160) — 401→wipe+session_expiry (`:205-208`), 429→rate_limited no-wipe (`:209-211`), 403→reason-first then `rls_denied` fallback; (4) the governance surfaces (status-approve, forensic) do NOT require the key (no seal/open) so they do not run the probe — but they STILL require the signed-in + active-member gate (server `_reprisal_gate()` is the real gate; the UI shows them only to signed-in members).
- **Testable mitigation (AC-5 / AC-6):**
  - _vitest (worker-without-key probe-first, AC-5):_ with `actor_has_wrap === false` from the probe, assert the `/reprisal` route renders the Phase-0a-setup guard and that `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` is NEVER called (assert the disclosure RPC transport is not invoked); `ensureHolderPopulated` returns `needs_setup`.
  - _vitest (401-wipe / 403-no-wipe, REUSED §3.16 F-145, AC-6):_ a reprisal-op 401 wipes the `CommitteeKeyHolder` (buffer zeroized + reference nulled) + fires `onSessionRevoked` + surfaces session_expiry; a 403 does NOT wipe the holder and does NOT clear the JWT (assert the buffer is still non-zero).
  - _vitest (governance reachable without a key, gated server-side):_ assert the status-approve / forensic compositions do NOT call `ensureHolderPopulated` (no seal/open) but a non-member call is still denied by the server `_reprisal_gate()` (cross-ref F-158).
  - _static/review (no divergent re-implementation):_ confirm the reprisal `ensureHolderPopulated` is the verbatim concerns probe-first logic and `classifyWireFailure` diverges ONLY in the reason-first branch (F-160) — a review-time structural check, not a hand-rolled probe.

#### F-164 | E | The per-record passphrase mis-modeled as the crypto gate rather than the UX-friction gate

`reprisal_read` enforces a per-record passphrase as a server-side FRICTION gate: a wrong/absent passphrase on a protected row emits `sensitive.access_attempt` + returns NO ciphertext (`:213-220`). The threat is a CLIENT mis-model: treating the passphrase as the DECRYPTION key (so a "correct" passphrase would gate `openUtf8`), or attempting decrypt on the null a wrong passphrase produces. The passphrase is NOT the crypto gate — the committee data key is; the passphrase is an additional server-side access-friction control on top of the E2EE. Mis-modeling it would either weaken the crypto posture (if the passphrase displaced the committee key) or crash on the null read.

- **Affected:** `submitReprisalViaProduction` (forwards `intake.passphrase` verbatim); `readReprisalViaProduction` (forwards the passphrase; surfaces `unavailable` on null, never decrypts on null — F-165); the server `reprisal_read` friction gate (`:213-220`).
- **Likelihood:** LOW. **Impact:** MEDIUM (a mis-model could weaken the crypto gate or crash; the passphrase is also a credential-class value that must not be logged, F-161). **Priority:** MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the passphrase is forwarded verbatim to the transport as a SERVER-side friction gate — the client never uses it as a decryption key; the committee data key (the holder) is the sole crypto gate (Decision 3); (2) a wrong passphrase yields `data:null` → `{ status: 'unavailable' }`, NEVER a decrypt attempt (F-165); (3) the passphrase is NEVER logged (F-161 — credential-class); (4) the wrong-passphrase attempt is audited server-side (`sensitive.access_attempt`, `:215-218`) — the friction gate's forensic value is preserved.
- **Testable mitigation (AC-3):**
  - _vitest (passphrase is friction, not crypto):_ assert `readReprisalViaProduction` does NOT derive any key from `intake.passphrase` and does NOT gate `openUtf8` on the passphrase — the committee data key (the holder) is the sole decrypt key; the passphrase is forwarded to the transport only.
  - _vitest (wrong passphrase → unavailable, never decrypt):_ a wrong passphrase yields `{ status: 'unavailable' }` with NO `openUtf8` call (cross-ref F-165, AC-3); the server emitted `sensitive.access_attempt` (transport-spy / pgTAP).
  - _vitest (passphrase never logged, cross-ref F-161):_ the `intake.passphrase` string never appears in any `console.*`/error/structured-log/audit-meta surface across submit/read (AC-8).

### §6 — Phase 2b compliance / breach-notification verification (PIPEDA s.10.1)

ADR-0028 introduces **no new PI field collected**, **no new subprocessor**, **no new region** (all rows land in the existing ca-central-1 project, ADR-0001), **no new audit enum value** (reuses `reprisal.created` / `reprisal.read` / `reprisal.update` / `reprisal.status_changed.4eyes_pending` / `reprisal.status_changed.4eyes_completed` / `sensitive.access_attempt` / `audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_pending` / `audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_completed` / `committee_data_key.unwrap` — all on the closed allowlist + ADR-0016 schedule; **no six-mirror dance**), and **no new retention class**. Constraints.md hard rule 6 (documented-purpose-per-new-field) is **N/A** — no new field; `reveal_reason` is operational justification stored in the pending op + the warn audit, not a new PI attribute about a user. Hard rule 3 (subprocessor) and hard rule 4 (region) are **N/A** by construction.

**PIPEDA fair-information principle mapping (the Phase 2b deltas):**

- **P1 Accountability / P2 Identifying purposes / P3 Consent / P4 Limiting collection:** unchanged — no new collection; the OHSA s.50 anti-reprisal-register purpose + consent posture carry forward (ADR-0003/0004). The forensic reveal is a use WITHIN that purpose (investigating a reprisal allegation), not a new collection.
- **P5 Limiting use/disclosure/retention:** **HONORED, with one deliberate, bounded disclosure.** The forensic reveal is a TIME-BOXED (≤24h, server-enforced `:331`/`:347-358`), 4-EYES-gated (role-pair + self-approve-denied, `:330-332`), AUDITED (warn-severity before-return, `:336-342`) de-pseudonymization — disclosure LIMITED to the minimum (one actor pseudonym, to a co-chair/certified pair, for the stated `reveal_reason`) and for the minimum duration. The feed (`:366-379`) and the new inbox (F-159) are pseudonymized-by-design (data minimization). Retention unchanged (existing enums + ADR-0016).
- **P6 Accuracy / P8 Openness / P9 Individual access / P10 Challenging compliance:** unchanged — no new processing.
- **P7 Safeguards:** **APPROPRIATE to the highest sensitivity in the system.** The C4 reprisal body is sealed (committee key, never plaintext past B2); the audited C4 read is audit-before-return (`:222-226`); the forensic reveal is the most-gated operation in the app (4-eyes + 24h + audit-before-reveal + UI no-cache, F-157). The inherited dwell safeguards (§3.16 F-145/F-146 six-trigger wipe + no-serialization) are REUSED. Net: safeguards are appropriate to the sensitivity and the new break-glass surface is mitigated + testable (AC-14..AC-17).

**Breach-notification trigger assessment (the forensic reveal, assessed explicitly as requested):**

The forensic reveal is the obvious candidate for an s.10.1 concern, so it is assessed head-on. **It is NOT a breach — it is a deliberate, authorized, audited, 4-eyes, time-boxed break-glass control.** s.10.1 fires on a breach of security safeguards creating a real risk of significant harm — i.e. an UNAUTHORIZED or unintended loss/disclosure. The forensic reveal is the opposite: an INTENTIONAL, governed de-pseudonymization, performed only by a valid co-chair/certified PAIR (`_reprisal_valid_pair`, `:332`), only after a second-approver gate the proposer cannot self-satisfy (`:330`), only within ≤24h (`:331`), only with a recorded `reveal_reason`, and witnessed by a warn-severity audit row that commits BEFORE the identity is shown (`:336-342`). The disclosure is to AUTHORIZED committee officers, not to an adversary; the identity is shown modal-local and never persisted/cached/logged (F-157). **This introduces NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 "real risk of significant harm" surface** — it is a safeguard EXERCISE, not a safeguard failure. (Where s.10.1 WOULD fire: if the revealed pseudonym LEAKED past the modal — to a store/log/URL/cache — that leak would be an unauthorized disclosure of a retaliation-context identity and would plausibly meet the significant-harm threshold; this is exactly why F-157's no-cache invariant is HIGH-priority and test-blocking, AC-17. The control's correctness is what keeps it on the right side of s.10.1.) The new inbox read (F-159) is pseudonymized-by-design — no raw actor, no revealed pseudonym, no ciphertext — so it introduces no disclosure surface. The C4-body residual (F-162) is a one-op typed `decrypt_failed`, self-healing — not a disclosure.

**Conclusion: Phase 2b introduces NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 breach-notification trigger.** The forensic reveal is an authorized, audited, 4-eyes, ≤24h break-glass (not a breach); the feed + new inbox reduce/avoid PI exposure; the C4 residual is non-disclosing. The 24-month breach-record-keeping obligation is unchanged. **No PHIPA trigger** (no health information — OHSA s.50 reprisal allegations are not PHIPA "personal health information"; if a future reprisal field captured identifiable health info, PHIPA's 60-day notice + custodian + lockbox rules would fire — flagged as a re-pass trigger). **No PCI trigger** (no payment data). **No cross-border transfer** introduced — all data stays in ca-central-1.

### Cross-border & subprocessor assessment

**No cross-border transfer and no new subprocessor are introduced by Phase 2b.** All reprisal data (the C4 body ciphertext, the pending-ops ledger, the feed/inbox projections, the audit rows) lands in the existing ca-central-1 Supabase project (ADR-0001, re-confirmed). The de-pseudonymized actor pseudonym crosses B2 ONLY browser↔Edge-Function (in-region) and is never transmitted off-platform. There is **nothing to approve under the cross-border human gate** for this feature (explicitly: all data remains in ca-central-1; no Sentry/SendGrid/US-region path is touched).

### Top 5 prioritized risks (Phase 2b only; for the parent agent's summary)

1. **F-157 (HIGH) — the FORENSIC-REVEAL break-glass (de-pseudonymization of a retaliation-context actor; the app's highest-privilege op):** server gates (self-approve `:330` / 24h expiry `:331` / role-pair `:332`) are un-bypassable from the client; the warn-audit commits BEFORE the pseudonym returns (`:336-342`) and the composition's await enforces it end-to-end; the revealed pseudonym is modal-local, `role=status`, cleared on close, NEVER cached/logged/persisted/in-URL. **Security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign at PR2** (AC-14..AC-17). A leaked/cached reveal is the one Phase 2b outcome that WOULD meet s.10.1 — which is why AC-17 (no-cache) is test-blocking.
2. **F-162 (HIGH — RULED) — the C4-body residual (probe-first stale-key window on `reprisal_read`):** RULED option (a) — probe-first parity, NO migration — ACCEPTED for the C4 reprisal body: the window is a one-op typed `decrypt_failed`, non-silent + self-healing, identical to the concerns window already accepted (§3.16 F-154), and (b) would diverge from the audited 2a baseline + modify the C4-read RPC for marginal gain. **Escalation path: (b) (the `key_id` migration) if the security-reviewer objects at PR1.** Security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign (AC-10).
3. **F-161 (HIGH) — key-material / reprisal-plaintext / passphrase leak:** the session-resident data key + plaintext reprisal title/body + `intake.passphrase` must never hit logs/errors/audit-meta/storage/URL. Mitigation: full-workflow leak-sweep CI gate across submit/read/update/feed + the no-serialization scan; extends the §3.16 F-148 / §3.15 F-132 gate (AC-8).
4. **F-159 (MED) — the new `reprisal_list_pending_ops` inbox read:** must project pseudonymized proposer, NO raw `proposer_id`, NO `revealed_actor_pseudonym`, NO ciphertext; gated `_reprisal_gate()`; REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role. **threat-modeler co-sign at P2b-5** (AC-18). The only new migration in Phase 2b (PR2 only).
5. **F-160 (MED) — governance 403 discrimination:** `self_approve_denied` vs `role_pair_invalid` (both 403) must be discriminated by `reason` (the EF maps by message, `core.ts:67`) — a verbatim copy of the concerns `classifyWireFailure` (403→`rls_denied`) would ERASE the distinction. Mitigation: reason-first branch; identity-safe copy that names neither other party (AC-11/AC-12/AC-16). Cross-cuts F-165 (the audited C4 read, MED-HIGH) and F-157 (which reuses the same discrimination).

### Handoff packets

- **To test-writer (priority order; each test RED against `main` before its implementer PR opens; AC-N = ADR-0028 acceptance criteria):**
  1. **F-157 (HIGH, AC-15/AC-17/AC-14/AC-16) — forensic break-glass (PR2):** vitest — audit-before-reveal (the `audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_completed` warn-audit-spy fires BEFORE the composition resolves the pseudonym; straight await, no eager paint); revealed-pseudonym-NOT-cached (a post-close leak-sweep: absent from DOM/JS-state/Svelte-store/localStorage/sessionStorage/URL/list-cache/logs after modal close); 24h-expiry honored on display (past-`expires_at` → `{status:'expired'}` + affordance disabled); self-approve vs role-pair distinct (both 403, by reason). pgTAP — gates RAISE in order (self/expiry/role-pair) before the de-pseudonymization, and the warn-audit is ordered before `RETURN v_revealed` (inject-failure pattern).
  2. **F-162 (HIGH, AC-10) — C4-body stale-key self-heal (PR1):** vitest — a populated holder + a probe reporting a NEWER `key_id` → wipe → re-unwrap on the next op; a `reprisal_read` under a stale key surfaces a typed `decrypt_failed` (the opened plaintext is NEVER returned, NOT a silent mis-decrypt); the next op's probe self-heals; the defensive `key_id?` passthrough is wired-but-inert under option (a). (Carry-forward: §3.16 F-145 trigger-6 / F-154.)
  3. **F-161 (HIGH, AC-8) — leak sweep (both PRs):** vitest — full submit/read/update/feed sweep across `console.*`/thrown-error/structured-log/audit-meta asserts NONE of {32 data-key bytes, identity privkey, plaintext reprisal title/body, `intake.passphrase`} appears; no-serialization scan; decrypt-fail surfaces typed `decrypt_failed` with no bytes; extend the §3.16 F-148 / §3.15 F-132 CI grep to the reprisal surfaces (P2b-4).
  4. **F-165 (MED-HIGH, AC-2/AC-3) — audited C4 read + never-decrypt-on-null (PR1):** vitest — `reprisal.read` audit-spy fires before the plaintext resolves (no `openUtf8` until the RPC returns); a wrong/absent passphrase → `data:null` → `{status:'unavailable'}` with NO `openUtf8` call; not-found → the SAME `unavailable` (assert both map identically — the wire cannot distinguish); no invented `invalid_passphrase`. pgTAP — `reprisal_read` emits `sensitive.access_attempt` then no rows on a wrong passphrase (`:215-219`), `reprisal.read` before `RETURN QUERY` on happy (`:222-226`), no audit on not-found (`:211`).
  5. **F-159 (MED, AC-18) — `reprisal_list_pending_ops` privacy (PR2 / P2b-5):** pgTAP — pseudonymized proposer (`= _committee_pseudonym(proposer_id)`); raw `proposer_id` structurally absent; `revealed_actor_pseudonym` structurally absent; NO ciphertext column; gated `_reprisal_gate()`; REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role + GRANT authenticated/supabase_auth_admin; a non-member call raises the gate; a seeded COMPLETED forensic op's revealed pseudonym is NEVER returned by the inbox.
  6. **F-160 (MED, AC-11/AC-12/AC-16) — governance 403 discrimination (PR2):** vitest — `approveStatusViaProduction` outside-pairing → `{status:'role_pair_invalid'}` (NOT generic `rls_denied`; discriminate on `reason`, both 403); self-approve → `{status:'self_approve_denied'}`; same for `approveForensicViaProduction`; the surfaced copy names NEITHER other party; the inbox suppresses the Approve affordance on a self-proposed op.
  7. **F-158 (MED, AC-6/AC-11/AC-16) — JWT / non-member / un-spoofable self-approve:** pgTAP — non-member gate on each governance RPC + the inbox read; server-resolved actor compared (`:287`/`:330`), not a body field. vitest — 401-wipe (holder zeroized + `onSessionRevoked`), 403-no-wipe.
  8. **F-163 (MED, AC-5/AC-6) — probe-first worker-without-key + REUSE:** vitest — `actor_has_wrap === false` renders the Phase-0a-setup guard and `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` is NEVER hit; governance compositions do NOT call `ensureHolderPopulated` but a non-member is still server-denied; review-check that `ensureHolderPopulated` is verbatim + `classifyWireFailure` diverges only in the reason-first branch.
  9. **F-167 (MED, AC-1/AC-8) — shared-seal extraction byte-identical + reprisal round-trip:** vitest — the pinned-hex KAT + the concern-core seal tests pass UNCHANGED after the move/re-export (no seal-format drift); reprisal submit→open round-trips under the shared seal; corrupted ciphertext → typed `decrypt_failed`.
  10. **F-164 (MED, AC-3) — per-record passphrase is friction, not crypto:** vitest — the composition derives NO key from `intake.passphrase` and does not gate `openUtf8` on it; wrong passphrase → `unavailable`, never decrypt; passphrase never logged. **F-166 (LOW-MED, AC-4) — feed has no ciphertext/no actor/no holder:** vitest + pgTAP — feed rows carry no `actor_pseudonym`/no `*_ct`, ts bucketed to hour, no `openUtf8`, `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` not hit on a feed read.
  - Group as **"Phase 2b must-fail-first"**: **F-161, F-162, F-165** are the blocking three for PR1 (the leak sweep + the C4-body residual + the audited-read/never-decrypt-on-null); **F-157, F-159, F-160** are the blocking three for PR2 (the forensic break-glass + the new inbox read + the governance 403 discrimination). **F-157 (AC-15/AC-17) is the architect's flagged HIGH edge and MUST be red first at PR2**; **F-162 (AC-10) is the C4-body co-sign edge and MUST be red first at PR1**.

- **To security-reviewer (required at each PR per HG-REPRISAL-PHASE2B — the TWO HIGH surfaces co-sign; forensic especially at PR2):**
  1. **F-157 (PR2, P2b-6/P2b-8 — the app's highest-privilege op):** verify `reprisal_approve_forensic` RAISEs self_approve_denied (`:330`) / expired (`:331`) / role_pair_invalid (`:332`) BEFORE `jhsc_forensic_reveal_actor_pseudonym` (`:334`), and that the warn `...4eyes_completed` `audit_emit` (`:336-341`) is ordered BEFORE `RETURN v_revealed` (`:342`). Verify the composition uses straight `await` (no eager paint) and holds NO module-level reference to the pseudonym. Verify the UI renders the pseudonym modal-local + `role=status` + cleared on close/unmount, NEVER to a store/localStorage/sessionStorage/URL/list-cache/log, and disables the Approve affordance past `expires_at`. (AC-14..AC-17.)
  2. **F-162 (PR1, P2b-2/P2b-3 — the C4-body residual + the (a)-vs-(b) call):** review the RULING — option (a) probe-first parity, NO migration. Confirm `reprisal_read` returns `TABLE(title_ct, body_ct)` no `key_id` (`:204`) and the composition satisfies C4 via `ensureHolderPopulated`'s probe `onKeyRotationObserved` (`:148-150`) + the defensive `key_id?` passthrough. **Your objection is the escalation trigger:** if you judge the C4 reprisal body materially higher-harm such that the one-op stale-key window is unacceptable, (b) (the `key_id` migration) becomes the ratified path as its own PR. (AC-10.)
  3. **F-161 (both PRs, P2b-4):** verify the leak-sweep CI gate covers the data key + plaintext reprisal title/body + `intake.passphrase`; verify the SEALED ciphertext is what crosses the wire on every flow; verify every decrypt surfaces a typed `decrypt_failed` (no libsodium bytes). (AC-8.)
  4. **F-165/F-158 (PR1/PR2):** verify the C4 read does not decrypt until the RPC returns and never decrypts on null (audit-before-return preserved end-to-end); verify the governance approve compares the SERVER-resolved actor (`:287`/`:330`), not a body field; verify 401-wipe/403-no-wipe and no new ungated op (F-122 grep unaffected; the seven RPCs + the new inbox REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/service_role).
  5. **F-160/F-163/F-167:** verify the reason-first 403 discrimination (not a verbatim concerns copy); verify the probe-first guard never hits the disclosure RPC for a no-wrap actor; verify the seal extraction is byte-identical (KAT green).

- **To privacy-reviewer (required at PR2 — the forensic disclosure + the new inbox read):**
  1. **F-157 (the forensic de-pseudonymization):** ratify that the reveal is an authorized, audited, 4-eyes, ≤24h break-glass — a SAFEGUARD EXERCISE, NOT a breach (no new s.10.1 trigger) — and that the no-cache invariant (AC-17) is what keeps it on the right side of s.10.1 (a leaked reveal WOULD meet significant-harm; the control's correctness is the mitigation). Confirm `reveal_reason` is operational justification, not a new PI field about a user (hard rule 6 N/A).
  2. **F-159 (the new inbox read):** confirm `reprisal_list_pending_ops` projects pseudonymized proposer, NO raw `proposer_id`, NO `revealed_actor_pseudonym`, NO ciphertext — ratify as pseudonymized-by-design (data minimization, PIPEDA P4/P5). This is the only new read surface; it is NOT an F-149-style widening.
  3. **§6:** ratify that Phase 2b introduces NO new PI field, NO new subprocessor, NO new region, NO new retention class, NO new audit enum (hard rules 3/4/6 N/A by construction) and NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 breach trigger — the forensic reveal is governed disclosure, not a breach; the feed + inbox reduce/avoid PI; the C4 residual is non-disclosing. Confirm the plaintext reprisal title/body live ONLY in render scope and the data key never serializes (F-161, REUSED §3.16 F-146).

- **To the user (required human-gate decisions):**
  1. **HG-REPRISAL-PHASE2B (PR1):** security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign of (i) the audited C4-read composition (F-165, P2b-2/P2b-3) and (ii) **the C4-body residual ruling (F-162, P2b-2)** — RULED option (a) probe-first parity, NO migration; the security-reviewer may escalate to option (b) (the `key_id` migration) if the C4 body is judged higher-harm than a concern body. This is the first of the two HIGH surfaces.
  2. **HG-REPRISAL-PHASE2B (PR2):** security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign of **the FORENSIC-REVEAL break-glass (F-157, P2b-6/P2b-8 — the app's highest-privilege operation: audit-before-reveal, 24h expiry, role-pair + self-approve, UI no-cache)** and threat-modeler co-sign of the new pseudonymized inbox read (F-159, P2b-5). This is the second, gravest HIGH surface — no autonomous merge.
  3. **Production deploy of either PR** touches the C4 PI path → never auto-merge (constraints.md Human Gates: "Production deploys of changes touching … personal data"; hard rule 5: auth/authz/session are security-critical).
  - **No new cross-border transfer, no new subprocessor, no new credential surface, no new region, no new retention class** is introduced by Phase 2b — so NO HG-NEW-style transfer/credential gate fires. There is **nothing to approve under the cross-border human gate** for this feature (explicitly: all data remains in ca-central-1).

### Re-pass triggers (Phase 2b)

1. Any change that lets the revealed forensic pseudonym escape modal-local state — a store outliving the modal, localStorage/sessionStorage/URL, a list-row cache, or any log/audit-meta path — OR any path that surfaces the pseudonym before the `audit.forensic_reveal.4eyes_completed` warn-audit commits, OR any weakening of the server self-approve/expiry/role-pair gates (`:330-332`) → re-open F-157 NO-GO (and a leaked reveal would itself be an s.10.1 unauthorized disclosure).
2. Any migration widening `reprisal_read` beyond `TABLE(title_ct, body_ct)` without the F-162 (b) review, OR any path that returns reprisal ciphertext without first committing `reprisal.read` (`:222-226`), OR a silent mis-decrypt under a stale key (instead of a typed `decrypt_failed`) → re-open F-162/F-165 NO-GO.
3. `reprisal_list_pending_ops` projecting a raw `proposer_id`, the `revealed_actor_pseudonym`, or any ciphertext, OR dropping the `_reprisal_gate()`/REVOKE posture → re-open F-159 NO-GO.
4. A reprisal `classifyWireFailure` that collapses `self_approve_denied`/`role_pair_invalid`/`expired` to a generic `rls_denied` (a verbatim concerns copy without the reason-first branch), or governance copy that names another member → re-open F-160.
5. Any new log/toast/error/audit-meta path touching the plaintext data key, a plaintext reprisal field, or `intake.passphrase`; OR a seal-extraction that changes the seal bytes (KAT drift) → re-open F-161/F-167.
6. A divergent re-implementation of the probe-first guard that hits `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` for a no-wrap actor, or a 401 that fails to wipe / a 403 that wipes → re-open F-163 (and §3.16 F-142/F-145).
7. A future reprisal field capturing identifiable health information → PHIPA fires (60-day notice, custodian, lockbox); escalate to privacy-reviewer + re-open §6.
8. Key rotation brought in-scope, a paged/filtered reprisal read, or any move of data off ca-central-1 / new subprocessor → re-open the relevant DFD + §6.

## §3.18 — Phase 1 member onboarding (co-chair invites → invitee redeems → enrolls → co-chair grants committee-key access) (ADR-0029)

Source: threat-modeler pass 2026-06-22, gating **HG-ONBOARD-PHASE1** (ADR-0029 Compliance check, the unchecked box), driven by ADR-0029 (Phase 1: the first production path to bring a SECOND human onto the committee — invite/redeem + grant-key). F-range continues from F-167 (no renumbering of prior findings); new findings **F-168…F-177**. The architect proposed F-168–F-176; this pass keeps that mapping and SPLITS the atomicity/race concern out as **F-177** (it is its own concrete pgTAP target, not a sub-clause of F-169). The single biggest new surface — the **repeatable, unauthenticated `redeem-invite` Edge Function** that CREATES nothing but ACTIVATES a pre-created user + binds a first passkey, gated only by an invite code + 15-min TOTP (NOT one-shot, NOT `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED`-gated) — is pinned at **F-168/F-170** and **requires security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign at PR P1-1 and P1-2**. The second HIGH surface — the **`get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` pubkey-disclosure RPC** (the first deliberate read of ANOTHER member's `identity_keys.public_key`, an otherwise fully read-locked table) and the **wrap-for-member production composition** — is pinned at **F-172/F-174** and co-signed at **P1-4/P1-5**. Verdict: **GO-WITH-CONDITIONS** — every testable mitigation below is implementation-blocking and maps to the ADR-0029 increments P1-1…P1-10.

This pass re-verified the ground truth the architect handed me, file:line, before ruling. Confirmations: `committee_invite.target_user_id` is `NOT NULL REFERENCES public.users(id) ON DELETE CASCADE` (`00000000000002_committee.sql:46`) and `bootstrap_id` is a nullable FK to `auth_totp_bootstraps(id)` (`:48`) — so the user row + TOTP MUST pre-exist at invite-creation, which is exactly what forces the issue-time user creation (Decision 2a) and closes retargeting BY CONSTRUCTION; `committee_invite_member` gates `session_is_live()` + `_committee_is_active_co_chair(auth.uid())` (`:230-235`), validates roles `<@ {worker_member,worker_co_chair,certified_member}` (`:237-240`), inserts a PENDING `committee_membership(active=false)` (`:246-247`) + the invite carrying `bootstrap_id` + `p_ttl_minutes` (`:250-251`); `committee_activate_membership` HARD-BINDS `v_inv.target_user_id <> p_enrolling_uid → invite_invalid` (`:275-277`), re-checks consumed/expired (`:271-273`), flips active + sets `users.role` + consumes the invite + emits `member.added` in one txn (`:286-300`). TOTP: `auth_totp_bootstraps` has `UNIQUE(user_id)` cap-of-1 (`00000000000001_auth.sql:268`), `expires_at = issued_at + 15min` (`:263`), `secret_hash = hmac(code, _hmac_pseudonym_key())` computed by the issuer with the raw code never persisted (`:258-261`), all client access REVOKED (`:278`); `enroll_first_passkey` is the exact consumer template — `FOR UPDATE` the bootstrap (`:388-392`), `NOT FOUND → TOTP_BOOTSTRAP_NOT_FOUND` (`:394-396`), consumed/locked/expired raises (`:398-408`), wrong code increments `wrong_attempts` + `locked_at = now()` at the 5th (`:413-419`), then writes the consumed-log + DELETEs the bootstrap (`:425-428`), granted `supabase_auth_admin` ONLY (`:460-465`). Bootstrap template: `bootstrap_first_co_chair` is `verify_jwt=false` (EF header `:7`), self-mints `mint_writer` (no service_role — F-118), `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED` default-deny at the edge (`:14-15`), advisory-lock + `EXISTS(users) → BOOTSTRAP_ALREADY_DONE` self-disabling guard (`:55-61`), `REVOKE ALL … FROM PUBLIC, anon, authenticated, service_role; GRANT … TO mint_writer` (`:124-127`). Pubkey: `identity_keys` is `REVOKE SELECT,INSERT,UPDATE,DELETE … FROM authenticated, anon` (`00000000000007_t07.sql:122`) with NO disclosure RPC today; the comment at `:118-121` ("Wrap routing reads the pubkey via the wrap_for_member function") is **factually wrong** — `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member` reads NO pubkey, it takes a PRE-SEALED `p_wrapped_ciphertext` (`:485-522`), gates `_t07_gate_active_member()` for the ACTOR (`:496`), re-asserts the TARGET is active (`:502-503`), and inserts `ON CONFLICT (user_id, key_id) DO NOTHING` (`:509-511`). The corresponding analysis ground-truth is ADR-0029 (decisions.md) Findings + Decisions 1–9 + the MANDATED threat-modeler handoff (F-168–F-176).

### Scope reconciliation against existing entries

- **THREE new trust boundaries / attack surfaces (the first material new boundaries since §3.16).**
  - **B-REDEEM (NEW) — browser(unauthenticated) ↔ `redeem-invite` EF.** A `verify_jwt=false` Edge Function reachable by anyone with the public URL, gated only by an invite code + TOTP. It is the repeatable sibling of `bootstrap-first-co-chair`'s B-BOOTSTRAP, but — unlike B-BOOTSTRAP — it is NOT one-shot, NOT self-disabling, and NOT `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED`-windowed. This is the single biggest new surface; F-168/F-169/F-170/F-171/F-177 all ride it.
  - **B-PUBKEY (NEW disclosure facet of B2) — browser(co-chair) ↔ `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap`.** The first deliberate read of ANOTHER member's `identity_keys.public_key`. `identity_keys` is otherwise fully read-locked (`:122`); this RPC is the ONE crack in that lock. F-172/F-174 ride it.
  - **B-WRAPFORMEMBER (first production use of an existing surface).** `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member` (`:485-522`) has existed since T07 but has had NO production consumer — every prior wrap was a SELF-wrap. Phase 1 is the FIRST time a co-chair seals the data key to a pubkey they just fetched for SOMEONE ELSE. F-172 rides it.
- **B-COMMITTEE-OP (REUSED).** `issue_invite` / `reissue_totp` ride the existing co-chair `committee-op` boundary (`assertKeyParity` + `assertSessionLive` + bearer + in-fn `_committee_is_active_co_chair` gates, §3.14 F-116/F-124–126 carry-forward). F-173/F-175 ride it; no new boundary.
- **The bootstrap EF is the verbatim template; the redeem EF CONSUMES its hardening but DEFEATS its one-shot guard by design.** F-168 below pins the precise delta: the redeem EF REUSES the `verify_jwt=false` + self-minted `mint_writer` + key-parity + `MINT_EXPECTED_ORIGINS` origin pin + `verifyWebAuthnRegistration` ceremony (all `bootstrap-first-co-chair` controls), but REPLACES the `EXISTS(users)` self-disabling guard with the invite+TOTP gate and does NOT reuse `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED`. This is a DELIBERATE removal of a security control (self-disabling), compensated by the invite+TOTP+single-use+TTL+lock set — F-168/F-170 assess whether that compensation is sufficient.
- **The F-122 session-live-uniformity grep allowlist (§3.13 F-123) MUST gain `redeem-invite` as a new unauthenticated-but-gated entry.** F-123's mitigation requires a threat-model re-pass for any allowlist addition; **this section IS that re-pass.** F-168 records the allowlist contract: `redeem-invite` is `verify_jwt=false` by NECESSITY (the invitee has no JWT — same rationale as `mint-session/challenge`/`bootstrap-first-co-chair`), so it legitimately skips the `session_is_live()` op-handler gate, BUT its SQL terminal `redeem_invite_complete` is `mint_writer`-ONLY (REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/authenticated/service_role) — it cannot be reached by a direct anon/authenticated RPC, exactly as `bootstrap_first_co_chair`.
- **ONE new audit enum value** (`identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap`, six-mirror dance, `membership+7y` — sibling of `member.added` at `retention_class_for:92`). Contrast §3.16/§3.17 which added zero. F-172/F-174 carry the audit-before-return + six-mirror assertions. All other audit emissions REUSE existing enums (`member.added` from `committee_activate_membership:293-300`; `auth.passkey.enrolled` from the redeem path mirroring `enroll_first_passkey:445-454`; `committee_data_key.wrapped_for_member` from `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member:512-521`).
- **NO new PI field, NO new subprocessor, NO new region, NO new retention class beyond the one audit enum's `membership+7y` (which is an EXISTING class, just newly mapped).** `display_name` / `off_employer_contact` are EXISTING OPTIONAL invite fields (`committee_invite_member` params `:215-216`), not new (hard rule 6 N/A). The central compliance win is the **out-of-band invite delivery** — no email/SMS provider, so Phase 1 adds ZERO cross-border / subprocessor surface (§6).

### Data flow (per ceremony; B-REDEEM = browser-unauth ↔ redeem-invite EF; B-PUBKEY = co-chair pubkey-disclosure facet; B2 = browser ↔ Edge Functions; B4 = browser RAM dwell of the data key)

```
[Ceremony 1 — Issue invite (co-chair → user-row + TOTP + invite; code returned ONCE; P1-1/P1-3)]
  Browser(co-chair) -> committee-op issue_invite { roles[], display_name?, off_employer_contact? }   [B2; co-chair JWT]
  EF: generate cryptographically-random 6-digit code (NEVER persisted/logged); call
      issue_member_invite(p_roles, p_totp_code:=code, p_ttl_minutes, p_display_name?, p_off_employer_contact?)
  Server (SECURITY DEFINER, gated session_is_live()+_committee_is_active_co_chair, ONE txn):
      v_new_uid := gen_random_uuid();
      INSERT public.users(id:=v_new_uid, active:=true, role:=NULL)             -- role set on activation, not now
      INSERT auth_totp_bootstraps(user_id:=v_new_uid, secret_hash:=hmac(code,_hmac_pseudonym_key()), expires_at:=now()+15min)
      committee_invite_member(v_new_uid, p_roles, …, p_bootstrap_id:=v_bootstrap_id, p_ttl_minutes:=p_ttl)
        -> INSERT pending committee_membership(active=false) + committee_invite(target_user_id=v_new_uid, bootstrap_id, expires_at)
      RETURN {invite_id, invitee_user_id, bootstrap_id}
  EF -> Browser(co-chair): { invite_id, raw_code, invitee_user_id }    -- raw_code: response-body-ONLY, ONCE, never re-fetchable
  Co-chair conveys {invite_id (the /redeem link) + raw_code} OUT-OF-BAND through their own channel.
  CROSSES B2: roles + optional display/contact (existing PI fields) → in; {invite_id, raw_code} → out (raw_code = transient secret).
  NEVER persisted/logged: raw_code (F-176). At rest: secret_hash (HMAC), NOT the code (mirrors :258-261).

[Ceremony 1b — Re-send code (co-chair → fresh TOTP against the SAME invite; P1-6)]
  Browser(co-chair) -> committee-op reissue_totp { invite_id }     [B2; co-chair JWT]
  EF: generate a FRESH 6-digit code; call reissue_member_totp(p_invite_id, p_totp_code:=code)
  Server (gated; ONE txn): upsert auth_totp_bootstraps for the invite's target_user_id (UNIQUE(user_id) → delete-then-insert),
      fresh secret_hash + fresh expires_at=now()+15min, reset wrong_attempts/locked_at. Does NOT touch user/invite/membership.
  EF -> Browser(co-chair): { raw_code }     -- the OLD code no longer validates (F-175).
  CROSSES B2: invite_id → in; raw_code → out. NEVER persisted/logged.

[Ceremony 2 — Redeem (UNAUTH → passkey + session + active membership; ATOMIC; P1-1/P1-2)]
  Browser(unauth) opens /redeem?... carrying invite_id ONLY (NEVER the code — code is member-entered, never in URL).
  Step A (challenge): Browser -> redeem-invite EF { action:'challenge', invite_id, rpId, origin }   [B-REDEEM]
      EF: validate origin (MINT_EXPECTED_ORIGINS) + key-parity; issue a single-use WebAuthn challenge.
          (Code/TOTP NOT checked yet — challenge issuance is cheap, leaks nothing.)
  Step B: Browser runs navigator.credentials.create() (the SAME registration ceremony as bootstrap).
  Step C (register): Browser -> redeem-invite EF
      { action:'register', invite_id, totp_code, challenge, credentialId, attestationObject, clientDataJSON, … }  [B-REDEEM]
      EF: validate origin + key-parity; consume+bind the challenge (rp_id/origin match); verifyWebAuthnRegistration
          (ONLY the verified pubkey/credId reach the RPC); self-mint a mint_writer token; call
          redeem_invite_complete(p_invite_id, p_totp_code, <verified credential fields>)
  Server redeem_invite_complete (SECURITY DEFINER, GRANT mint_writer ONLY, ONE txn):
      (i)   SELECT invite FOR UPDATE; assert NOT consumed + NOT expired + bootstrap_id present (else invite_invalid)
      (ii)  validate p_totp_code against the bound bootstrap with the EXACT enroll_first_passkey logic
            (FOR UPDATE; consumed/locked/expired raise; wrong → wrong_attempts++ + lock at 5; :402-419)
      (iii) write consumed-log + DELETE bootstrap (:425-428)
      (iv)  INSERT webauthn_credentials for the invite's target_user_id (the redeemer NEVER supplies a uid)
      (v)   committee_activate_membership(p_invite_id, p_enrolling_uid:=invite.target_user_id)
            -> the :275-277 target=enrolling bind is satisfied BY CONSTRUCTION (uses the invite's own bound target)
            -> flips active, sets users.role, consumes invite, emits member.added (:286-300)
      (vi)  emit auth.passkey.enrolled
      RETURN {user_id}
  EF guides the browser into sign-in (mint a session) → identity-enroll → recovery (Phase 0a compositions, MINUS key-init).
  CROSSES B-REDEEM: invite_id + totp_code + verified credential fields → in; {user_id} → out.
  NEVER crosses: the raw code is member-entered, never in URL/logs; the member's privkey is device-custody (never sent).
  ATOMIC: a failure at any (i)–(vi) ROLLS BACK whole — no passkey-bound-but-membership-inactive split (F-177).

[Ceremony 3 — Identity-enroll + recovery (member self; REUSED Phase 0a verbatim; P1-7)]
  (Identical to ADR-0026 enrollIdentityViaProduction + storeRecoveryBlobViaProduction — Phase 1 adds nothing here EXCEPT
   it does NOT run committee-key INIT. The member ends with an enrolled identity_keys.public_key + a recovery blob,
   but NO committee_key_wraps row → "waiting for committee access" holding state, P1-9.)
  CROSSES B2: the F-02 sealed challenge + the enrolled pubkey (server-persisted) + the sealed recovery blob. Self-scoped.

[Ceremony 4 — Grant key access (co-chair → pubkey-disclosure → seal → wrap; ASYNC step 2; P1-4/P1-5/P1-8)]
  Browser(co-chair) -> get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap { p_member_user_id }    [B-PUBKEY; co-chair JWT]
  Server (SECURITY DEFINER, gated session_is_live()+_committee_is_active_co_chair, AUDIT-BEFORE-RETURN):
      assert target is an active member with an enrolled, non-revoked identity key (else member_not_enrolled/not_found);
      emit identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap (actor=co-chair pseudonym, target=member) BEFORE returning;
      RETURN { public_key, fingerprint }
  Browser(co-chair): confirm the fingerprint in the UI (visual target check, Decision 6);
      ensure the CommitteeKeyHolder is populated (ADR-0027 unwrap if null — emits the co-chair's OWN committee_data_key.unwrap);
      seal := crypto_box_seal(holder.data_key, member_pubkey)   [libsodium, sender-anonymous; co-chair privkey NOT needed]
  Browser(co-chair) -> wrap_committee_data_key_for_member { p_member_user_id, p_key_id:=holder.key_id, p_wrapped_ciphertext:=seal }  [B-WRAPFORMEMBER]
  Server: _t07_gate_active_member() (actor) + is_active_member(target) (:496/:502-503); INSERT wrap ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING (:509-511);
      emit committee_data_key.wrapped_for_member (actor+target+key) (:512-521)
  Now the member's existing get_committee_key_wrap_for_self (auth.uid()-scoped) returns a wrap → the app comes alive for them.
  CROSSES B-PUBKEY: member uid → in; member's pubkey + fingerprint → out (pseudonymous, audited). CROSSES B-WRAPFORMEMBER:
      the SEALED data key (sealed-box ciphertext) → in. NEVER crosses: the plaintext committee data key (sealed client-side; Decision 4 rejects server-side seal — ADR-0003 Invariant 1/5/6).
```

**PI / secret classification per store / transit path (Phase 1 deltas):**

| Surface | Classification | At rest where | Crosses boundary as | Residency | Retention |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| The 6-digit one-time invite code | **Transient secret** (code, B4-class) | **NEVER at rest** — exists only in the issue/reissue EF response body + the co-chair's screen + the member's entry | EF response (out) + redeem `totp_code` (in); NEVER a URL | ca-central-1 (transit only) | none — never persisted (F-176) |
| `auth_totp_bootstraps.secret_hash` | Derived secret (HMAC of the code) | Postgres `auth_totp_bootstraps` | NEVER leaves the server | ca-central-1 | ≤15min live then DELETEd on consume (`:428`) or expiry; `UNIQUE(user_id)` cap-of-1 |
| `public.users` row (invitee) | PI container (id; `role` set on activation) | Postgres `public.users` | created server-side at issue (Ceremony 1) | ca-central-1 | member lifecycle (existing class) |
| `display_name` / `off_employer_contact` | PI (optional, EXISTING fields) | Postgres (invite/membership path) | issue request (in) | ca-central-1 | member lifecycle; **no new field** (hard rule 6 N/A) |
| `committee_invite` row | Onboarding-state metadata (target_user_id, bootstrap_id FK, role, expires_at, consumed_at) | Postgres `committee_invite` | never client-readable (REVOKE all, `:60`) | ca-central-1 | consumed_at set on redeem; TTL ≤7 days (Decision 3) |
| WebAuthn credential (member's first passkey) | Auth credential (public_key + credId) | Postgres `webauthn_credentials` | verified attestation → RPC (Ceremony 2) | ca-central-1 | member lifecycle |
| Member's identity privkey | **Secret (Ed25519/X25519 private key)** | **Device-custody only** (+ the encrypted recovery blob) | NEVER crosses any boundary in plaintext | n/a (device) | device + recovery-blob lifecycle (ADR-0026) |
| Member's `identity_keys.public_key` | **Pseudonymous identifier** (small re-identification aid via uid↔pubkey map) | Postgres `identity_keys` (read-locked `:122`) | disclosed to a co-chair via `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` ONLY (audited, B-PUBKEY) | ca-central-1 | member lifecycle |
| Plaintext committee data key | Secret (32-byte symmetric key) | **Co-chair browser RAM only** (the SHIPPED `CommitteeKeyHolder`, §3.16 F-145) | NEVER crosses any boundary (sealed client-side, Decision 4) | n/a (device) | session-scoped; six-trigger wipe (§3.16 F-145) — REUSED |
| Sealed wrap (data key → member pubkey) | Sealed-box ciphertext (the member's at-rest key access) | Postgres `committee_key_wraps` | the SEALED ct crosses B-WRAPFORMEMBER (in) | ca-central-1 | with the key; `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` |
| `identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap` audit row | Governance provenance (actor+target pseudonyms; NO pubkey bytes in meta) | Postgres `audit_log` | n/a | ca-central-1 | **`membership+7y`** (new enum, existing class; six-mirror) |

**No name/email/phone is newly REQUIRED by Phase 1.** The only NEW collection-adjacent artifact is the 6-digit code (a transient secret, never persisted) and the audited pubkey disclosure (a pseudonymous identifier already destined to be sealed-to). The purpose of every PI touchpoint is the **established committee-membership register** (ADR-0001/0004, unchanged): a member must have a `users` row + a passkey to be a committee member, and an `identity_keys.public_key` to receive the committee data key. Data minimization: the invite-time user row sets `role=NULL` (role is bound only on activation, `:290`) and the code is never stored — both are minimal-by-construction.

### Spoofing (S)

#### F-168 | S/E | HIGH — the repeatable, unauthenticated `redeem-invite` Edge Function (the single biggest new surface; NOT one-shot, NOT BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED-gated)

`redeem-invite` is `verify_jwt=false` and reachable by anyone with the public URL. Unlike `bootstrap-first-co-chair` (one-shot, advisory-lock + `EXISTS(users)` self-disabling, `:55-61`; `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED` default-deny edge gate, `:14-15`), the redeem EF is PERMANENTLY available and repeatable for the committee's life — by design (Decision 2b). Its ONLY gate is (a) a valid `invite_id` that is unconsumed + unexpired, (b) the matching 15-min TOTP, (c) origin pin + key-parity, (d) the verified-attestation registration. The threats this surface introduces: an attacker hits the EF (i) to ENUMERATE valid invite_ids or probe which invites are live; (ii) to MASS-trigger the challenge/register ceremony for resource exhaustion (DoS) without any code; (iii) to brute-force a 6-digit code against a known invite_id; (iv) to reach the `redeem_invite_complete` RPC directly (bypassing the EF) via a forged/stolen `mint_writer` token. This is the keystone surface; **security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign at P1-1 (the SQL) and P1-2 (the EF).**

- **Affected:** the `redeem-invite` EF (challenge + register actions); `redeem_invite_complete` (SQL terminal); the F-122/F-123 session-live-uniformity grep allowlist (NEW entry); `config.toml [functions.redeem-invite] verify_jwt=false`.
- **Likelihood:** MEDIUM (a `verify_jwt=false` public EF is internet-reachable; enumeration/flood require zero credentials — the attacker effort floor is low). **Impact:** HIGH (account-binding to a committee member's pre-created user row — the C2/C3/C4 trust tier). **Priority:** HIGH — co-sign at P1-1/P1-2.
- **Existing/required mitigation (the bootstrap hardening REUSED + the invite gate REPLACING the one-shot guard):**
  1. **`redeem_invite_complete` is `mint_writer`-ONLY** — `REVOKE ALL … FROM PUBLIC, anon, authenticated, service_role; GRANT … TO mint_writer` (mirrors `bootstrap_first_co_chair:124-127`). The terminal cannot be reached by a direct anon/authenticated REST RPC — only the EF's self-minted `mint_writer` token reaches it. The self-mint uses the isolated mint key (F-118; NEVER service_role).
  2. **Origin pin + key-parity at the edge** — `MINT_EXPECTED_ORIGINS` (reused from bootstrap) + `assertKeyParity` 503-on-mismatch (§3.14 F-124–126) run on BOTH the challenge and register actions BEFORE any DB call.
  3. **Verified-attestation-only** — ONLY the `verifyWebAuthnRegistration`-verified pubkey/credId reach `redeem_invite_complete`; a forged attestation is rejected at the EF (the bootstrap `auth.passkey.enroll_failed`-on-forgery posture, reused).
  4. **The invite gate REPLACES the one-shot guard** — the EF does NOT reuse `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED` (that flag stays default-deny so the one-shot path stays closed) and does NOT copy the `EXISTS(users)` guard (it must be repeatable). Its gate is: invite unconsumed + unexpired (`:271-273` re-check in `redeem_invite_complete` step i) + the TOTP (step ii).
  5. **Enumeration resistance** — `invite_id` is a `gen_random_uuid()` (122-bit unguessable, `:45`/`:249`); the redeem error oracle is NORMALIZED (F-169) so a probe cannot distinguish a non-existent invite_id from a consumed/expired one.
- **Testable mitigation (P1-1 / P1-2):**
  - _pgTAP (terminal grant lockdown, P1-1):_ assert `redeem_invite_complete` EXECUTE is REVOKED from PUBLIC/anon/authenticated/service_role and GRANTED to `mint_writer` ONLY (byte-for-byte the `bootstrap_first_co_chair` grant posture); a direct anon/authenticated call raises insufficient-privilege.
  - _deno test (origin + parity gate, P1-2):_ a `redeem-invite` call with a bad `origin` (not in `MINT_EXPECTED_ORIGINS`) is rejected BEFORE any DB call; a key-parity mismatch 503s before dispatch (reuse the bootstrap origin/parity fixtures).
  - _deno test (forged attestation rejected, P1-2):_ a register action with an attestation that fails `verifyWebAuthnRegistration` is rejected at the EF and NEVER calls `redeem_invite_complete` (assert the RPC transport is not invoked).
  - _grep self-test (allowlist re-pass, P1-2):_ `scripts/verify-session-live-uniformity.sh` includes `redeem-invite` in its explicit allowlist constant (alongside `mint-session/challenge`, `mint-session/assert`, `bootstrap-first-co-chair`) WITH a header note citing §3.18/F-168 as the threat-model re-pass that authorized it; the self-test fixture asserts the entry passes WITHOUT the `session_is_live()` gate (it is unauthenticated-by-necessity) but that its SQL terminal is `mint_writer`-only.

#### F-171 | S | Malicious redeemer RETARGETING — can a redeemer bind the invite to a DIFFERENT (attacker) user? (the construction must close it)

ADR-0029 Decision 2b claims the user row is created at ISSUE time and the redeemer NEVER supplies a uid, so retargeting is closed BY CONSTRUCTION. This finding VERIFIES that the construction actually closes it and writes the test that proves it. The threat: a malicious redeemer (with a valid code+invite) attempts to bind THEIR passkey to a uid OTHER than the invite's target — e.g. to an existing co-chair's user row (account-takeover-via-redeem) — by smuggling a `p_enrolling_uid` / `user_id` field through the EF or the RPC.

- **Affected:** `redeem_invite_complete` (must use `committee_invite.target_user_id`, NOT any caller-supplied uid); `committee_activate_membership` (the `:275-277` target=enrolling hard-bind); the redeem EF (must NOT accept/forward a caller uid).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (the construction closes it — IF built as designed). **Impact:** HIGH (a retarget would be an account-takeover of an arbitrary existing member). **Priority:** MEDIUM (low likelihood given the construction; HIGH impact if a regression reintroduces a caller-uid param).
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) `redeem_invite_complete` resolves the target ENTIRELY from the loaded `committee_invite.target_user_id` (set at issuance, FK-bound `:46`) — it has NO `p_enrolling_uid` / `p_user_id` parameter the caller controls; (2) it passes `p_enrolling_uid := invite.target_user_id` to `committee_activate_membership`, so the `v_inv.target_user_id <> p_enrolling_uid → invite_invalid` bind (`:275-277`) is satisfied BY CONSTRUCTION and the activation can ONLY touch the invite's own target; (3) the passkey INSERT in step (iv) uses the SAME `invite.target_user_id`, so the credential binds to the invited row, never an attacker-chosen one; (4) the redeem EF's request schema does NOT include any uid field (only `invite_id`, `totp_code`, verified credential fields).
- **Testable mitigation (P1-1 / P1-2):**
  - _pgTAP (no caller-controlled target, P1-1):_ assert `redeem_invite_complete`'s signature has NO uid/enrolling parameter; redeem a valid invite and assert the activated membership + the bound credential are BOTH on `committee_invite.target_user_id` and on NO other user; an attempt to influence the target (where the EF would forward one) is structurally impossible — the function reads the invite's own target.
  - _pgTAP (activation target hard-bind, carry-forward):_ assert `committee_activate_membership` RAISEs `invite_invalid` when `p_enrolling_uid <> v_inv.target_user_id` (`:275-277`) — the defense-in-depth re-check, even though `redeem_invite_complete` passes the invite's own target.
  - _deno test (EF schema has no uid, P1-2):_ assert the `redeem-invite` register payload schema rejects/ignores any `user_id`/`enrolling_uid` field; a request smuggling one does not change which user is activated.

### Tampering (T) / Replay

#### F-169 | T/S | Invite replay / multi-use — single-use enforcement, concurrent double-redeem (exactly-one-wins), and a NORMALIZED error oracle (consumed ≡ expired ≡ invalid)

The invite is the durable gate; if it could be redeemed twice, an intercepted code (F-170) plus the legitimate redeemer could BOTH bind a passkey, or an attacker could re-bind after the member. Two correctness properties: (1) single-use — `committee_invite.consumed_at` set atomically inside `redeem_invite_complete` (mirroring `committee_activate_membership:289`); (2) the error oracle is NORMALIZED — a consumed, an expired, and a never-existed invite must yield a BYTE-IDENTICAL error so an attacker cannot use the response to learn whether an invite_id is real-but-spent vs real-but-expired vs fictional (an enumeration/timing aid).

- **Affected:** `redeem_invite_complete` (the `FOR UPDATE` invite load + the consumed/expired/not-found branches in step i; the `consumed_at` write in step v via `committee_activate_membership:289`); the redeem EF error mapping (the normalized `{error}` surface); `committee_activate_membership` (`:271-273` consumed/expired re-check).
- **Likelihood:** MEDIUM (an intercepted or shoulder-surfed code makes replay the natural attack; concurrent redeem is a realistic race if a member double-submits). **Impact:** HIGH (a second successful redeem = a second account bound to the member's row, or an attacker re-binding). **Priority:** HIGH.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) `redeem_invite_complete` loads the invite `… FOR UPDATE` (mirrors `enroll_first_passkey:388-392` and `committee_activate_membership:279`) — concurrent redeems SERIALIZE on the row lock; the first to commit sets `consumed_at`, the second observes `consumed_at IS NOT NULL → invite_invalid`; (2) the consume is in the SAME txn as the activate + passkey-bind (atomic, F-177) — there is no window where the invite is consumed but the membership is not, or vice versa; (3) the TOTP is ALSO single-use (deleted on consume, `:428`) — even a re-presented valid code finds no bootstrap (`TOTP_BOOTSTRAP_NOT_FOUND`); (4) **normalized oracle:** consumed (`invite_invalid`), expired (`invite_invalid`), and never-existed (`invite_invalid`) all RAISE the SAME literal, and the EF maps all three to a BYTE-IDENTICAL `{error}` response (no "expired" vs "already used" vs "not found" discrimination).
- **Testable mitigation (P1-1 / P1-2):**
  - _pgTAP (single-use, P1-1):_ redeem a valid invite (succeeds, sets `consumed_at`); a SECOND redeem of the same invite_id → `invite_invalid` and NO second credential bound, NO second activation.
  - _pgTAP (concurrent double-redeem — exactly-one-wins, P1-1):_ two concurrent `redeem_invite_complete` calls on one invite (the `FOR UPDATE` race) → EXACTLY ONE commits a passkey+activation, the other raises `invite_invalid`; assert exactly one `webauthn_credentials` row + one active membership result (mirror the bootstrap advisory-lock TOCTOU pgTAP, ADR-0025).
  - _pgTAP/deno (normalized oracle, P1-1/P1-2):_ a consumed invite, an expired invite, and a random non-existent invite_id ALL yield the SAME `invite_invalid` SQL literal AND the EF returns a BYTE-IDENTICAL `{error}` JSON for all three (assert the three response bodies are byte-equal — no field, no message, no status-code difference distinguishes them).

### Information disclosure (I)

#### F-170 | I/S | HIGH — invite-code custody / interception (the CENTRAL threat): intercepted/shoulder-surfed/replayed code → impostor binds their passkey to the invited user row

The architect's central threat. The 6-digit code travels OUT-OF-BAND through the co-chair's own channel (no app-side delivery surface — the deliberate compliance win). But that channel is outside the app's control: the code can be intercepted in transit (a compromised messaging app, a forwarded email the co-chair used), shoulder-surfed, or socially engineered. An interceptor with `{invite_id, code}` within the 15-min TOTP window can run the redeem ceremony and bind THEIR passkey to the INVITED person's pre-created user row — becoming that member (an account-takeover OF THE INVITE, bounded to the invited role; NOT a privilege grab beyond it — F-171/F-173 bound the role). The legitimate invitee then finds the invite already consumed and alerts the co-chair. The question the architect posed: **is the residual acceptable for a ~12-person committee with out-of-band delivery?**

- **Affected:** the out-of-band delivery (outside the app boundary); the redeem ceremony (the 15-min TOTP window + the single-use invite + the 5-attempt lock); the co-chair-removal recovery path (`committee_remove_member`); the `member.added` audit row (the binding's forensic trace, `:293-300`).
- **Likelihood:** MEDIUM (interception of an out-of-band code is plausible — it is the weakest link, by the design's own admission). **Impact:** HIGH (account-takeover of a committee seat — read/file access to C2/C3/C4 once the member is also granted the key in Ceremony 4). **Priority:** HIGH — the central threat; co-sign at P1-1/P1-2.
- **RULING — the residual is ACCEPTED for Phase 1 (~12-person committee, out-of-band delivery), with the mitigation set below MANDATORY and the recovery path documented. Reasoning:**
  1. **The compensating controls bound the window tightly.** An interceptor needs BOTH the invite_id AND the code AND must act within the **15-min TOTP window** (`auth_totp_bootstraps.expires_at`, `:263`, the SECURITY-critical non-extendable clock) — the invite's longer 7-day TTL does NOT widen the brute/replay window because a stale TOTP fails (`:406-408`) and re-issuing the TOTP is a co-chair action (F-175). The **5-attempt lock** (`:413-419`) defeats online brute force of the 6-digit code (a blind guess is 1-in-a-million per attempt, locked after 5). The **single-use invite** (F-169) means the FIRST successful redeem wins and the second (legitimate or attacker) is locked out — making the takeover DETECTABLE (the loser sees `invite_invalid`).
  2. **The takeover is bounded to the invited role and fully attributable + reversible.** Even a successful interception only binds the attacker as the INVITED member (the invited role array, F-173) — it is NOT an escalation beyond what the co-chair chose to grant. The binding emits `member.added` (`:293-300`, attributable to the issuing co-chair's pseudonym + the timestamp); the co-chair, alerted by the legitimate invitee, runs `committee_remove_member` (existing) and the audit trail reconstructs exactly what happened. Critically, the attacker does NOT get committee-DATA access from the redeem alone — Ceremony 4 (grant-key) is a SEPARATE co-chair action with a fingerprint confirmation (F-172), so a vigilant co-chair never seals the key to an impostor.
  3. **Out-of-band delivery is the RIGHT call despite this residual** — adding an email/SMS subprocessor to "secure" delivery would add a cross-border/PI-bearing surface (a NEW interception point + a new subprocessor + a likely cross-border transfer) that is WORSE than the out-of-band residual for this audience. The compliance win (zero subprocessor, §6) outweighs the marginal interception risk at ~12 people.
- **Existing/required mitigation (all MANDATORY):** (1) 15-min TOTP window, non-extendable (`:263`); (2) 5-attempt lock on wrong code (`:413-419`, reused via `redeem_invite_complete` step ii); (3) single-use invite (F-169) — first-redeem-wins, takeover is detectable; (4) short invite TTL (Decision 3: 7 days, with re-send for a fresh TOTP — F-175); (5) the code is member-ENTERED, never in a URL/link (the link carries only `invite_id`) — keeps the code off proxy logs/browser history/referrer headers (constraints "No PII in URL query strings"); (6) `member.added` audit trail makes every binding attributable + the takeover reconstructable; (7) the co-chair-removal recovery path + the Ceremony-4 fingerprint gate (a co-chair grants the data key only after confirming the member, so an impostor never gets C2/C3/C4 data if the co-chair is vigilant).
- **Testable mitigation (P1-1 / P1-2):**
  - _pgTAP (15-min window + lock, P1-1):_ a redeem with a code whose bootstrap `expires_at < now()` → `TOTP_BOOTSTRAP_EXPIRED`, no binding; five wrong codes set `locked_at` and the sixth → `TOTP_BOOTSTRAP_LOCKED` (reuse the `enroll_first_passkey:402-419` lock fixtures against `redeem_invite_complete`).
  - _deno test (code never in URL, P1-2/P1-7):_ assert the `/redeem` link/route carries ONLY `invite_id` and NEVER the code; the code is entered in the form, never appended to the URL/query (cross-ref F-176).
  - _pgTAP (binding is attributable, P1-1):_ a successful redeem emits `member.added` carrying the ISSUING co-chair's pseudonym + the target — the forensic trace for a takeover reconstruction.
  - _pgTAP (takeover is detectable via single-use, carry-forward F-169):_ after a redeem, a second redeem of the same invite → `invite_invalid` (the loser's signal that someone already bound).

#### F-174 | I | HIGH — pubkey-disclosure deanonymization: `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` maps member-uid → pubkey (the first crack in the read-locked identity_keys)

`identity_keys` is otherwise fully read-locked (`REVOKE SELECT … FROM authenticated, anon`, `:122`) — NO RPC returns another user's pubkey today. The new `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` is the first deliberate disclosure of ANOTHER member's `public_key`. The pubkey is PSEUDONYMOUS (not direct PI), but disclosing WHICH member-uid maps to WHICH pubkey is a (small) re-identification aid — and it interacts with the `_committee_pseudonym` lockdown that keeps audit actors pseudonymous: a member who could enumerate uid↔pubkey could, in principle, correlate a pseudonymous audit actor to a pubkey seen elsewhere. The threats: (i) the RPC is over-exposed (readable by any member, not just co-chairs) enabling bulk enumeration of the uid↔pubkey map; (ii) no audit trail on disclosure; (iii) the pubkey BYTES leak into the audit `meta` (defeating the pseudonymity of the audit row itself).

- **Affected:** the new `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` RPC; the new `identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap` audit enum (six-mirror); the `identity_keys` read-lock (`:122`, must STAY locked — the RPC is the ONLY crack); the aspirational comment fix (`:118-121`).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (co-chair-gated; no bulk endpoint). **Impact:** MEDIUM (a re-identification aid — uid↔pubkey; HIGH only if it became bulk-enumerable or leaked into the pseudonymous audit). **Priority:** MEDIUM — co-sign at P1-4.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) **co-chair-ONLY** — gated `session_is_live()` + `_committee_is_active_co_chair(auth.uid())` (STRICTER than `_t07_gate_active_member` — pubkey disclosure is a co-chair governance action, not a member-level read; Decision 4); a non-co-chair member CANNOT read another member's pubkey; (2) **per-disclosure AUDIT-BEFORE-RETURN** — `identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap` (actor=co-chair pseudonym, target=member) emits BEFORE the bytes return (mirrors `reveal_concern_source` / `get_committee_key_wrap_for_self` audit-before-return), so every uid→pubkey disclosure leaves a forensic trace; (3) **NO bulk-enumeration endpoint** — the RPC takes a SINGLE `p_member_user_id` and returns ONE pubkey; there is no "list all pubkeys" surface; (4) **the audit meta carries NO pubkey bytes** — only the actor + target pseudonyms (the disclosure is recorded WITHOUT re-leaking the pubkey into the audit, preserving the audit's own pseudonymity); (5) the `identity_keys` table read-lock (`:122`) is UNCHANGED — the RPC is the only path; (6) the aspirational comment (`:118-121`) is corrected to point at the real disclosure path (doc-only, no behavior).
- **Testable mitigation (P1-4):**
  - _pgTAP (co-chair-only gate):_ a co-chair gets an active member's pubkey + fingerprint; a NON-co-chair member call raises `rls_denied`; an anon/`authenticated`-but-non-member call is denied; the `identity_keys` table itself stays `REVOKE SELECT` (assert a direct SELECT is denied).
  - _pgTAP (audit-before-return + meta has no pubkey bytes):_ assert `identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap` is emitted BEFORE the function returns the bytes (inject-failure pattern: a failure after the emit still leaves the audit row); assert the audit `meta` contains the actor + target pseudonyms but NO `public_key` byte field.
  - _pgTAP (no bulk enumeration):_ assert the RPC signature takes a single `p_member_user_id` and returns a single pubkey — there is no list/all variant; a member-without-identity → `member_not_enrolled`/`not_found` (no pubkey, but STILL no enumeration of who-has-vs-hasn't beyond the single queried uid).
  - _pgTAP (six-mirror, P1-4):_ assert `identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap` passes all six: the `audit_log.event_type` CHECK accepts it; the `audit_log_retention_schedule` has its row; `retention_class_for('identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap') = 'membership+7y'` (sibling of `member.added`, `:92`); the `audit_emit` allowlist includes it; emission succeeds; a NON-allowlisted sibling string is rejected.

#### F-176 | I | Code / TOTP / key-material leakage into logs, URLs, storage, or audit-meta (the P1-10 CI gate)
