Phase 1 handles, transiently: the 6-digit one-time code (issue/reissue EF response + member entry), the raw TOTP code (member-entered at redeem), the plaintext committee data key (co-chair's session-resident holder, §3.16 F-145 — REUSED), the member's identity privkey (device-custody), the member's pubkey bytes, and the sealed wrap ciphertext. Any of {raw code, raw TOTP, plaintext data key, privkey} landing in `console.*`, a thrown error message/stack, the structured-log path, an audit `meta`, sessionStorage/localStorage/IndexedDB, or a URL is a confidentiality break. The 6-digit code and the data key are the highest-harm transients; the privkey is the E2EE root. This EXTENDS the existing key-material-never-logged CI gate (ADR-0026 P0a-6 / ADR-0027 P2a-10 / §3.16 F-148 / §3.15 F-132) to the redeem EF + the issue path + `wrapMemberInViaProduction`.

- **Affected:** `redeem-invite` EF (must log closed-literal reasons only, never the code/TOTP/credential secrets); the committee-op `issue_invite`/`reissue_totp` handlers (the raw code in the response body ONLY); `issueInviteViaProduction` / `wrapMemberInViaProduction` (the data key + the seal); the `/redeem` route (code/TOTP never in URL/storage); all error/toast/log surfaces touched by the flows.
- **Likelihood:** LOW (mitigated by the CI gate). **Impact:** HIGH (a leaked code/TOTP enables impersonation in-window; a leaked data key defeats the E2EE model; a leaked privkey is the E2EE root). **Priority:** HIGH — the P1-10 CI gate.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the raw code exists server-side ONLY in the single issue/reissue statement frame (the SQL computes `secret_hash` from the passed code and persists only the HMAC, mirroring `enroll_first_passkey:410-412`/`:425-426`) and in the EF RESPONSE BODY once — NEVER in logs/audit/persistence; (2) the redeem EF logs closed-literal reasons only (the `bootstrap-first-co-chair` reason-only logging posture, reused); (3) the invite link carries only the opaque `invite_id`, never the code (F-170/F-176 — code is member-entered, never in URL); (4) the plaintext data key exists ONLY in the heap holder, NEVER serialized (§3.16 F-145/F-146, REUSED) and is sealed CLIENT-side (never sent to the server, Decision 4); (5) the privkey is device-custody, never sent (ADR-0026); (6) audit emission is server-owned — the client cannot put the code/key/privkey into audit meta; (7) the pubkey-disclosure audit meta carries NO pubkey bytes (F-174).
- **Testable mitigation (P1-10 CI gate — extends the §3.16 F-148 / §3.15 F-132 leak-sweep gate):**
  - _vitest (full-workflow leak sweep):_ instrument `console.*`, captured thrown-error `.message`/`.stack`, the structured-log emit surface, and any client-constructed audit `meta`; run issue + reissue + redeem (challenge+register) + grant-key (happy + each error branch); assert NONE of {the 6-digit raw code, the raw TOTP, the 32-byte plaintext data key, the identity privkey bytes} appears in any captured surface.
  - _vitest (no serialization, REUSED §3.16):_ assert the raw code, the data key, and the privkey are NOT readable from `sessionStorage`/`localStorage`/IndexedDB/URL/any serialized store at any point of the redeem + grant flows.
  - _deno test (EF logs reasons only):_ a `redeem-invite` failure logs a closed-literal reason (`invite_invalid`/normalized), NEVER the submitted `totp_code`/`invite_id`/credential secrets.
  - _CI grep (uniformity, P1-10):_ extend the existing key-material-leak grep to flag any redeem/issue/wrap path passing the raw code, the raw TOTP, the data-key buffer, or the privkey into a log/toast/error/audit-meta constructor (the Decision 8 canary as a CI gate).

### Denial of service (D)

#### F-175 | D/S | TOTP issuance / re-send abuse + resource exhaustion on the unauthenticated redeem surface

Two DoS facets. (1) **Issuance side (authenticated):** only an active co-chair can `issue_invite` / `reissue_totp` (gated `_committee_is_active_co_chair`); abuse is bounded by `UNIQUE(user_id)` cap-of-1 on `auth_totp_bootstraps` (`:268`, so re-send is a delete-then-insert, not unbounded accumulation) + the 15-min expiry + the audit trail (every issue is attributable). A co-chair spamming invites inflates their OWN attributable rows (self-limited). (2) **Redeem side (unauthenticated, the real DoS surface):** the `verify_jwt=false` redeem EF can be hit by anyone — a flood of challenge actions (cheap, no code needed) or register actions (forces a `verifyWebAuthnRegistration` + a DB round-trip) is the cheapest way to load the surface. Clock-skew on the TOTP is a correctness facet: a member's/server's clock drift near the 15-min boundary could spuriously expire a valid code.

- **Affected:** `issue_member_invite` / `reissue_member_totp` (co-chair-gated, `UNIQUE(user_id)` cap); the unauthenticated `redeem-invite` EF (the flood surface); the 15-min TOTP boundary (clock-skew).
- **Likelihood:** MEDIUM (the unauthenticated redeem EF is internet-reachable — a flood needs zero credentials). **Impact:** MEDIUM (a redeem flood degrades the EF / DB; issuance abuse is self-limited + attributable). **Priority:** MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) **issuance is bounded** — co-chair-gated + `UNIQUE(user_id)` cap-of-1 (re-send replaces, never accumulates, `:268`) + 15-min expiry + per-issue audit; the OLD code stops validating on re-send (delete-then-insert); (2) **the challenge action leaks nothing and does no expensive work** before the code/TOTP check — the code is validated only at the `register` action's `redeem_invite_complete` step ii (so a code-less flood cannot reach the lock-state-mutating path); (3) **rate-limiting on the redeem EF** — the EF SHOULD apply per-IP / per-invite_id rate limiting on the register action (constraints "Rate limiting and abuse controls on auth endpoints"); a flood is bounded at the edge before the DB; (4) **the 5-attempt lock** caps per-invite brute-force regardless of flood (`:413-419`); (5) **clock-skew** — the 15-min window is generous relative to realistic NTP drift (seconds); the server `now()` is authoritative (`:406-408` compares against server time, not a client clock), so member-clock skew does NOT affect validity — only the member's PERCEPTION of remaining time; the re-send path (F-175 facet 1) is the recovery for a genuinely-expired code.
- **Testable mitigation (P1-2 / P1-3 / P1-6):**
  - _pgTAP (re-send replaces, old code dies, P1-6):_ `reissue_member_totp` upserts the bootstrap (fresh `secret_hash` + fresh `expires_at` + reset `wrong_attempts`/`locked_at`); the OLD code NO LONGER validates against the new hash; a non-co-chair `reissue_totp` → `rls_denied`; the `UNIQUE(user_id)` invariant holds (exactly one bootstrap per user after re-send).
  - _deno test (challenge does no code work / register rate-limited, P1-2):_ the `redeem-invite` `challenge` action does NOT touch `auth_totp_bootstraps` (no code check, no lock mutation); the `register` action applies the rate-limit/abuse control (assert the control is present — per-invite_id / per-IP throttle) before the DB round-trip.
  - _pgTAP (server-clock authoritative, clock-skew safe, P1-1):_ a redeem with the SERVER clock past `expires_at` → `TOTP_BOOTSTRAP_EXPIRED` regardless of any client-asserted time (the function compares `now() >= v_bootstrap.expires_at`, `:406`, never a client field).

### Elevation of privilege (E)

#### F-172 | E/T | HIGH — wrapping the data key to an ATTACKER-controlled pubkey (a compromised/malicious co-chair client seals the committee data key to a pubkey it controls)

The wrap-for-member composition (Ceremony 4) seals the committee data key to a pubkey and lands it via `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member`. The threat: a compromised or malicious co-chair CLIENT seals the data key to an ATTACKER-controlled pubkey (instead of the intended member's), giving the attacker the ability to `crypto_box_seal_open` the committee data key — a full E2EE compromise. The defense rests on the server returning the AUDITED enrolled pubkey for a specific member uid (the co-chair cannot substitute), a fingerprint confirmation, and the wrap audit binding actor+target+key. **CRITICAL: the rejected server-side-seal alternative (which would require the plaintext data key to touch the server) MUST stay rejected** — it would convert the E2EE system into a server-trusts system for its most sensitive key (ADR-0003 Invariant 1/5/6). **security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign at P1-4 (the disclosure RPC) and P1-5 (the wrap composition).**

- **Affected:** `wrapMemberInViaProduction` (the seal composition, Decision 5); `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` (the server-bound pubkey↔member source, F-174); `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member` (the active-member re-assert `:502-503`); the co-chair grant UI (the fingerprint confirmation, Decision 6); the REJECTED server-side-seal (must stay rejected).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (requires a compromised co-chair client; the server-bound pubkey + fingerprint + audit are layered). **Impact:** HIGH (sealing the data key to an attacker pubkey = a full E2EE compromise — the attacker can open the committee data key). **Priority:** HIGH — co-sign at P1-4/P1-5.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) **the co-chair seals to a pubkey the SERVER returned for a specific member uid** — `wrapMemberInViaProduction` obtains the pubkey from `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap(member_uid)` (F-174), which binds pubkey↔member server-side; the co-chair client cannot substitute an attacker pubkey for the member's (it receives what the server has on file); (2) **`wrap_committee_data_key_for_member` re-asserts the TARGET is an active member** (`is_active_member(p_member_user_id)`, `:502-503`) — a wrap can only land for an active member, not an arbitrary attacker uid; (3) **fingerprint confirmation in the UI** — the grant flow shows the member's pubkey FINGERPRINT (returned by F-174) so the co-chair visually confirms the intended target before committing (Decision 5/6); (4) **the wrap audit binds actor+target+key** — `committee_data_key.wrapped_for_member` records the co-chair pseudonym + target member + key_id (`:512-521`), so a mis-wrap is attributable + reconstructable; (5) **the plaintext data key is sealed CLIENT-side** (`crypto_box_seal`, libsodium, sender-anonymous — the co-chair's privkey is not even needed) — it NEVER touches the server (Decision 4 rejects server-side seal); (6) **a wrong wrap is self-detecting** — if a bad seal lands, the member's `crypto_box_seal_open` fails (the bytes don't open) and they stay in the holding state, recoverable by re-granting (the `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` means a re-grant needs the prior bad wrap removed first — flag the "re-grant overwrites" sub-case).
- **Testable mitigation (P1-4 / P1-5):**
  - _hermetic test (seal to the server-disclosed pubkey, P1-5):_ `wrapMemberInViaProduction` seals the data key to the pubkey RETURNED by `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` (not a client-supplied one); the member's keypair can `crypto_box_seal_open` the wrap back to the SAME 32 data-key bytes; assert the composition does NOT accept a caller-supplied pubkey that bypasses the disclosure RPC.
  - _pgTAP (active-member re-assert, carry-forward):_ `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member` raises `rls_denied` when the target is NOT an active member (`:502-503`) — a wrap cannot land for an inactive/non-member uid.
  - _hermetic test (server-side seal stays REJECTED, P1-5):_ assert there is NO RPC/EF that accepts a PLAINTEXT data key for server-side sealing (grep/structural: no `wrap_member_server_side`-shaped function); the plaintext data key NEVER appears in any request payload to the server (cross-ref F-176, ADR-0003 Invariant 1/5/6).
  - _hermetic test (fingerprint confirmation surfaced, P1-8):_ the grant UI surfaces the member's pubkey fingerprint (from F-174) for confirmation BEFORE the wrap call; assert the fingerprint shown equals the fingerprint of the disclosed pubkey.
  - _hermetic test (wrong wrap self-detects + re-grant, P1-5):_ a wrap sealed to the WRONG pubkey causes the member's `crypto_box_seal_open` to FAIL (they stay in the holding state, no silent wrong-key success); a re-grant after removing the bad wrap lands a correct one (the `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` "re-grant overwrites" sub-case).

#### F-173 | E | Role escalation via the invite role array (`worker_co_chair` self-grant; tampering with the role set between issue and activate)

`committee_invite_member` validates the role array `<@ {worker_member, worker_co_chair, certified_member}` (`:237-240`) — a co-chair CAN invite another `worker_co_chair`. The threats: (i) a malicious/compromised co-chair invites a `worker_co_chair` CONFEDERATE (a deliberate escalation of their faction); (ii) the role set is TAMPERED with between issue (Ceremony 1) and activate (Ceremony 2) — e.g. a redeemer elevates their own role from `worker_member` to `worker_co_chair`.

- **Affected:** `committee_invite_member` (the role-array validation `:237-240`); `committee_activate_membership` (sets `users.role` from the MEMBERSHIP role, `:290`, NOT a redeemer-supplied value); the invite role array (set at issue, immutable thereafter).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (facet i is within the co-chair trust model; facet ii is closed by the construction). **Impact:** MEDIUM (a co-chair confederate; bounded by the existing co-chair trust + audit). **Priority:** MEDIUM (facet i ACCEPTED within the trust model; facet ii must be VERIFIED closed).
- **RULING — facet (i) is ACCEPTED within the existing co-chair trust model; facet (ii) must be CLOSED by construction.** A co-chair inviting a `worker_co_chair` is INTENDED (the spec's "2nd co-chair" — ADR-0025/0029); the escalation risk (a co-chair inviting a confederate) is the SAME trust the existing `committee_set_roles` already vests in a co-chair, bounded by the audit trail (`member.added` records the issuer + the roles, `:293-300`) and the human-governance posture. It is NOT a new escalation surface. Facet (ii) — a redeemer elevating their own role — must be structurally impossible.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) the role array is set at ISSUE time in `committee_invite` (`:250-251`) + the pending membership (`:246-247`) — it is server-bound to the invite, NOT supplied at redeem; (2) `committee_activate_membership` sets `users.role := _committee_primary_role(v_mem.role)` from the MEMBERSHIP's role (`:290`), NOT any redeemer-supplied value — the redeemer cannot elevate their own role at activation; (3) `redeem_invite_complete` does NOT accept a role parameter (the role is read from the pre-set membership); (4) the role-array validation `<@ {worker_member, worker_co_chair, certified_member}` (`:237-240`) bounds the role set to the allowed enum — no out-of-band role can be smuggled in; (5) facet (i) is bounded by the `member.added` audit + the co-chair trust model (accepted, per the ruling).
- **Testable mitigation (P1-1 / P1-3):**
  - _pgTAP (redeemer cannot self-elevate, P1-1):_ issue an invite with `roles := {worker_member}`; redeem it (where the EF/RPC schema has no role field); assert the activated membership + `users.role` are `worker_member` — NOT a redeemer-supplied `worker_co_chair`; an attempt to smuggle a role through the redeem payload does not change the activated role.
  - _pgTAP (role-array validation, carry-forward):_ `issue_member_invite` / `committee_invite_member` raises `invalid_role` for a role array NOT `<@ {worker_member, worker_co_chair, certified_member}` (`:237-240`); a `worker_co_chair` invite by a co-chair SUCCEEDS (the accepted facet-i case) and emits `member.added` with the role recorded.
  - _pgTAP (non-co-chair cannot issue, carry-forward):_ a non-co-chair `issue_invite` → `rls_denied` (the `_committee_is_active_co_chair` gate, `:233-235`) — only a co-chair can grant any role.

### Atomicity / race (the failure-mode findings)

#### F-177 | T/D | Atomicity & race: partial state (user created but passkey not bound), invite-expires-mid-redeem, two concurrent redeems of one code

The redeem ceremony composes consume-TOTP + bind-passkey + activate-membership + consume-invite. A partial commit (e.g. passkey bound but membership not activated, or invite consumed but no credential) would leave a corrupt onboarding state. The architect's atomicity claim (Decision 2b / Failure-mode analysis) must be VERIFIED: redemption is ONE txn inside `redeem_invite_complete`, all-or-nothing. Plus the invite-expires-mid-redeem and concurrent-double-redeem races (the latter overlaps F-169; this finding pins the PARTIAL-STATE + mid-redeem-expiry facets the test-writer turns into pgTAP).

- **Affected:** `redeem_invite_complete` (the single-txn composition: consume-TOTP + bind-passkey + activate + consume-invite); the issue path `issue_member_invite` (its own single-txn create-user + TOTP + pending-membership + invite); `committee_activate_membership` (`:271-273` mid-redeem expiry re-check).
- **Likelihood:** LOW (single-txn by design). **Impact:** MEDIUM (a partial state = a corrupt half-onboarded member; recoverable but confusing). **Priority:** MEDIUM.
- **Existing/required mitigation:** (1) **redemption is ONE txn** — `redeem_invite_complete` does consume-TOTP (delete bootstrap) + bind-passkey + `committee_activate_membership` (flip active + consume invite + emit `member.added`) all inside one transaction frame; a failure at ANY step ROLLS BACK whole — no passkey-bound-but-inactive split, no invite-consumed-but-no-credential split; (2) **issuance is ONE txn** — `issue_member_invite` does create-user + TOTP-issue + pending-membership + invite all-or-nothing (a partial issue leaves no danglers — no orphan user without an invite); (3) **invite-expires-mid-redeem** — `redeem_invite_complete` loads the invite `FOR UPDATE` and re-checks `expires_at < now()` (mirroring `committee_activate_membership:271-273`) → `invite_invalid`, whole txn rolls back, no binding; (4) **the ONE intentionally-committed side effect on a bad code** is the `wrong_attempts`/`locked_at` mutation (matching `enroll_first_passkey:413-419`) — this is a deliberate exception to the all-or-nothing (the lock counter must persist across attempts), and it is the ONLY mutation that survives a rolled-back redeem; (5) **post-redeem identity-enroll is a SEPARATE txn by necessity** (client-driven, needs a session) — an active-member-without-identity is a VALID resumable state (Phase 0a-style, ADR-0026), NOT a corrupt partial.
- **Testable mitigation (P1-1):**
  - _pgTAP (redeem is all-or-nothing):_ inject a failure AFTER the passkey INSERT but BEFORE `committee_activate_membership` → assert the WHOLE txn rolls back: NO credential bound, NO membership activated, the invite STILL unconsumed, the bootstrap STILL present (no half-onboarded state).
  - _pgTAP (issue is all-or-nothing):_ inject a failure after the user INSERT but before the invite INSERT → assert NO orphan `public.users` row survives (no danglers).
  - _pgTAP (invite-expires-mid-redeem):_ a redeem where the invite `expires_at < now()` → `invite_invalid`, whole rollback, no binding (the `FOR UPDATE` + expiry re-check).
  - _pgTAP (lock-counter is the one persisting side effect):_ a redeem with a WRONG code rolls back the activation but PERSISTS the `wrong_attempts++` / `locked_at` mutation (the deliberate exception, mirroring `:413-419`); assert the counter survived the rollback.
  - _pgTAP (concurrent double-redeem, cross-ref F-169):_ two concurrent redeems on one invite → exactly one commits a complete onboarding, the other rolls back whole with `invite_invalid` (no partial state from the loser).

### §6 — Phase 1 compliance / breach-notification verification (PIPEDA s.10.1)

ADR-0029 introduces **no new PI field collected** (`display_name`/`off_employer_contact` are EXISTING optional invite fields, `committee_invite_member:215-216`; hard rule 6 N/A), **no new subprocessor**, **no new region** (all rows land in the existing ca-central-1 project, ADR-0001), and **no new retention class** (the one new audit enum `identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap` maps to the EXISTING `membership+7y` class, `retention_class_for:92`). The 6-digit code is a transient secret (never persisted/logged — F-176). The central compliance win is **out-of-band invite delivery**: NO email/SMS provider, so Phase 1 adds ZERO cross-border / subprocessor / PI-bearing delivery surface (hard rules 3/4 N/A by construction).

**PIPEDA fair-information principle mapping (the Phase 1 deltas):**

- **P1 Accountability / P2 Identifying purposes:** the purpose of every Phase 1 touchpoint is the ESTABLISHED committee-membership register (ADR-0001/0004) — a member needs a `users` row + passkey to be a member, and a pubkey to receive the data key. No new purpose; the issue/redeem/grant flow serves the existing membership-administration purpose.
- **P3 Consent / P4 Limiting collection:** **data-minimal by construction.** The invite-time user row sets `role=NULL` (role bound only at activation, `:290`); the code is never stored (only its HMAC, ≤15min); `display_name`/`off_employer_contact` are OPTIONAL (not required to onboard); no name/email/phone is REQUIRED. The pubkey is pseudonymous and already destined to be sealed-to. Nothing beyond what membership administration needs is collected.
- **P5 Limiting use/disclosure/retention:** **HONORED, with one new bounded disclosure** — the pubkey disclosure (F-174) is LIMITED to a co-chair (co-chair-gated), to a SINGLE member per call (no bulk), AUDITED per disclosure (`identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap`), and the audit meta carries NO pubkey bytes. The TOTP is ≤15min then deleted (`:428`); the invite is single-use + ≤7-day TTL. Retention: the one new audit enum on the existing `membership+7y` class.
- **P6 Accuracy / P8 Openness / P9 Individual access / P10 Challenging compliance:** unchanged — no new processing beyond the established membership lifecycle.
- **P7 Safeguards:** **APPROPRIATE to the new surfaces.** The unauthenticated redeem EF is gated by invite+TOTP+single-use+TTL+5-attempt-lock+origin-pin+key-parity+verified-attestation + a `mint_writer`-only SQL terminal (F-168/F-170); the pubkey disclosure is co-chair-gated + audited (F-174); the wrap seals client-side (the plaintext data key never touches the server — F-172, ADR-0003 Invariant 1/5/6); the code/key/privkey never log (F-176). MFA preserved (the member ends with a passkey + the TOTP was the bootstrap second factor — ADR-0002).

**Breach-notification trigger assessment (the two new surfaces, assessed head-on):**

The two candidate s.10.1 concerns are (a) an account-takeover-via-intercepted-code (F-170) and (b) a pubkey-disclosure deanonymization (F-174). **Neither, as designed, is a breach of security safeguards.** (a) The redeem surface is a GOVERNED control: even a successful interception is bounded to the invited role, is single-use-detectable, emits an attributable `member.added`, and does NOT grant committee-DATA access (Ceremony 4 is a separate co-chair action with a fingerprint gate). An interception is an out-of-band custody failure, not an app-safeguard failure — and the compensating controls (15-min TOTP, lock, single-use, removal path) keep the residual acceptable (F-170 ruling). **WHERE s.10.1 WOULD fire:** if the 6-digit code, the plaintext committee data key, or a member's privkey LEAKED into logs/URL/storage (F-176) — a leaked data key is a full E2EE compromise of the committee's C2/C3/C4 register (an unauthorized disclosure with real risk of significant harm); this is exactly why F-176 (the P1-10 CI gate) is HIGH-priority and test-blocking. (b) The pubkey disclosure is co-chair-gated + per-disclosure-audited + non-bulk + carries no pubkey bytes in the audit — a governed disclosure, not a safeguard failure; **s.10.1 WOULD fire** only if the RPC became bulk-enumerable or member-readable (F-174's mitigations are what keep it on the right side). **A successful wrap-to-attacker-pubkey (F-172) WOULD be an s.10.1 trigger** (the attacker gains the committee data key) — which is why the server-bound pubkey + fingerprint + active-member re-assert + audit are mandatory and the server-side-seal stays rejected.

**Conclusion: Phase 1 introduces NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 breach-notification trigger AS DESIGNED.** The redeem surface, the pubkey disclosure, and the wrap are governed controls with mandatory, testable mitigations; the s.10.1 triggers are the FAILURE modes of those controls (a leaked code/key/privkey — F-176; a bulk/over-exposed pubkey RPC — F-174; a wrap-to-attacker — F-172), and each is closed by an implementation-blocking test. The 24-month breach-record-keeping obligation is unchanged. **No PHIPA trigger** (no health information — committee onboarding captures no PHI; if a future field captured identifiable health info, PHIPA's 60-day notice + custodian + lockbox would fire — flagged as a re-pass trigger). **No PCI trigger** (no payment data). **No cross-border transfer** introduced — all data stays in ca-central-1; out-of-band delivery means no delivery-channel subprocessor.

### Cross-border & subprocessor assessment

**No cross-border transfer and no new subprocessor are introduced by Phase 1.** All onboarding data (the user row, the TOTP HMAC, the invite, the passkey credential, the identity pubkey, the sealed wrap, the audit rows) lands in the existing ca-central-1 Supabase project (ADR-0001, re-confirmed). The 6-digit code crosses B2 only browser↔Edge-Function (in-region) and is conveyed OUT-OF-BAND through the co-chair's OWN channel — there is NO app-side delivery subprocessor (no email/SMS provider), which is the deliberate compliance win. The pubkey + fingerprint cross B-PUBKEY only in-region. **There is nothing to approve under the cross-border human gate for this feature** (explicitly: all data remains in ca-central-1; no Sentry/SendGrid/US-region path is touched). The co-chair's out-of-band channel is OUTSIDE the app's processing boundary (it is the co-chair's own messaging) — it is not a subprocessor the app integrates; the residual interception risk of that channel is assessed at F-170 (accepted).

### Top 5 prioritized risks (Phase 1 only; for the parent agent's summary)

1. **F-168 (HIGH) — the repeatable, unauthenticated `redeem-invite` EF (the single biggest new surface):** `verify_jwt=false`, NOT one-shot, NOT `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED`-gated. Mitigation: the SQL terminal `redeem_invite_complete` is `mint_writer`-ONLY (REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/authenticated/service_role, mirroring `bootstrap_first_co_chair:124-127`); origin-pin + key-parity + verified-attestation at the edge; the invite+TOTP gate REPLACES the one-shot guard; `invite_id` is a 122-bit uuid + a normalized error oracle defeat enumeration; `redeem-invite` is added to the F-122/F-123 grep allowlist (this §3.18 IS the mandated re-pass). **Co-sign at P1-1/P1-2.**
2. **F-170 (HIGH) — invite-code custody / interception (the CENTRAL threat):** an intercepted/shoulder-surfed code → impostor binds their passkey to the invited user row (account-takeover of the invite, bounded to the invited role). **RULED acceptable** for a ~12-person committee with out-of-band delivery, mitigation set MANDATORY: 15-min TOTP window + 5-attempt lock + single-use invite (takeover detectable) + short TTL + code-never-in-URL + `member.added` attribution + the co-chair-removal recovery + the Ceremony-4 fingerprint gate (impostor gets no DATA access without a separate, confirmed grant). **Co-sign at P1-1/P1-2.**
3. **F-172 (HIGH) — wrap-to-attacker-pubkey (a full E2EE compromise if it succeeds):** a compromised co-chair client seals the data key to an attacker pubkey. Mitigation: the co-chair seals to the SERVER-disclosed pubkey for a specific member uid (cannot substitute, F-174); `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member` re-asserts the target is active (`:502-503`); UI fingerprint confirmation; the wrap audit binds actor+target+key (`:512-521`); the plaintext data key is sealed CLIENT-side and NEVER touches the server (server-side seal STAYS rejected — ADR-0003 Invariant 1/5/6); a wrong wrap self-detects (the member's `seal_open` fails). **Co-sign at P1-4/P1-5.**
4. **F-176 (HIGH) — code/TOTP/key-material leakage (the P1-10 CI gate; the s.10.1 trip-wire):** the 6-digit code, the raw TOTP, the plaintext data key, and the privkey must never hit logs/errors/audit-meta/storage/URL. Mitigation: full-workflow leak-sweep CI gate across issue/reissue/redeem/grant + no-serialization scan + reason-only EF logging + code-only-in-response-body; extends the §3.16 F-148 / §3.15 F-132 gate. A leaked data key/privkey is the one Phase 1 outcome that WOULD meet s.10.1 — which is why this is test-blocking (P1-10).
5. **F-174 (MED→HIGH-adjacent) — pubkey-disclosure deanonymization (the first crack in the read-locked `identity_keys`):** `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` maps member-uid → pubkey. Mitigation: co-chair-ONLY gate (stricter than member-level); per-disclosure audit-before-return (`identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap`, six-mirror, `membership+7y`); NO bulk-enumeration endpoint (single uid per call); the audit meta carries NO pubkey bytes; the `identity_keys` table read-lock (`:122`) stays — the RPC is the only crack. **Co-sign at P1-4.** (F-171 retargeting, F-173 role-escalation, F-169 replay, F-175 DoS, F-177 atomicity are MED and ride below the top 5.)

### Handoff packets

- **To test-writer (priority order; each test RED against `main` before its implementer PR opens; P1-N = ADR-0029 increment):**
  1. **F-168 (HIGH, P1-1/P1-2) — the unauthenticated redeem surface:** pgTAP — `redeem_invite_complete` EXECUTE REVOKED from PUBLIC/anon/authenticated/service_role + GRANTED `mint_writer` ONLY; a direct anon/authenticated call denied. deno — bad-origin rejected pre-DB; key-parity 503 pre-dispatch; forged attestation never reaches the RPC. grep self-test — `redeem-invite` in the F-122/F-123 allowlist with the §3.18/F-168 re-pass note; unauthenticated-by-necessity but `mint_writer`-only terminal.
  2. **F-170 (HIGH, P1-1/P1-2) — invite-code interception controls:** pgTAP — expired TOTP → `TOTP_BOOTSTRAP_EXPIRED` no binding; 5 wrong codes → `locked_at`, 6th → `TOTP_BOOTSTRAP_LOCKED` (reuse `enroll_first_passkey:402-419` fixtures); a successful redeem emits `member.added` with the issuing co-chair's pseudonym (attribution). deno — the `/redeem` link carries ONLY `invite_id`, the code is never in the URL.
  3. **F-176 (HIGH, P1-10) — leak sweep CI gate:** vitest — instrument `console.*`/thrown-error/structured-log/audit-meta; run issue+reissue+redeem(challenge+register)+grant (happy + each error branch); assert NONE of {6-digit code, raw TOTP, 32-byte data key, identity privkey} appears anywhere; no-serialization scan; the EF logs closed-literal reasons only; CI grep extension (the Decision 8 canary).
  4. **F-172 (HIGH, P1-4/P1-5) — wrap-to-attacker-pubkey:** hermetic — `wrapMemberInViaProduction` seals to the SERVER-disclosed pubkey (not a caller-supplied one) and the member `seal_open`s back to the SAME 32 bytes; NO `wrap_member_server_side`-shaped fn exists (plaintext data key never in a request payload); fingerprint surfaced before the wrap; a wrong wrap → the member's `seal_open` FAILS (no silent wrong-key success) + re-grant after removing the bad wrap. pgTAP — `wrap_committee_data_key_for_member` `rls_denied` on a non-active target (`:502-503`).
  5. **F-174 (HIGH-adjacent, P1-4) — pubkey-disclosure:** pgTAP — co-chair gets the pubkey+fingerprint; a non-co-chair → `rls_denied`; `identity_keys` direct SELECT stays denied; `identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap` emitted BEFORE return + meta has NO pubkey bytes; single-uid (no bulk); six-mirror (CHECK + schedule + `retention_class_for = membership+7y` + `audit_emit` allowlist).
  6. **F-169 (HIGH, P1-1/P1-2) — invite replay + normalized oracle:** pgTAP — single-use (second redeem → `invite_invalid`, no second binding); concurrent double-redeem (`FOR UPDATE`) → exactly-one-wins; consumed ≡ expired ≡ non-existent yield a BYTE-IDENTICAL `invite_invalid` SQL literal AND a byte-identical EF `{error}` response (assert the three bodies are byte-equal).
  7. **F-171 (MED, P1-1/P1-2) — retargeting closed:** pgTAP — `redeem_invite_complete` has NO caller-controlled uid param; a redeem activates + binds the credential ONLY on `committee_invite.target_user_id`; `committee_activate_membership` RAISEs `invite_invalid` on target≠enrolling (`:275-277`). deno — the EF schema rejects/ignores any `user_id` field.
  8. **F-173 (MED, P1-1/P1-3) — role escalation:** pgTAP — a redeemer of a `{worker_member}` invite cannot self-elevate (activated role = `worker_member`, set from the membership `:290`, no redeem role param); `invalid_role` for an out-of-enum array (`:237-240`); a `worker_co_chair` invite by a co-chair succeeds (accepted facet-i) + emits `member.added`; non-co-chair issue → `rls_denied`.
  9. **F-177 (MED, P1-1) — atomicity:** pgTAP — inject-failure mid-redeem → whole rollback (no half-onboarded state: no credential, no activation, invite unconsumed, bootstrap present); inject-failure mid-issue → no orphan user; invite-expires-mid-redeem → `invite_invalid` rollback; a wrong code rolls back the activation but PERSISTS `wrong_attempts++`/`locked_at` (the one deliberate exception).
  10. **F-175 (MED, P1-2/P1-3/P1-6) — TOTP/redeem DoS:** pgTAP — `reissue_member_totp` replaces the bootstrap (old code dies, `UNIQUE(user_id)` holds, reset attempts/lock); non-co-chair reissue → `rls_denied`; server `now()` authoritative on expiry (`:406`, client-clock-skew-safe). deno — the `challenge` action does no code/lock work; the `register` action has a rate-limit/abuse control before the DB.
  - Group as **"Phase 1 must-fail-first"**: **F-168, F-170, F-169, F-177** are the blocking four for the KEYSTONE PR1 (P1-1 SQL) + PR2 (P1-2 EF) — the unauthenticated surface + interception controls + replay/oracle + atomicity. **F-174, F-172** are the blocking two for the GRANT-KEY path (P1-4 disclosure RPC + P1-5 wrap composition). **F-176** is the cross-cutting CI gate (P1-10), red across both keystone and grant. **F-168/F-170 (P1-1/P1-2) and F-172/F-174 (P1-4/P1-5) MUST be red first at their respective co-sign PRs.**

- **To security-reviewer (required at each PR per HG-ONBOARD-PHASE1 — the unauthenticated user-creation surface + the pubkey-disclosure + the grant-key path):**
  1. **F-168/F-170 (PR P1-1 SQL + P1-2 EF — the keystone, the biggest new surface):** verify `redeem_invite_complete` is `mint_writer`-ONLY (REVOKE PUBLIC/anon/authenticated/service_role, mirroring `bootstrap_first_co_chair:124-127`) and is the ONLY consumer of the invite+TOTP gate; verify the EF reuses origin-pin (`MINT_EXPECTED_ORIGINS`) + key-parity + `verifyWebAuthnRegistration` + self-minted `mint_writer` (NEVER service_role — F-118) and does NOT reuse `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED` or the `EXISTS(users)` guard; verify the 15-min TOTP + 5-attempt lock + single-use invite + normalized error oracle; verify `redeem-invite` is added to the F-122/F-123 grep allowlist with the §3.18 re-pass citation.
  2. **F-172/F-174 (PR P1-4 disclosure RPC + P1-5 wrap composition — the E2EE-compromise edge):** verify `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` is co-chair-gated + audit-before-return + single-uid (no bulk) + meta-has-no-pubkey-bytes + the six-mirror enum (`membership+7y`); verify `wrapMemberInViaProduction` seals to the SERVER-disclosed pubkey (cannot substitute) + the plaintext data key is sealed client-side and NEVER sent to the server (server-side seal STAYS rejected — ADR-0003 Invariant 1/5/6) + the active-member re-assert (`:502-503`) + the fingerprint confirmation; verify the `identity_keys` read-lock (`:122`) is unchanged and the aspirational comment (`:118-121`) is corrected.
  3. **F-176 (P1-10, both surfaces):** verify the leak-sweep CI gate covers the 6-digit code + raw TOTP + the data key + the privkey across issue/reissue/redeem/grant; verify the code is response-body-only (never persisted/logged) and the link carries only `invite_id`.
  4. **F-171/F-173/F-177 (P1-1):** verify the redeemer cannot retarget (no caller uid; `committee_invite.target_user_id` is authoritative) or self-elevate (role from the membership, `:290`); verify the redeem is one atomic txn (no partial state) with the `wrong_attempts`/`locked_at` mutation as the one deliberate persisting exception.
  5. **F-169/F-175:** verify the normalized error oracle (consumed ≡ expired ≡ invalid, byte-identical); verify `reissue_member_totp` replaces (old code dies) + the rate-limit on the unauthenticated register action.

- **To privacy-reviewer (required at P1-1/P1-2 — the unauthenticated user-creation surface; and P1-4 — the pubkey disclosure):**
  1. **F-174 (the pubkey disclosure):** confirm `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` is co-chair-gated, single-member-per-call (no bulk), per-disclosure audited (`identity_pubkey.disclosed_for_wrap`), with NO pubkey bytes in the audit meta — ratify as a governed, minimal, audited disclosure (PIPEDA P5), NOT an ambient collection. Confirm the pubkey is pseudonymous (not direct PI) and the uid↔pubkey re-identification aid is bounded by the co-chair-only gate.
  2. **F-170 (the central interception threat):** confirm the residual is acceptable for a ~12-person committee with out-of-band delivery (the F-170 ruling) and that the s.10.1 trip-wire is a LEAKED code/key (F-176), not the interception itself; confirm a successful interception is bounded to the invited role + detectable + reversible + grants no DATA access without a separate confirmed grant.
  3. **§6:** ratify that Phase 1 introduces NO new PI field (hard rule 6 N/A — `display_name`/`off_employer_contact` are existing optional fields), NO new subprocessor (out-of-band delivery — hard rule 3 N/A), NO new region (ca-central-1 — hard rule 4 N/A), NO new retention class (the one new audit enum on the existing `membership+7y`), and NO new PIPEDA s.10.1 breach trigger AS DESIGNED — the redeem/disclosure/wrap are governed controls whose FAILURE modes (F-176/F-174/F-172) are the s.10.1 triggers, each closed by an implementation-blocking test. Confirm the 6-digit code is a transient secret (never persisted/logged) and the plaintext data key/privkey never serialize (F-176, REUSED §3.16 F-146).

- **To the user (required human-gate decisions):**
  1. **HG-ONBOARD-PHASE1 (PR P1-1 + P1-2 — the keystone, the unauthenticated user-creation surface):** security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign of the repeatable `verify_jwt=false` `redeem-invite` EF + `redeem_invite_complete` SQL (F-168/F-170/F-169/F-171/F-173/F-177) AND **ratification of the F-170 central-threat ruling** — the out-of-band-code interception residual is RULED acceptable for a ~12-person committee, with the 15-min-TOTP + 5-attempt-lock + single-use + short-TTL + removal-path mitigation set MANDATORY. This is the biggest new surface — no autonomous merge.
  2. **HG-ONBOARD-PHASE1 (PR P1-4 + P1-5 — the pubkey-disclosure + grant-key path):** security-reviewer + threat-modeler co-sign of `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` (F-174 — the first crack in the read-locked `identity_keys`) and `wrapMemberInViaProduction` (F-172 — the wrap-to-attacker-pubkey edge; the plaintext data key NEVER touches the server). No autonomous merge.
  3. **Production deploy of any of P1-1/P1-2/P1-4/P1-5/P1-7/P1-8** touches the auth + user-creation + key-material path → never auto-merge (constraints.md Human Gates: "Production deploys of changes touching auth … or personal data"; hard rule 5).
  4. **The F-173 facet-(i) ruling for explicit acknowledgement:** a co-chair CAN invite another `worker_co_chair` (the spec's "2nd co-chair") — this is within the existing co-chair trust model + audit, ACCEPTED. If the committee wants a 4-eyes gate on co-chair-role invites specifically, that is a product decision to flag (out of Phase 1 scope as designed).
  - **No new cross-border transfer, no new subprocessor, no new region, no new credential surface** is introduced by Phase 1 — so NO transfer/credential human gate fires. There is **nothing to approve under the cross-border human gate** for this feature (explicitly: all data remains in ca-central-1; out-of-band delivery means no delivery-channel subprocessor). The co-chair's own out-of-band channel is outside the app's processing boundary.

### Re-pass triggers (Phase 1)

1. Any change making the `redeem-invite` EF terminal reachable by anon/authenticated/service_role (weakening the `mint_writer`-only grant), OR reusing `BOOTSTRAP_ENABLED` / copying the `EXISTS(users)` one-shot guard onto it, OR dropping origin-pin/key-parity/verified-attestation, OR an error oracle that distinguishes consumed/expired/invalid → re-open F-168/F-169 NO-GO + a new F-122/F-123 allowlist re-pass.
2. Any path that lets the 6-digit code, the raw TOTP, the plaintext committee data key, or a member's privkey reach a log/URL/storage/audit-meta surface (the s.10.1 trip-wire) → re-open F-176 NO-GO (a leaked data key/privkey is itself an s.10.1 unauthorized disclosure).
3. `get_member_identity_pubkey_for_wrap` becoming member-readable (not co-chair-only), gaining a bulk/list variant, dropping the per-disclosure audit, OR leaking pubkey bytes into the audit meta; OR any OTHER new read path on `identity_keys` beyond this single RPC → re-open F-174 NO-GO.
4. `wrapMemberInViaProduction` accepting a caller-supplied pubkey that bypasses the disclosure RPC, OR any introduction of a server-side-seal fn that accepts the plaintext data key, OR dropping the active-member re-assert / the fingerprint confirmation → re-open F-172 NO-GO (ADR-0003 Invariant 1/5/6).
5. `redeem_invite_complete` gaining a caller-controlled uid/enrolling/role parameter, OR `committee_activate_membership` setting `users.role` from anything but the membership (`:290`), OR the redeem composition splitting into multiple txns (re-introducing a partial-state window) → re-open F-171/F-173/F-177.
6. Re-send / issuance losing the co-chair gate or the `UNIQUE(user_id)` cap, OR the redeem EF shipping without a rate-limit on the register action, OR the TOTP window/lock being weakened → re-open F-175/F-170.
7. A future onboarding field capturing identifiable health information → PHIPA fires (60-day notice, custodian, lockbox); escalate to privacy-reviewer + re-open §6.
8. Any move to email/SMS/in-app invite DELIVERY (a delivery subprocessor), any move of onboarding data off ca-central-1, or any new collected PI field on the invite → re-open the DFD + §6 + a cross-border/subprocessor human gate.

---
